### 2.1 SID Format (from Definitions)
C  sid_format_prefix_s1  §2 130
   SID string format starts with `S-1-` followed by authority and sub-authorities: `S-1-{authority}-{sub1}-{sub2}-...`
C  sid_binary_compatible_with_windows  §2 135-136
   SID binary representation is byte-for-byte compatible with Windows SIDs -- same bytes, same comparison rules, same well-known values
C  sid_system_is_s1_5_18  §2 131
   Well-known SYSTEM SID is S-1-5-18
C  sid_administrators_is_s1_5_32_544  §2 131
   Well-known Administrators SID is S-1-5-32-544
C  sid_domain_user_format  §2 131-132
   Domain user SIDs follow pattern S-1-5-21-{domain sub-authorities}-{RID}
C  sid_logon_format_s1_5_5_x_y  §2 242
   LogonSession SID format is S-1-5-5-{high}-{low}
C  sid_creator_owner_is_s1_3_0  §9.5 3584
   CREATOR OWNER SID is S-1-3-0
C  sid_creator_group_is_s1_3_1  §9.5 3591
   CREATOR GROUP SID is S-1-3-1
C  sid_owner_rights_is_s1_3_4  §2 151, §9.7 3778
   OWNER RIGHTS SID is S-1-3-4
C  sid_everyone_is_s1_1_0  §9.3 3404
   Everyone SID is S-1-1-0
C  sid_integrity_medium_is_s1_16_8192  §9.3 3389
   Medium integrity SID is S-1-16-8192
C  sid_integrity_high_is_s1_16_12288  §9.3 3389
   High integrity SID is S-1-16-12288
C  sid_integrity_system_is_s1_16_16384  §11 11683
   System integrity SID is S-1-16-16384
C  sid_comparison_is_byte_equality  §2 136
   SID comparison is byte-for-byte equality (same comparison rules as Windows)
C  sid_parse_roundtrip  §2 130-136
   SID string-to-binary-to-string roundtrip produces the original string
C  sid_structurally_wellformed_validation  §7.5 2341
   CreateToken validates all SIDs are structurally well-formed
### 2.2 Token Definition (from Definitions)
C  token_contains_user_sid  §2 108-109
   Token contains a user SID (primary identity)
C  token_contains_group_sids  §2 109
   Token contains group SIDs
C  token_contains_privilege_bitmask  §2 110, §7.3 2086
   Token contains a privilege bitmask (u64)
C  token_contains_integrity_level  §2 110, §7.3 2079
   Token contains an integrity level (Untrusted, Low, Medium, High, System)
C  token_contains_impersonation_level  §2 110, §7.3 2073
   Token contains an impersonation level (Anonymous, Identification, Impersonation, Delegation)
C  token_identity_immutable  §2 112-113
   Token identity (SIDs, type, level) is immutable after creation
C  token_privileges_atomically_adjustable  §2 113
   Token privilege enable/disable state is atomically adjustable at runtime
C  token_groups_atomically_adjustable  §2 113
   Token group enabled state is atomically adjustable at runtime
P  token_never_null  §2 114
   Every thread has a token -- there are no NULL tokens
P  token_is_sole_identity_mechanism  §2 115-116
   Tokens are the sole identity mechanism; UIDs and GIDs play no role in access decisions
### 2.3 Primary vs Impersonation Token (from Definitions)
P  primary_token_inherited_on_fork  §2 119
   Primary token is inherited by child processes on fork
P  primary_token_set_once_at_creation  §2 120-121
   Primary token is set once at process creation (or via SeAssignPrimaryTokenPrivilege)
P  primary_token_in_real_cred  §2 121
   Primary token is stored in task->real_cred
P  impersonation_token_overrides_primary  §2 124
   Impersonation token overrides primary token for access control decisions
P  impersonation_token_per_thread  §2 126-127
   Impersonation token only affects the thread that set it, not other threads in the process
P  impersonation_token_in_cred  §2 125-126
   Impersonation token is stored in task->cred (effective/subjective credential)
### 2.4 Security Descriptor Definition (from Definitions)
C  sd_contains_owner_sid  §2 140
   SD contains an owner SID
C  sd_contains_primary_group_sid  §2 141
   SD contains a primary group SID
C  sd_contains_dacl  §2 141-142
   SD contains a DACL (Discretionary Access Control List)
C  sd_contains_optional_sacl  §2 142-143
   SD optionally contains a SACL (System Access Control List)
C  sd_binary_format_windows_compatible  §2 147-148, §9.1 3136-3138
   SD uses Windows self-relative binary format, byte-for-byte compatible
C  sd_self_relative_format_header  §9.1 3197-3202
   SD self-relative format: 20-byte header (revision, control flags, four 32-bit offsets) followed by owner SID, group SID, SACL, DACL at specified offsets
C  sd_self_relative_no_pointers  §9.1 3200-3201
   Self-relative format packs everything into a contiguous byte buffer -- no pointers, no external references
C  sd_only_self_relative_format  §9.1 3204-3205
   KACS uses the self-relative format exclusively; there is no absolute format
C  sd_owner_implicit_read_control_write_dac  §2 149-150
   By default owner receives implicit READ_CONTROL + WRITE_DAC
C  sd_owner_rights_ace_overrides_implicit  §2 151-152
   OWNER RIGHTS ACE (S-1-3-4) in the DACL overrides owner implicit grants
P  sd_attached_to_files_in_xattr  §2 145, §9.11 3896
   SDs on files stored in xattr (`security.peios.sd`)
C  sd_max_size_64kb  §9.11 3907
   Architectural maximum SD size is 64 KB (ACL header AclSize is u16)
### 2.5 ACL Definition (from Definitions)
C  dacl_empty_denies_all  §2 165-166, §9.8 3824-3827
   Empty DACL (present but zero entries) denies all access (except owner implicit rights)
C  dacl_null_grants_all  §2 166-167, §9.8 3818-3822
   NULL DACL (absent, DP flag clear) grants all access
C  dacl_walked_sequentially  §2 163-164, §11.3 3472-3473
   AccessCheck walks the DACL sequentially from first ACE to last
C  dacl_respects_order_as_given  §2 167-168
   Evaluator respects whatever ACE order is present (does not reorder)
C  dacl_deny_before_allow_canonical  §9.4 3486-3496
   Canonical ordering: explicit deny ACEs before explicit allow ACEs before inherited deny before inherited allow
C  dacl_non_canonical_not_rejected  §9.4 3481-3482
   KACS does not reject non-canonical DACLs -- evaluates whatever order it receives
C  null_dacl_grants_valid_rights_not_0xffffffff  §11.3 4464-4465
   NULL DACL grants all valid rights bounded to GenericMapping(GENERIC_ALL), not raw 0xFFFFFFFF

   DELETE is bit 16

   SYNCHRONIZE is bit 20

   Bits 21-23 are reserved

   ACCESS_SYSTEM_SECURITY is bit 24
C  mask_maximum_allowed_bit_25  §2 194, §9.2 3245
   MAXIMUM_ALLOWED is bit 25

   Bits 26-27 are reserved

   GENERIC_WRITE is bit 30

   GENERIC_READ is bit 31

   MAXIMUM_ALLOWED cannot appear in an ACE -- it is a request flag only
C  mask_generic_mapped_once_at_request_time  §9.2 3264-3268
   Generic bits in requested mask are mapped to object-specific bits once, then cleared; DACL walk operates on specific+standard bits only
C  mask_ace_generic_bits_mapped_at_eval_time  §9.2 3271-3282, §11.3 4452-4458
   (Divergence) Peios maps each ACE's mask via MapGenericBits at eval time using a local variable -- ACE itself never mutated
### 2.8 AccessCheck Definition (from Definitions)
C  accesscheck_three_inputs  §2 178-179
   AccessCheck takes three inputs: token (who), SD (policy), desired access mask (what)
C  accesscheck_returns_granted_or_denial  §2 184-186
   AccessCheck returns the set of access rights actually granted, or denial
P  accesscheck_single_function_for_all_decisions  §2 186-187
   Every access control decision passes through AccessCheck -- file opens, registry reads, IPC, signals, network binds
C  accesscheck_evaluates_privilege_gates_first  §2 180
   AccessCheck evaluates privilege gates (ACCESS_SYSTEM_SECURITY)
C  accesscheck_evaluates_integrity_policy  §2 180
   AccessCheck evaluates integrity policy (MIC and PIP)
C  accesscheck_evaluates_dacl_walk  §2 181
   AccessCheck evaluates DACL walk (owner implicit rights, deny/allow ACEs, conditional expressions)
C  accesscheck_evaluates_post_dacl_privilege_overrides  §2 182
   AccessCheck evaluates post-DACL privilege overrides (SeTakeOwnershipPrivilege)
C  accesscheck_first_writer_wins  §9.4 3474-3476, §11.3 4420-4423
   DACL walk uses first-writer-wins: deny ACE after allow ACE for same bits has no effect (bits already granted)
C  accesscheck_short_circuit_when_all_bits_decided  §11.3 4476-4479
   DACL walk can stop early when all bits in desired mask are decided
C  accesscheck_no_short_circuit_maximum_allowed  §11.3 4479-4481
   Short-circuit does not apply in MAXIMUM_ALLOWED mode; walk runs to completion
### 2.9 Impersonation Level Definition (from Definitions)
C  impersonation_level_anonymous  §2 217-218
   Anonymous level: identity is hidden; server cannot identify the caller
C  impersonation_level_identification  §2 219-220
   Identification level: server can identify caller but cannot act as them
C  impersonation_level_impersonation  §2 221-224
   Impersonation level: server can act as caller for all local operations including local IPC; cannot forward across machine boundaries
C  impersonation_level_delegation  §2 225-227
   Delegation level: server can forward caller's identity to remote services on other machines
C  impersonation_level_order  §2 215-227
   Impersonation levels form a total order: Anonymous < Identification < Impersonation < Delegation
### 2.10 Integrity Level / MIC Definition (from Definitions)
C  integrity_levels_five_values  §2 231, §11 5317, §7.3 2079
   Five integrity levels exist: Untrusted, Low, Medium, High, System
C  integrity_level_strict_total_order  §11 5348
   Integrity levels form a strict total order: System > High > Medium > Low > Untrusted
C  mic_evaluated_before_dacl  §2 233
   MIC is evaluated before the DACL walk
C  mic_blocks_write_if_below_label  §2 233-237, §11 5325-5326
   If token integrity is below object label, write access is denied regardless of DACL
C  mic_optionally_blocks_read  §2 234, §11 5332-5333
   Object label can additionally block reads (no-read-up) for processes below its integrity
C  mic_optionally_blocks_execute  §2 234, §11 5333
   Object label can additionally block execution (no-execute-up) for processes below its integrity
C  mic_default_is_no_write_up_only  §11 5325, 5335-5336
   Default MIC behavior is no-write-up only (most common case)
C  mic_default_label_is_medium  §11 5361-5365
   Unlabeled objects default to Medium integrity with no-write-up
C  mic_does_not_constrain_privileges  §11 5369-5378
   MIC does not revoke rights granted by privileges -- it constrains what the DACL can grant
C  mic_label_in_sacl  §2 232, §9.3 3387-3390
   Object integrity label is stored as a SYSTEM_MANDATORY_LABEL_ACE in the SACL
C  mic_label_sid_encodes_level  §9.3 3389
   Label SID encodes the integrity level (e.g., S-1-16-8192 = Medium)
C  mic_label_mask_encodes_policy  §9.3 3390-3391
   Label ACE access mask encodes which operations (write, read, execute) are blocked
### 2.11 Ownership Definition (from Definitions)
C  ownership_implicit_read_control  §2 283-284, §9.7 3769
   Owner receives implicit READ_CONTROL regardless of DACL
C  ownership_implicit_write_dac  §2 283-284, §9.7 3770
   Owner receives implicit WRITE_DAC regardless of DACL
C  ownership_implicit_before_dacl_walk  §11.4 4503-4508
   Owner implicit rights granted before DACL walk -- deny ACEs cannot override them
C  ownership_owner_rights_suppress_implicit  §2 285-286, §11.4 4511-4514
   Presence of any OWNER RIGHTS ACE (S-1-3-4) in DACL suppresses the implicit READ_CONTROL + WRITE_DAC grant entirely
C  ownership_owner_rights_prescan  §11.4 4523-4524
   OWNER RIGHTS check is a pre-scan of DACL before implicit grant, before walk
C  ownership_owner_rights_prescan_checks_presence_not_condition  §11.4 4530-4532
   Pre-scan checks for ACE presence only, not whether conditional expression evaluates to TRUE
C  ownership_owner_rights_restrict_pattern  §9.7 3794-3796
   Allow ACE for S-1-3-4 with only READ_CONTROL restricts owner to read-only on the SD
C  ownership_owner_rights_expand_pattern  §9.7 3791-3793
   Allow ACE for S-1-3-4 with READ_CONTROL + WRITE_DAC + DELETE expands owner rights
C  ownership_owner_rights_suppress_pattern  §9.7 3788-3790
   Deny ACE for S-1-3-4 with READ_CONTROL + WRITE_DAC suppresses owner rights entirely
C  ownership_transfer_requires_write_owner  §9.7 3806
   Changing object owner requires WRITE_OWNER
C  ownership_take_ownership_privilege_grants_write_owner  §9.7 3810-3811
   SeTakeOwnershipPrivilege grants WRITE_OWNER on any object regardless of DACL
### 2.12 ACL Revision (from §9.9)
C  acl_revision_0x02_basic_types  §9.9 3846-3849
   ACL_REVISION (0x02) permits basic ACE types (0x00, 0x01, 0x02, 0x03), mandatory label (0x11), resource attribute (0x12), scoped policy ID (0x13), process trust label (0x14)
C  acl_revision_0x04_ds_types  §9.9 3850-3852
   ACL_REVISION_DS (0x04) additionally permits object-type ACEs (0x05-0x08), callback ACEs (0x09-0x0D, 0x0F), and alarm callback/object variants (0x0E, 0x10)
C  acl_revision_both_accepted  §9.9 3855
   KACS accepts both ACL_REVISION and ACL_REVISION_DS
C  acl_revision_set_to_minimum  §9.9 3855-3858
   When creating new ACLs, revision is set to minimum required: ACL_REVISION if only basic ACEs, ACL_REVISION_DS if object-type or callback ACEs included

### 2.14 GenericMapping (from §2 and §9.2)
C  generic_mapping_provided_by_caller  §2 277-278, §9.2 3284-3294
   GenericMapping is provided by the caller at AccessCheck time, not by KACS
C  generic_mapping_generic_read_file_example  §2 273-274
   GENERIC_READ on file maps to FILE_READ_DATA + FILE_READ_ATTRIBUTES + READ_CONTROL
C  generic_bits_cleared_after_mapping  §9.2 3267
   After mapping generic bits to specific bits, generic bits are cleared from the request mask
### 2.15 SID Matching in DACL Walk
C  sid_match_user_sid  §11.3 4425-4426
   ACE SID matches if it equals the token's user SID
C  sid_match_group_sid  §11.3 4426
   ACE SID matches if it equals a group SID on the token
C  sid_match_allow_requires_enabled  §11.3 4427-4428
   For allow ACEs, only groups that are SE_GROUP_ENABLED and not deny-only match
C  sid_match_deny_includes_deny_only  §11.3 4428-4430
   For deny ACEs, both enabled groups and SE_GROUP_USE_FOR_DENY_ONLY groups match
C  sid_match_deny_only_overrides_enabled  §11.3 4430-4432
   Deny-only flag overrides enabled check: deny-only group always participates in deny matching regardless of enabled state
C  sid_match_neither_flag_no_match  §11.3 4432-4433
   A group with neither ENABLED nor USE_FOR_DENY_ONLY set does not participate in any matching
C  sid_match_user_deny_only  §11.3 4438-4441
   When token user SID is deny-only, it matches deny ACEs but not allow ACEs
C  sid_match_mandatory_group_cannot_be_disabled  §7.3 2064, 2435
   Mandatory groups (SE_GROUP_MANDATORY) cannot be disabled
C  sid_match_deny_only_cannot_be_reverted  §7.3 2065-2066
   Deny-only groups (SE_GROUP_USE_FOR_DENY_ONLY) are permanently set via FilterToken, cannot be reverted
### 2.16 Token Privilege Bitmask Fields (from §7.3)
C  privilege_present_u64  §7.3 2086
   privileges_present is a u64 bitmask -- bits can be cleared (permanent removal) but never set
C  privilege_enabled_u64  §7.3 2087
   privileges_enabled is a u64 bitmask -- toggleable for non-removed privileges
C  privilege_enabled_by_default_u64  §7.3 2088
   privileges_enabled_by_default is a u64 -- the reset position for AdjustTokenPrivileges
C  privilege_used_u64  §7.3 2089
   privileges_used is a u64 bitmask -- set when a privilege is exercised, audit trail
C  privilege_removal_clears_all_three_masks  §7.3 2093-2094
   Removing a privilege clears the bit in present, enabled, and enabled_by_default
C  privilege_lifecycle  §7.3 2091-2094
   Privilege lifecycle: present+disabled -> enabled -> used -> optionally disabled -> optionally permanently removed
C  privilege_present_bits_never_set_after_creation  §7.3 2086
   Bits in privileges_present can only be cleared, never set after token creation
---

### 10.1 Privileges Not Capabilities
P  privilege_check_is_identity_aware  §10.1 3978-3981
   Privilege check is always "does this principal hold this privilege?" -- answer differs per principal (unlike capabilities)
P  capabilities_neutralized_via_switchboard  §10.1 4001-4005
   Linux capabilities neutralized: every process gets full capability set so Linux checks pass; LSM hooks enforce KACS privileges instead
C  privilege_has_enable_disable_lifecycle  §10.1 3988-3991
   Privileges have explicit enabled/disabled state, unlike capabilities which are binary (have or not)
C  privilege_usage_tracked  §10.1 3995-3999
   privileges_used field records which privileges have been exercised; privilege use generates audit events
### 10.2 Privilege Model
C  privilege_assigned_at_token_creation  §10.2 4011-4016
   Privileges resolved at token creation time -- no runtime privilege grants
C  privilege_no_add_after_creation  §10.2 4015-4016
   If a privilege is not on the token at birth, it cannot be added later
C  privilege_most_start_disabled  §10.2 4018-4020
   Most privileges start disabled (present but not active)
C  privilege_must_enable_before_use  §10.2 4023-4025
   Before using a privilege, holder enables it via AdjustPrivileges
C  privilege_check_requires_present_and_enabled  §10.2 4054
   Kernel checks whether token holds the privilege (present AND enabled) before permitting operation
C  privilege_can_be_disabled_after_use  §10.2 4033
   After exercise, privilege can be disabled (returns to resting state)
C  privilege_can_be_permanently_removed  §10.2 4033-4034
   Privilege can be permanently removed from token (irreversible -- cannot be re-added)
C  privilege_check_is_bitmask_test  §10.2 4055-4056
   Privilege check is a simple bitmask test against token's privileges_enabled field
### 10.3 Two Categories
C  privilege_standalone_independent_of_accesscheck  §10.3 4050-4052
   Standalone operation gate privileges are independent of AccessCheck
P  privilege_standalone_via_capability_switchboard  §10.3 4057-4059
   Most standalone privileges enforced via capability switchboard: Linux capability check -> security_capable() hook -> KACS privilege check
C  privilege_accesscheck_influencing_count  §10.3 4072
   Exactly five privileges influence AccessCheck
### 10.3 Five AccessCheck-Influencing Privileges
C  se_security_privilege_grants_sacl_access  §10.3 4074-4080
   SeSecurityPrivilege grants ability to read and write an object's SACL
C  se_security_privilege_required_for_sacl  §10.3 4077-4078
   Without SeSecurityPrivilege, SACL is inaccessible regardless of DACL
C  se_take_ownership_grants_ownership_any_object  §10.3 4082-4086
   SeTakeOwnershipPrivilege lets administrator take ownership of any object even without current permissions
C  se_backup_grants_read_any_object  §10.3 4088-4091
   SeBackupPrivilege grants read access to any object regardless of DACL
C  se_restore_grants_write_and_permissions  §10.3 4093-4096
   SeRestorePrivilege grants write access plus ability to modify permissions, change ownership, and access audit policy
C  se_relabel_punches_write_owner_through_mic  §10.3 4099-4101
   SeRelabelPrivilege punches WRITE_OWNER through MIC for non-dominant callers
C  se_relabel_removes_only_lower_restriction  §10.3 4103-4104
   SeRelabelPrivilege removes the "only lower" restriction at label-write time -- any level permitted
C  se_relabel_label_gated_by_write_owner_not_ass  §10.3 4101-4102
   Label modification is gated by WRITE_OWNER, not ACCESS_SYSTEM_SECURITY, despite label residing in SACL
### 10.4 Intent-Gated Privileges
C  se_backup_intent_gated  §10.4 4114-4118, §10.8 4241
   SeBackupPrivilege is only evaluated when caller passes BACKUP_INTENT flag
C  se_restore_intent_gated  §10.4 4114-4118, §10.8 4242
   SeRestorePrivilege is only evaluated when caller passes RESTORE_INTENT flag
### 10.5 Privilege Assignment
C  privilege_not_from_group_membership  §10.5 4122-4124
   Being a member of Administrators group does not automatically confer any privilege
C  privilege_orthogonal_to_groups  §10.5 4126-4128
   Privileges and group memberships are orthogonal: groups determine object access (DACL), privileges determine system operations
C  privilege_set_fixed_at_birth  §10.5 4147-4150
   Token's set of possible privileges is fixed at birth -- none can be added after creation
C  privilege_no_runtime_escalation  §10.5 4152-4154
   Process cannot acquire new privileges by joining a group, calling a syscall, or exploiting a race
C  privilege_new_token_only_via_auth_or_create  §10.5 4155-4157
   Only path to different privileges is new authentication event or SeCreateTokenPrivilege
P  kernel_trusts_authd_does_not_evaluate_policy  §10.5 4143-4145
   Kernel does not verify or evaluate privilege policy -- trusts authd as TCB component
### 10.6 Custom Peios Privileges
C  custom_privileges_from_bit_63_downward  §10.6 4165-4166
   Custom Peios privileges allocated from bit 63 downward in 64-bit bitmask
C  windows_privileges_from_bit_2_upward  §10.6 4166-4167
   Windows-compatible privileges occupy standard bit positions starting from bit 2
C  custom_grow_down_windows_grow_up  §10.6 4169-4170
   Custom allocations grow downward from top, Windows grow upward from bottom -- avoids collision
C  v1_only_custom_privilege_is_bind_port  §10.6 4172-4173
   Only custom privilege defined for v1 is SeBindPrivilegedPortPrivilege
P  se_bind_privileged_port_gates_below_1024  §10.6 4173-4174, §10.8 4268
   SeBindPrivilegedPortPrivilege gates binding to TCP/UDP ports below 1024
### 10.7 Privilege Auditing
C  privilege_used_is_monotonic  §10.7 4188-4189
   privileges_used bitmask is a monotonic accumulator -- bits set but never cleared
C  accesscheck_privilege_audit_only_when_necessary  §10.7 4191-4196
   For AccessCheck-influencing privileges, audit emitted only when privilege was actually necessary (access would have been denied without it)
P  standalone_privilege_audit_on_exercise  §10.7 4200-4201
   For standalone privileges, capability switchboard records privilege exercise when security_capable() grants based on KACS privilege check
P  audit_event_identifies_privilege_operation_token  §10.7 4202-4203
   Audit event identifies the privilege, the operation, and the calling thread's token
### 10.8 Privilege Catalog -- Identity and Token Management
P  se_create_token_is_kernel_standalone  §10.8 4231
   SeCreateTokenPrivilege is kernel standalone enforcement; creates tokens from scratch
P  se_create_token_only_tcb  §10.8 4231
   SeCreateTokenPrivilege is limited to TCB components (authd, peinit)
P  se_assign_primary_token_is_kernel_standalone  §10.8 4232
   SeAssignPrimaryTokenPrivilege is kernel standalone; installs token as another process's primary identity
P  se_impersonate_is_kernel_standalone  §10.8 4233
   SeImpersonatePrivilege is kernel standalone; required to impersonate another principal
### 10.8 Privilege Catalog -- Access Control
C  se_security_is_accesscheck_enforcement  §10.8 4239
   SeSecurityPrivilege is AccessCheck enforcement category
C  se_take_ownership_is_accesscheck_enforcement  §10.8 4240
   SeTakeOwnershipPrivilege is AccessCheck enforcement category
C  se_backup_is_accesscheck_enforcement  §10.8 4241
   SeBackupPrivilege is AccessCheck enforcement category
C  se_restore_is_accesscheck_enforcement  §10.8 4242
   SeRestorePrivilege is AccessCheck enforcement category
C  se_relabel_is_accesscheck_plus_enforcement  §10.8 4243
   SeRelabelPrivilege is AccessCheck + enforcement layer category
P  se_change_notify_is_kernel_standalone  §10.8 4244
   SeChangeNotifyPrivilege is kernel standalone; bypasses traverse checking
C  se_change_notify_default_granted  §10.8 4244
   SeChangeNotifyPrivilege granted to all principals by default
P  se_create_symbolic_link_is_kernel_standalone  §10.8 4245
   SeCreateSymbolicLinkPrivilege is kernel standalone; gates symlink creation
C  se_create_symbolic_link_default_granted  §10.8 4245
   SeCreateSymbolicLinkPrivilege granted to all principals by default
### 10.8 Privilege Catalog -- System Operations
P  se_tcb_is_kernel_standalone  §10.8 4251
   SeTcbPrivilege is kernel standalone; catch-all for CAP_SYS_ADMIN-gated operations
P  se_shutdown_is_kernel_standalone  §10.8 4252
   SeShutdownPrivilege is kernel standalone; gates shutdown/reboot
P  se_remote_shutdown_requires_both  §10.8 4253
   Remote shutdown requires both SeShutdownPrivilege AND SeRemoteShutdownPrivilege when logon type is Network
P  se_remote_shutdown_checks_logon_type  §10.8 4253
   SeRemoteShutdownPrivilege enforcement resolves token auth_id to LogonSession and checks logon_type
P  se_load_driver_is_kernel_standalone  §10.8 4254
   SeLoadDriverPrivilege is kernel standalone; gates kernel module load/unload
P  se_load_driver_must_be_stripped  §10.8 4254
   SeLoadDriverPrivilege must be stripped from all non-peinit tokens via FilterToken
P  se_debug_is_kernel_standalone  §10.8 4255
   SeDebugPrivilege is kernel standalone; grants ptrace/memory access to any process regardless of SD
P  se_debug_does_not_bypass_pip  §10.8 4255
   SeDebugPrivilege does not bypass PIP protections -- PIP-protected processes require both privilege and sufficient PIP trust level
P  se_systemtime_is_kernel_standalone  §10.8 4256
   SeSystemtimePrivilege is kernel standalone; gates system clock changes
P  se_increase_base_priority_is_kernel_standalone  §10.8 4257
   SeIncreaseBasePriorityPrivilege is kernel standalone; gates scheduling priority and CPU affinity changes
P  se_increase_quota_is_kernel_standalone  §10.8 4258
   SeIncreaseQuotaPrivilege is kernel standalone; gates resource limit overrides
P  se_lock_memory_is_kernel_standalone  §10.8 4259
   SeLockMemoryPrivilege is kernel standalone; gates mlock/mlockall
P  se_audit_is_kernel_standalone  §10.8 4260
   SeAuditPrivilege is kernel standalone; allows userspace services to generate audit records
P  se_profile_single_process_is_kernel_standalone  §10.8 4261
   SeProfileSingleProcessPrivilege is kernel standalone; gates perf_event_open
P  se_create_job_is_kernel_standalone  §10.8 4262
   SeCreateJobPrivilege is kernel standalone; custom Peios privilege; gates JFS syscall
### 10.8 Privilege Catalog -- Network
P  se_bind_privileged_port_is_kernel_standalone  §10.8 4268
   SeBindPrivilegedPortPrivilege is kernel standalone; custom Peios privilege

C  se_sync_agent_is_application_level  §10.8 4274

   SeUndockPrivilege is reserved -- server OS, no use case
C  reserved_privileges_have_no_enforcement  §10.8 4280-4284

C  privilege_all_fit_in_u64  §10.6 4165-4170

### 10.2/10.5 Privilege Lifecycle Enforcement
P  adjust_privileges_enable_present  §10.2 4023-4025
   AdjustPrivileges can enable a privilege that is present but disabled

   AdjustPrivileges can disable an enabled privilege
P  adjust_privileges_remove_permanent  §10.2 4033-4034
   AdjustPrivileges can permanently remove a privilege -- irreversible
P  adjust_privileges_cannot_add_missing  §10.2 4015-4016
   AdjustPrivileges cannot add a privilege not present on the token
P  adjust_privileges_cannot_reenable_removed  §10.2 4033-4034
   AdjustPrivileges cannot re-enable a permanently removed privilege

   AdjustTokenPrivileges can restore all privileges to privileges_enabled_by_default state
C  privilege_present_disabled_not_exercised  §10.2 4054
   A privilege that is present but disabled is not exercised by privilege check

   Exercising a privilege sets the corresponding bit in privileges_used

   SYSTEM token groups include BUILTIN\Administrators (S-1-5-32-544)

### Token Lifecycle across fork/exec (from §7.4, referenced by §2 definitions)
P  fork_copies_primary_token  §7.4 2238-2240
   Fork (clone without CLONE_THREAD) gives child independent deep copy of parent's primary token
P  fork_does_not_inherit_impersonation  §7.4 2241-2242
   Fork does not inherit parent's impersonation token -- child gets identity from real_cred
P  fork_token_mutations_independent  §7.4 2242-2243
   After fork, mutations to either token are invisible to the other
P  clone_thread_shares_primary_token  §7.4 2247-2249
   Clone with CLONE_THREAD: threads share parent's real_cred (refcounted), same primary token object
P  thread_privilege_adjustments_visible_to_all  §7.4 2249-2250
   Privilege adjustments on primary token visible to all threads in process
P  threads_independent_impersonation  §7.4 2250-2252
   Each thread maintains independent impersonation state -- new thread does not inherit impersonation
P  exec_preserves_primary_token  §7.4 2255-2256
   Primary token survives execve unchanged (unless NEW_PROCESS_MIN applies)
P  exec_reverts_impersonation  §7.4 2257-2258
   If thread is impersonating, impersonation is reverted before new program runs

# Section 5: Linux Application Compatibility + Section 6: Feature Overview
## KACS Test Corpus: Sections 5 and 6
---

### Section 5.1 — Credential Projection
P  cred_proj_uid_from_ad_uidnumber  §5.1 L1001-1002
   When a token is installed on a process, `getuid()` returns the UID mapped from the token's user SID via the AD `uidNumber` attribute.
P  cred_proj_uid_fallback_anonymous  §5.1 L1002-1003
   If the token's user SID has no `uidNumber` attribute, the process's UID defaults to 65534 (Anonymous SID / `nobody`).
P  cred_proj_gid_from_ad_gidnumber  §5.1 L1004-1005
   The token's primary group SID maps to a GID via the AD `gidNumber` attribute.
P  cred_proj_gid_fallback_anonymous  §5.1 L1005
   If the token's primary group SID has no `gidNumber`, the GID defaults to 65534.
P  cred_proj_supplementary_groups  §5.1 L1006-1007
   The token's group SIDs map to supplementary GIDs where `gidNumber` attributes exist; `getgroups()` returns these.
P  cred_proj_getuid_returns_projected  §5.1 L1008
   `getuid()` returns the projected UID matching the token's user SID.
P  cred_proj_getgid_returns_projected  §5.1 L1008
   `getgid()` returns the projected GID matching the token's primary group SID.
P  cred_proj_getgroups_returns_projected  §5.1 L1008
   `getgroups()` returns projected supplementary GIDs matching the token's group SIDs.
P  cred_proj_proc_status_reflects_uid  §5.1 L1009
   `/proc/<pid>/status` reflects the projected UID and GID values.
P  cred_proj_stat_reflects_projected  §5.1 L1009-1010
   `stat()` on process-owned resources reflects the projected UID/GID.
P  cred_proj_no_uid0_without_system_token  §5.1 L1014-1015
   No process runs as UID 0 unless it holds the SYSTEM token (S-1-5-18).
P  cred_proj_root_refusing_software_works  §5.1 L1018-1019
   Software that refuses to run as root (checks `getuid() == 0`) works without modification for non-SYSTEM tokens.
P  cred_proj_system_token_gets_uid0  §5.1 L1015
   A process with the SYSTEM token (S-1-5-18) has UID 0.
P  cred_proj_different_services_different_uids  §5.1 L1023-1025
   Different services with different token user SIDs get different projected UIDs.
P  cred_proj_on_fork  §5.1 L997-998
   When a process forks, the child inherits the projected credentials matching the parent's token.
P  cred_proj_on_exec  §5.1 L997-998
   When a process execs, projected credentials are set to match the installed token.
P  cred_proj_impersonation_not_projected  §5 L969-975
   Projected Linux credentials reflect the process's primary token, not any impersonation token. `getuid()` and KACS identity may disagree during impersonation.
P  cred_proj_proc_status_shows_primary_not_impersonation  §5.6 L1482-1484
   `/proc/<pid>/status` always shows the primary token's projected UID, even if individual threads are impersonating different identities.
P  cred_proj_groups_without_gidnumber_omitted  §5.1 L1006-1007
   Group SIDs that lack a `gidNumber` attribute are not included in the supplementary GID list.
---

### Section 5.2 — DAC Neutralization / Capability Switchboard
P  dac_neutral_all_processes_full_capset  §5.2 L1048-1050
   All processes receive a full capability set in their Linux credentials.
P  dac_neutral_dac_never_blocks_kacs  §5.2 L1047-1051
   DAC checks pass (because full capabilities) so the LSM hook is always reached for KACS evaluation.
P  dac_neutral_cross_uid_signal_reaches_lsm  §5.2 L1042-1045
   A process with UID 1000 can attempt `kill()` on UID 2000; DAC does not block it, KACS LSM hook evaluates.
P  dac_neutral_cross_uid_file_access_reaches_lsm  §5.2 L1044-1045
   File access by a process whose UID does not match the file owner reaches KACS `inode_permission` hook instead of failing at DAC.
#### 5.2.1 — Capability Classification: ALLOW

   CAP_WAKE_ALARM (35) requires `SeTcbPrivilege`.
P  cap_priv_block_suspend_requires_setcb  §5.2.1 L1122

   CAP_PERFMON (38) requires `SeProfileSingleProcessPrivilege`.
P  cap_priv_bpf_requires_setcb  §5.2.1 L1125
   CAP_BPF (39) requires `SeTcbPrivilege`.
P  cap_priv_checkpoint_restore_requires_setcb  §5.2.1 L1126
   CAP_CHECKPOINT_RESTORE (40) requires `SeTcbPrivilege`.
P  cap_priv_unmapped_cap_denied  §5.2 L1072-1073
   An unmapped or unknown capability is denied by default (fail-closed).
#### 5.2.1 — Capability Classification: DENY
P  cap_deny_setpcap  §5.2.1 L1132
   CAP_SETPCAP (8) is unconditionally denied.

   CAP_SETFCAP (31) is unconditionally denied.
P  cap_deny_mac_override  §5.2.1 L1134
   CAP_MAC_OVERRIDE (32) is unconditionally denied; KACS LSM must not be bypassable.
#### 5.2.2 — Capability Inspection Compat Gap
P  cap_inspect_capget_shows_full_set  §5.2.2 L1174-1176
   `capget()` returns a full capability set even when KACS privilege restrictions apply.
P  cap_inspect_proc_status_shows_full_set  §5.2.2 L1174-1176
   `/proc/self/status` shows a full capability set regardless of KACS privilege restrictions.
P  cap_inspect_branch_then_denied  §5.2.2 L1177-1181
   An application that branches on capability presence takes the "capable" path, but the underlying operation is denied by the KACS switchboard if the privilege is absent.

### Section 5.3 — The setuid() Syscall
P  setuid_no_security_properties  §5.3 L1189-1206
   UIDs have zero security properties under KACS. A process with UID 0 and a process with UID 65534 holding the same KACS token have identical authority.
P  setuid_noop_without_privilege  §5.3 L1221-1227
   `setuid()` without `SeAssignPrimaryTokenPrivilege` returns 0 (success) but neither the Linux credential nor the KACS token changes.
P  setuid_noop_uid_unchanged  §5.3 L1221-1227
   After a no-op `setuid(nobody)`, `getuid()` still returns the original UID.
P  setuid_noop_token_unchanged  §5.3 L1221-1227
   After a no-op `setuid()`, the KACS token is unchanged (same authority as before).
P  setuid_noop_returns_success  §5.3 L1223
   The no-op `setuid()` returns 0, not an error code.
P  setgid_noop_without_privilege  §5.3 L1216-1217
   `setgid()` without `SeAssignPrimaryTokenPrivilege` is a silent no-op returning 0.
P  setresuid_noop_without_privilege  §5.3 L1216-1217
   `setresuid()` without `SeAssignPrimaryTokenPrivilege` is a silent no-op returning 0.
P  setresgid_noop_without_privilege  §5.3 L1216-1217
   `setresgid()` without `SeAssignPrimaryTokenPrivilege` is a silent no-op returning 0.
P  setgroups_noop_without_privilege  §5.3 L1216-1217
   `setgroups()` without `SeAssignPrimaryTokenPrivilege` is a silent no-op returning 0.
P  setuid_with_privilege_swaps_token  §5.3 L1230-1238
   `setuid()` with `SeAssignPrimaryTokenPrivilege` triggers a genuine identity transition: both the KACS token and Linux credential change.
P  setuid_with_privilege_seccomp_intercept  §5.3 L1232-1238
   The privileged `setuid()` path uses seccomp user notification (`SECCOMP_RET_USER_NOTIF`) to redirect to userspace for authd token swap.
P  setuid_seccomp_only_on_privileged  §5.3 L1241-1244
   The seccomp filter is only installed on processes holding `SeAssignPrimaryTokenPrivilege`. Unprivileged processes never enter the seccomp path.
P  setuid_lsm_hook_handles_unprivileged  §5.3 L1224-1227
   Unprivileged `setuid()` calls are handled entirely by the `task_fix_setuid` LSM hook (in-kernel, no userspace round-trip).
P  setuid_noop_preserves_uid_token_consistency  §5.3 L1279-1284
   The no-op preserves consistency: `getuid()` and KACS identity remain in sync (no split).
P  setfsuid_noop_without_privilege  §5.6 L1400-1407
   `setfsuid()` follows the same no-op/swap model as `setuid()`.
P  setfsgid_noop_without_privilege  §5.6 L1400-1407
   `setfsgid()` follows the same no-op/swap model as `setgid()`.
---

### Section 5.4 — The Setuid Bit on Exec
P  setuid_bit_with_privilege_changes_euid_and_token  §5.4 L1313-1316
   Executing a setuid binary with `SeAssignPrimaryTokenPrivilege` changes euid/suid to the file owner's UID AND swaps the KACS token to the corresponding identity.
P  setuid_bit_without_privilege_changes_euid_only  §5.4 L1318-1321
   Executing a setuid binary without `SeAssignPrimaryTokenPrivilege` changes euid/suid to the file owner's UID but the KACS token is unchanged.
P  setuid_bit_euid_suid_change  §5.4 L1307-1309
   The setuid bit on exec changes the effective UID (euid) and saved set-user-ID (suid) to the file owner's UID.
P  setuid_bit_ruid_unchanged  §5.4 L1309-1310
   The real UID (ruid) is unchanged after executing a setuid binary.
P  setuid_bit_fsuid_follows_euid  §5.4 L1310
   The fsuid follows the euid after executing a setuid binary.
P  setuid_bit_cosmetic_escalation_kacs_enforces_original  §5.4 L1349-1354
   In cosmetic escalation (no privilege): the process sees `geteuid() == 0` but KACS continues to enforce the original token's authority.
P  setuid_bit_genuine_escalation_sudo  §5.4 L1315-1316
   With privilege: `sudo` running with `geteuid() == 0` AND a SYSTEM token is real `sudo`.
P  setuid_bit_at_secure_triggered  §5.6 L1439-1449
   Executing a setuid binary triggers Linux's secure-exec mode (`AT_SECURE`), stripping `LD_PRELOAD`, `LD_LIBRARY_PATH`, clearing `PR_SET_PDEATHSIG`, resetting dumpability — even in cosmetic escalation.
---

### Section 5.5 — Root-Assuming and Root-Refusing Software
P  root_refusing_software_no_uid0  §5.5 L1361-1363
   Root-refusing software (checks `getuid() == 0` and aborts) works without modification because no regular process has UID 0 under credential projection.
P  root_assuming_no_dangerous_paths  §5.5 L1366-1369
   Root-assuming software's dangerous codepaths (checks `getuid() == 0` to enable) do not activate in normal operation because no regular process has UID 0.
P  uid0_tool_cosmetic_uid0  §5.5 L1374-1377
   A `uid0` setuid-root wrapper provides cosmetic UID 0 without token swap (per §5.4 without privilege).
---

### Section 5.6 — Known Compat Gaps (still testable assertions)
P  capset_behavior_unexpected  §5.6 L1384-1391
   `capset()` / `capget()` calls may behave unexpectedly; the switchboard allows a full set, but modifying capabilities has no KACS effect.
P  access_and_open_agree  §5.6 L1409-1418
   `access()` and `open()` both use the same KACS token for evaluation, so they agree. The Linux real-UID vs effective-UID distinction is lost.
P  so_peercred_returns_projected_uid  §5.6 L1421-1423
   `SO_PEERCRED` on a Unix socket returns the projected UID/GID/PID, not KACS token information.
P  scm_credentials_returns_projected  §5.6 L1423-1424
   `SCM_CREDENTIALS` sends projected UIDs, not KACS token information.
P  scm_credentials_forgery_cosmetic  §5.6 L1426-1430
   `CAP_SETUID` being ALLOWED permits forging the UID field in `SCM_CREDENTIALS` — this is a cosmetic forgery under KACS.
P  so_reuseport_uses_projected_uid  §5.6 L1432-1437
   `SO_REUSEPORT` enforces same-UID requirement based on projected UIDs. Services with different KACS tokens (different UIDs) cannot share a port via `SO_REUSEPORT`.
P  linux_auditd_uses_projected_uids  §5.6 L1452-1458
   Linux `auditd` records use projected UID/GID values, which remain meaningful (each service has a distinct UID).
P  per_thread_cred_divergence_primary_visible  §5.6 L1476-1488
   Linux credentials show the primary token's UID; impersonation tokens are NOT projected. Multi-threaded apps see consistent process-wide UID from primary token.
---

### Section 5 — Overriding Constraints (cross-cutting)
P  compat_never_bypasses_accesscheck  §5 L949-952
   No compatibility shim, silent no-op, or credential projection may bypass AccessCheck or create a path where a UID grants authority the token does not.
P  uid_grants_no_authority  §5.3 L1189-1206
   A UID alone never grants any authority. Two processes with different UIDs but the same KACS token have identical access.
P  uid_not_in_any_sd  §5.3 L1192-1194
   The UID does not appear in any Security Descriptor. No ACE references a UID.

### Section 6.1 — Identity
P  every_thread_has_token  §6.1 L1499-1503

### Section 6.2 — Access Control
P  sd_on_every_protected_object  §6.2 L1532-1534
   Every protected object (file, registry key, IPC endpoint, service) has a Security Descriptor.
C  sd_windows_binary_format  §6.2 L1535-1536
   SDs use the Windows binary format and are fully compatible with Samba and Windows file servers.
C  dacl_ordered_evaluation  §6.2 L1538-1541
   DACL is an ordered list of rules evaluated in order.
C  dacl_allow_and_deny_rules  §6.2 L1541
   Both allow and deny rules are supported in a DACL.
C  object_type_ace_targets_subobject  §6.2 L1543-1546
   Access rules can target specific properties or sub-objects via object-type ACEs with property GUIDs.
C  conditional_ace_evaluates_token_attrs  §6.2 L1548-1551
   Conditional ACEs evaluate expressions against token attributes (e.g., `department=engineering AND clearance >= 3`).
C  central_access_policy_both_must_allow  §6.2 L1555-1557
   AccessCheck evaluates both the file's normal DACL and the referenced central policy; access granted only if both allow.
C  central_policy_via_scoped_policy_id_ace  §6.2 L1562

   No Propagate flag limits inheritance to one level only.
C  sd_inheritance_inherit_only  §6.2 L1568
   Inherit Only flag means the ACE does not apply to the container itself, only its children.
P  default_security_on_create  §6.2 L1570-1573
   When a new object is created, it automatically gets an SD: creator as owner, inheritable rules from parent, default DACL from creator's token.
P  no_object_without_sd  §6.2 L1573

C  owner_implicit_read_control_write_dac  §6.2 L1575-1577

C  accesscheck_all_subsystems_same_evaluator  §6.2 L1584-1586

### Section 6.4 — Privileges

C  privilege_granted_by_policy_not_identity  §6.4 L1606-1608

### Section 6.5 — Impersonation
P  impersonation_per_thread  §6.5 L1629-1633
   Impersonation is per-thread; a server thread takes on the user's identity while other threads are unaffected.
C  impersonation_level_anonymous  §6.5 L1637
   Anonymous level: the server cannot identify the caller.
C  impersonation_level_identification  §6.5 L1638-1639
   Identification level: the server can identify the caller but cannot act as them.
C  impersonation_level_impersonation  §6.5 L1640-1641
   Impersonation level: the server can act as the caller for local operations.
C  impersonation_level_delegation  §6.5 L1642-1643
   Delegation level: the server can forward the caller's identity to other services.
P  revert_to_self  §6.5 L1645-1647
   A server thread can drop the impersonated identity and return to its own service identity.

### Section 6.6 — Delegation

### Section 6.7 — Elevation

   The filtered token is the default for day-to-day work.

### Section 6.8 — Token Restriction

   Access is granted only if both the normal SIDs and the restricted SIDs pass the access check independently.
C  write_restricted_token_reads_normal  §6.8 L1682-1684
   A write-restricted variant subjects only write access to the restricted SID check; reads use the normal SID list.

### Section 6.9 — Application Confinement
C  confinement_default_deny  §6.9 L1693-1696
   A confined token is default-deny: the process can only access objects that explicitly grant access to its confinement SID, its capability SIDs, or `ALL_APPLICATION_PACKAGES`.
C  confinement_accesscheck_behavior  §6.9 L1697-1699
   Confined tokens are denied by default in AccessCheck unless the object explicitly opts in. This is real kernel behavior in AccessCheck, not just group membership.
C  confinement_capability_sids  §6.9 L1701-1703
   Confined services declare what they need via capability SIDs. Objects can grant access to specific capability SIDs.
P  confinement_scope_enforced  §6.9 L1703-1705
   A service that declares only filesystem access cannot touch the network, even if its user identity would otherwise permit it.

   LPAC is a confined token that lacks the `ALL_APPLICATION_PACKAGES` group; retains `ALL_RESTRICTED_APPLICATION_PACKAGES` instead.
C  lpac_smaller_access_surface  §6.9 L1710-1712
   LPAC tokens have a smaller default access surface because fewer objects grant to `ALL_RESTRICTED_APPLICATION_PACKAGES`.
C  lpac_kernel_eval_identical  §6.9 L1712-1713

C  confinement_exempt_flag  §6.9 L1715-1717
   A confinement-exempt token has confinement restrictions not evaluated.

### Section 6.10 — Process Protection (PIP)

   Unlike MIC, PIP actively revokes privilege-granted bits — even SeBackupPrivilege and SeTakeOwnershipPrivilege cannot bypass PIP.
P  pip_ptrace_blocked  §6.10 L1733-1737
   Kernel hooks on ptrace enforce PIP: even full admin privileges cannot ptrace a PIP-protected process.
P  pip_memory_access_blocked  §6.10 L1733-1737
   Kernel hooks on memory access enforce PIP: even full admin privileges cannot read memory of a PIP-protected process.
P  pip_signal_delivery_blocked  §6.10 L1733-1737
   Kernel hooks on signal delivery enforce PIP: even full admin privileges cannot send signals to a PIP-protected process.

### Section 6.16 — Linux Compatibility (summary)

### Summary Counts
- **Total tests extracted: 192**
- **Cargo tests (pure Rust logic, no kernel): 68**
- **Provium tests (requires booted KACS kernel): 124**

The Cargo tests cluster around AccessCheck evaluation logic (DACL ordered evaluation, conditional ACEs, inheritance flags, owner implicit grants, OWNER RIGHTS override, MIC no-write-up, PIP trust label revocation, privilege enable/disable semantics, restricted token dual-SID check, confinement default-deny, SD binary format correctness, SID parsing and comparison, token elevation types, claims evaluation, audit SACL matching).

The Provium tests cluster around syscall interception and kernel behavior (credential projection via getuid/getgid/getgroups, /proc visibility, capability switchboard enforcement for all 41 capabilities, setuid() no-op vs swap behavior, setuid bit on exec, seccomp filter installation, DAC neutralization, signal delivery authorization, PIP kernel hooks for ptrace/memory/signals, FACS xattr storage, SD inheritance propagation, process creation restrictions, impersonation per-thread lifecycle, logon session invalidation).

---

# Section 7: Tokens + Section 8: Process Security Block
## Exhaustive Test Corpus: KACS Specification §7 (Tokens) and §8 (Process Security Block)
---

### §7.0 Token Fundamentals (lines 1850-1923)
#### Cargo
- `token_is_refcounted_kernel_object`: Token is a separately-allocated, refcounted KACS kernel object [§7, line 1857]
- `cred_blob_holds_pointer_not_data`: The credential's LSM security blob holds a pointer to the token, not the token data itself [§7, line 1858]
- `token_carries_all_identity_fields`: Token carries SIDs, group memberships, privileges, integrity level, claims, and security policy [§7, lines 1859-1860]
- `token_supersedes_credential_for_kacs`: For all KACS-mediated access control decisions, the token supersedes traditional credential attributes [§7, lines 1861-1862]
- `token_mutation_no_cred_realloc`: Token-internal mutations (privilege enable/disable, group adjustment) do not require credential reallocation [§7, lines 1870-1872]
- `credential_immutable_token_mutable`: The credential is immutable after commit; the token it points to is not [§7, lines 1872-1873]
- `adjust_privilege_visible_to_all_sharers`: AdjustTokenPrivileges modifies the token in place; all threads sharing that token see the change immediately [§7, lines 1876-1878]
- `real_cred_holds_primary_token`: real_cred's LSM blob holds a pointer to the primary token (baseline identity inherited from parent on fork) [§7, lines 1891-1894]
- `cred_holds_effective_token`: cred's LSM blob holds a pointer to the effective token (either primary or impersonation) [§7, lines 1896-1900]
- `no_impersonation_same_cred_same_token`: In the common case (no impersonation), real_cred and cred point to the same struct cred, and both resolve to the same token object [§7, lines 1902-1903]
- `all_threads_share_primary_token`: All threads in a process share the primary token; privilege adjustments on the primary token are visible to every thread [§7, lines 1904-1906]
- `impersonation_is_cred_swap`: Impersonation is a credential swap: the thread's cred is pointed at a new struct cred whose LSM blob points to a different token object [§7, lines 1908-1909]
- `revert_restores_real_cred`: Reverting to self restores cred to real_cred [§7, line 1910]
- `projection_one_way_token_to_cred`: Credential projection is one-way: token state flows into credential fields, never the reverse [§7, lines 1918-1919]
- `projected_creds_observational_only`: Projected credentials are observational compatibility data; the token is the authority [§7, lines 1921-1922]

#### Provium
- `thread_identity_divergence`: Two threads in the same process can carry different effective tokens (one impersonating, one not) [§7, lines 1884-1886]
- `impersonation_swap_rcu_safe`: Impersonation swap uses override_creds/revert_creds and is atomically and RCU-safely handled [§7, lines 1911-1914]

---

### §7.1 Token Evaluation and Asynchronous Kernel Contexts (lines 1924-1993)
#### Cargo
- `access_check_at_synchronous_boundary`: Authorization is evaluated once at the synchronous boundary where the user requests access [§7.1, lines 1948-1950]
- `cached_mask_on_file_lsm_blob`: The granted access mask from AccessCheck at open() is cached on the file's LSM blob [§7.1, lines 1958-1960]
- `open_handles_survive_sd_changes`: Open handles survive subsequent SD changes; if a file's DACL is modified to deny access after open, existing fd retains its cached grants [§7.1, lines 1961-1966]

#### Provium
- `file_access_check_at_open`: AccessCheck runs at open() via security_file_open LSM hook [§7.1, lines 1958-1959]
- `reads_writes_verify_cached_mask`: Reads and writes verify the cached mask, not re-evaluate identity [§7.1, lines 1960-1961]
- `writeback_no_identity_reevaluation`: Writeback, journaling, and other deferred I/O never re-evaluate identity [§7.1, lines 1961-1962]
- `ipc_access_check_at_connect`: IPC AccessCheck runs at connection time; messages authorized by connection's cached state [§7.1, lines 1970-1972]
- `io_uring_captures_submitter_cred`: io_uring captures the submitter's effective credential at submission time and applies it to worker threads via override_creds [§7.1, lines 1974-1976]
- `io_uring_impersonation_token_honored`: Operations submitted through io_uring are evaluated under the submitter's identity including impersonation tokens [§7.1, lines 1977-1979]
- `kthread_no_override_hard_deny`: LSM hooks that detect running without a meaningful user context (PF_KTHREAD without override, interrupt context) must hard-deny rather than evaluate a meaningless identity [§7.1, lines 1991-1993]
- `kernel_maintenance_implicitly_trusted`: Kernel-internal maintenance (writeback, journaling, memory reclaim, deferred fput) operates on already-authorized file objects [§7.1, lines 1981-1984]

---

### §7.2 External Token Replacement (lines 1995-2037)
#### Cargo
- `external_replacement_primary_only`: If a thread is impersonating, replacement affects real_cred (primary token) only; impersonation state is left intact until the thread reverts [§7.2, lines 2009-2010]

#### Provium
- `external_token_replacement_via_task_work`: External token replacement uses task_work_add to queue a credential swap on each task in the target thread group [§7.2, lines 2004-2005]
- `each_task_executes_own_swap`: Each task executes the swap in its own context (prepare_creds, set new token pointer, commit_creds), preserving RCU safety [§7.2, lines 2005-2007]
- `gated_by_assign_primary_privilege`: External token replacement is gated by SeAssignPrimaryTokenPrivilege [§7.2, line 2008]
- `non_atomic_window_acceptable`: Brief transition window where some threads have new token while others still have old is acceptable because replacement is always a privilege downgrade [§7.2, lines 2012-2016]
- `no_completion_semantics`: No barrier or acknowledgment mechanism; caller cannot determine when all threads have executed the swap [§7.2, lines 2018-2019]
- `v1_mitigation_filter_token`: v1 mitigation: peinit uses FilterToken to create a copy of the SYSTEM token with dangerous privileges permanently deleted for pre-authd services [§7.2, lines 2025-2032]

### §7.4 Token Lifecycle Across Fork and Exec (lines 2232-2295)
#### Cargo
- `fork_deep_copies_primary_token`: Clone without CLONE_THREAD: child gets independent deep copy of parent's primary token [§7.4, lines 2238-2240]
- `fork_does_not_inherit_impersonation`: If parent is impersonating, the impersonation token is not inherited; child's effective credential is set from real_cred [§7.4, lines 2241-2242]
- `fork_mutations_invisible_to_other`: After fork, mutations to either token are invisible to the other [§7.4, lines 2242-2243]
- `clone_thread_shares_primary_token`: Clone with CLONE_THREAD: threads share the parent's real_cred (refcounted) and therefore share the same primary token object [§7.4, lines 2247-2249]
- `thread_priv_adjustments_visible_all`: Privilege adjustments on the primary token are visible to all threads [§7.4, lines 2249-2250]
- `thread_independent_impersonation`: Each thread maintains independent impersonation state via its own cred; new thread does not inherit another thread's impersonation [§7.4, lines 2250-2253]
- `exec_primary_token_survives`: Primary token survives execve unchanged unless NEW_PROCESS_MIN replaces it [§7.4, lines 2255-2256]
- `exec_reverts_impersonation`: If the calling thread is impersonating, impersonation is reverted before the new program runs (enforced in security_bprm_creds_for_exec) [§7.4, lines 2256-2258]
- `exec_starts_with_primary_token`: The new program always starts with the primary token as its effective identity [§7.4, lines 2258-2259]
- `new_process_min_can_only_lower`: NEW_PROCESS_MIN can only lower integrity, never raise it; child's integrity is always <= parent's [§7.4, lines 2292-2293]
- `new_process_min_creates_new_token`: NEW_PROCESS_MIN creates a new token rather than mutating an existing one, preserving token immutability [§7.4, lines 2280-2283]
- `new_process_min_integrity_from_file_label`: If file's integrity < token's integrity, create a new token with integrity_level set to the file's label; all other fields copied unchanged [§7.4, lines 2274-2276]
- `new_process_min_no_action_if_file_ge_token`: If file's integrity >= token's integrity, no action; fork'd token survives exec unchanged [§7.4, lines 2277-2278]
- `new_process_min_default_medium`: If the file has no label, use the default (Medium) [§7.4, lines 2271-2272]
- `new_process_min_flag_immutable`: The NEW_PROCESS_MIN flag is immutable on the token (set by authd at creation) [§7.4, lines 2293-2294]

#### Provium
- `fork_child_primary_token_independent`: After fork, parent and child have independent token objects; mutating parent's privileges does not affect child [§7.4]
- `fork_impersonating_parent_child_gets_primary`: If parent thread is impersonating, forked child starts with parent's primary (not impersonation) token [§7.4]
- `clone_thread_shares_primary_token_object`: New thread shares the same primary token object as siblings; privilege change visible to all threads [§7.4]
- `new_thread_no_inherit_impersonation`: A new thread does not inherit the creating thread's impersonation state [§7.4]
- `exec_reverts_impersonation_provium`: Thread impersonating calls execve; the new program starts with primary token, impersonation is reverted [§7.4]
- `exec_preserves_primary_token`: Primary token survives exec unchanged (no NEW_PROCESS_MIN) [§7.4]
- `new_process_min_lowers_integrity_on_exec`: Token with NEW_PROCESS_MIN policy: exec of lower-integrity-labeled binary creates new token with lower integrity [§7.4]
- `new_process_min_no_action_high_integrity_file`: Token with NEW_PROCESS_MIN: exec of same-or-higher-integrity-labeled binary keeps token unchanged [§7.4]
- `token_assignment_between_fork_and_exec`: peinit forks, installs service's token on child via SeAssignPrimaryTokenPrivilege, then child execs service binary [§7.4, lines 2260-2263]

### §7.6 Token Adjustment (lines 2401-2471)
#### AdjustPrivileges
##### Cargo
- `adjust_priv_requires_access_right`: AdjustPrivileges requires TOKEN_ADJUST_PRIVILEGES on the token [§7.6, line 2409]
- `adjust_priv_enable_disable_present_only`: Enable/disable flips bits in privileges_enabled for privileges that are present on the token; privileges not present cannot be enabled [§7.6, lines 2412-2415]
- `adjust_priv_cannot_grant_new`: Enable/disable cannot grant new privileges, only activate existing ones [§7.6, lines 2414-2415]
- `adjust_priv_reset_to_defaults`: Reset restores privileges_enabled to match privileges_enabled_by_default [§7.6, lines 2416-2418]
- `adjust_priv_remove_permanent`: Remove permanently deletes a privilege; clears the bit in all three masks (present, enabled, enabled_by_default) [§7.6, lines 2419-2421]
- `adjust_priv_remove_irreversible`: Removal is irreversible; the privilege cannot be re-added [§7.6, line 2421]
- `adjust_priv_remove_sets_used_for_audit`: Removal sets privileges_used for audit if the privilege was exercised before removal [§7.6, lines 2422-2423]
- `adjust_priv_returns_previous_state`: Caller receives a report of the previous state of each adjusted privilege [§7.6, lines 2425-2427]

##### Provium
- `adjust_priv_enable_disable_roundtrip`: Enable a present privilege, verify it is active; disable it, verify it is inactive [§7.6]
- `adjust_priv_enable_nonpresent_fails`: Attempting to enable a privilege not present on the token fails [§7.6]
- `adjust_priv_remove_then_enable_fails`: Remove a privilege, then attempt to enable it; operation fails [§7.6]
- `adjust_priv_reset_to_defaults_restores`: After enable/disable changes, reset restores all to default state [§7.6]
- `adjust_priv_without_access_right_denied`: AdjustPrivileges without TOKEN_ADJUST_PRIVILEGES access right fails [§7.6]
- `adjust_priv_visible_to_all_threads`: Privilege adjustment on primary token visible to all threads sharing it [§7.6]

#### AdjustGroups
##### Cargo
- `adjust_groups_requires_access_right`: AdjustGroups requires TOKEN_ADJUST_GROUPS on the token [§7.6, line 2431]

- `adjust_groups_without_access_right_denied`: AdjustGroups without TOKEN_ADJUST_GROUPS fails [§7.6]

#### AdjustDefault
##### Cargo
- `adjust_default_requires_access_right`: AdjustDefault requires TOKEN_ADJUST_DEFAULT on the token [§7.6, line 2450]
- `adjust_default_dacl_rcu_swap`: Default DACL replacement is an RCU pointer swap; readers see old or new value, never partial update [§7.6, lines 2452-2454]
- `adjust_default_owner_must_be_valid`: Owner SID index must reference user SID or a group with SE_GROUP_OWNER on the token [§7.6, lines 2456-2457]

- `adjust_default_no_escalation`: No escalation possible: caller chooses among SIDs already on their token, not adding new ones [§7.6, lines 2463-2464]

#### Shared Semantics
##### Cargo

- `adjustments_visible_immediately`: The change is visible immediately to all threads sharing the token [§7.6, lines 2469-2470]
- `adjustments_bump_modified_id`: All adjustments bump modified_id, invalidating cached AccessCheck results keyed on this token's identity [§7.6, lines 2470-2471]

##### Provium

- `cached_access_check_stale_after_adjustment`: A cached AccessCheck result from before an adjustment is stale (modified_id changed) [§7.6]

### §7.7 Linked Tokens and Elevation (lines 2473-2604)
#### Cargo
- `elevated_token_full_type`: Elevated token has elevation_type = Full, all groups active, all assigned privileges present and enabled [§7.7, lines 2495-2497]
- `filtered_token_limited_type`: Filtered token has elevation_type = Limited, administrative groups deny-only, dangerous privileges stripped [§7.7, lines 2498-2501]
- `filtered_created_via_filter_token`: Filtered token is created from the elevated token via FilterToken [§7.7, line 2501]
- `both_share_auth_id`: Both tokens in linked pair share the same auth_id (logon session) [§7.7, line 2503]
- `linked_via_weak_references`: Both tokens linked via weak references (linked_token field) [§7.7, line 2504]
- `no_linked_pair_default_elevation`: A token with no linked pair has elevation_type = Default [§7.7, line 2509]
- `unprivileged_query_returns_identification_copy`: When unprivileged caller queries a token's linked token, KACS returns a copy at Identification impersonation level [§7.7, lines 2523-2524]
- `identification_copy_cannot_be_used`: The Identification-level copy can inspect the elevated token but cannot be used for access control decisions, impersonation, or assignment as primary token [§7.7, lines 2525-2528]
- `tcb_privilege_gets_full_handle`: A caller holding SeTcbPrivilege receives a full handle to the actual linked token instead [§7.7, lines 2529-2530]
- `linked_token_query_exception_to_duplicate_model`: Returning a token copy via TOKEN_QUERY is an intentional exception to the normal access-right model [§7.7, lines 2531-2537]
- `session_termination_destroys_both_tokens`: Both tokens in a linked pair share a logon session; session termination destroys both [§7.7, lines 2603-2604]

##### Provium
- `query_linked_token_unprivileged`: Unprivileged process queries own token's linked token; receives Identification-level copy that cannot be installed for impersonation [§7.7]
- `query_linked_token_with_tcb`: TCB-privileged process queries linked token; receives full usable handle [§7.7]
- `identification_copy_reject_impersonation`: Attempt to install Identification-level linked token copy as impersonation token fails [§7.7]
- `identification_copy_reject_assign_primary`: Attempt to assign Identification-level linked token copy as primary token fails [§7.7]

### §7.8 Token Expiration and Revocation (lines 2606-2700)
#### Cargo
- `expiration_not_enforced_v1`: In v1, the expiration field is not enforced by KACS during access evaluation; AccessCheck does not consult it [§7.8, lines 2611-2613]
- `expiration_informational_only`: expiration exists for informational queries and future enforcement [§7.8, lines 2617-2618]
- `token_lifetime_by_refcount`: Token lifetime is governed by reference counting, not by expiration timestamp [§7.8, lines 2620-2621]
- `tokens_exist_while_any_reference`: Tokens exist as long as at least one reference (process credential or open fd) exists [§7.8, lines 2621-2622]
- `logon_session_identified_by_luid`: A logon session is a lightweight kernel object identified by a LUID (auth_id) [§7.8, lines 2630-2631]
- `every_token_references_logon_session`: Every token references a logon session [§7.8, line 2631]
- `multiple_tokens_share_session`: Multiple tokens can share a session (linked pairs, tokens derived via duplication) [§7.8, lines 2638-2640]
- `last_token_freed_destroys_session`: When the last token referencing a logon session is freed, the kernel destroys the session object [§7.8, lines 2641-2642]
- `session_cleanup_notifies_authd`: Session cleanup notifies authd (with dead session's auth_id asynchronously) [§7.8, lines 2642-2647]
- `logon_sessions_are_bookkeeping`: Logon sessions are bookkeeping; no access control decision depends on the logon session [§7.8, lines 2649-2650]
- `access_check_never_consults_auth_id`: AccessCheck never consults auth_id [§7.8, line 2650]
- `compare_tokens_uses_auth_id`: CompareTokens uses auth_id to determine whether two tokens originate from the same authentication event [§7.8, lines 2651-2653]
- `interactive_session_id_is_metadata`: interactive_session_id is metadata; no kernel security mechanism evaluates it [§7.8, lines 2655-2659]
- `no_token_revocation_primitive`: KACS does not provide a token revocation primitive; no "invalidate token X" or "kill session Y" syscall [§7.8, lines 2663-2665]

#### Provium
- `logon_session_creation_by_authd`: authd creates a logon session via KACS syscall at authentication time, before creating the token [§7.8, lines 2634-2636]
- `logon_session_cleanup_on_last_ref_drop`: When last token referencing a session is freed, session is destroyed [§7.8]
- `session_termination_is_userspace_coordination`: Session termination is userspace coordination: authd enumerates processes, requests termination, processes die, token references drop [§7.8, lines 2667-2677]
- `token_fd_survives_session_termination`: Token fd passed via IPC to process outside session survives session's process termination [§7.8, lines 2686-2693]

### §7.9 Token Access Rights (lines 2702-2797)
#### Cargo

- `token_fd_access_check_at_open`: Accessing a token requires passing an AccessCheck against that SD [§7.9, line 2707]

- `token_query_right_value`: TOKEN_QUERY = 0x0008; read token information [§7.9, line 2738]

- `token_duplicate_right_value`: TOKEN_DUPLICATE = 0x0002 [§7.9, line 2743]

- `delete_right_no_practical_effect`: DELETE right present for uniformity but has no practical effect for tokens [§7.9, line 2763]
- `implicit_self_access_for_query`: Thread always has implicit access to its own effective token for query operations [§7.9, lines 2731-2732]
- `self_access_no_fd_required`: Self-inspection (getuid, privilege checks) does not require opening a token fd [§7.9, line 2732]

- `default_sd_no_self_write_dac`: WRITE_DAC not granted to the token's subject by default [§7.9, line 2785]

##### Provium

- `open_process_token_requires_process_query`: Opening a process's token also requires sufficient access to the process itself (analogous to PROCESS_QUERY_INFORMATION) [§7.9, lines 2721-2723]

### §8.0 Process Security Block - Intro (lines 2799-2837)
#### Cargo
- `psb_not_affected_by_impersonation`: The PSB is never affected by impersonation; impersonation changes who the thread is acting as, not what the process is [§8, lines 2828-2830]
- `psb_on_task_struct_security`: PSB lives on task_struct->security (the task's own LSM blob), not on struct cred [§8, lines 2832-2836]
- `token_on_cred_psb_on_task`: Token lives on struct cred; PSB lives on task_struct->security [§8, lines 2832-2835]
- `impersonation_swaps_cred_not_task_blob`: Credential is swapped by impersonation; the task blob (PSB) is not [§8, line 2836]

#### Provium
- `psb_unchanged_during_impersonation`: A thread impersonating a client retains its process's PSB values (PIP, mitigations) unchanged [§8]
- `pip_stays_during_impersonation`: A Protected process impersonating a None client retains PIP protection [§8, lines 2810-2813]

### §8.1 PSB Object Model (lines 2838-2936)
#### Protection
##### Cargo
- `pip_type_enum_values`: pip_type is enum: Isolated, Protected, or None [§8.1, line 2847]
- `pip_type_immutable_after_exec`: pip_type is set at exec, immutable afterward [§8.1, line 2843]
- `pip_type_signing_based`: PIP fields are signing-based; determined by the binary's cryptographic signature at exec time [§8.1, lines 2850-2852]
- `pip_not_configurable_by_parent`: PIP not configurable by parent process; even compromised peinit cannot forge PIP for unsigned binary [§8.1, lines 2852-2854]
- `pip_trust_is_uint`: pip_trust is uint; higher values can access lower [§8.1, line 2848]
- `pip_trust_from_signer_identity`: pip_trust determined by the binary's signer identity [§8.1, line 2848]
- `public_key_compiled_into_kernel`: Public verification key is compiled into the kernel image [§8.1, line 2857]
- `kernel_only_verifies_never_signs`: Kernel only verifies signatures; it never signs [§8.1, line 2858]

#### Process Mitigations
##### Cargo
- `lsv_signed_libraries_only`: LSV: only cryptographically signed shared libraries can be loaded [§8.1, line 2879]
- `wxp_no_write_and_execute`: WXP: memory pages cannot be simultaneously writable and executable [§8.1, line 2880]
- `wxp_blocks_shellcode_injection`: WXP blocks shellcode injection [§8.1, line 2880]
- `tlp_approved_directories_only`: TLP: shared libraries can only be loaded from approved directories [§8.1, line 2881]
- `tlp_weaker_than_lsv`: TLP is weaker than LSV (trusts the path, not the binary) [§8.1, line 2881]
- `cfi_hardware_control_flow`: CFI: hardware control-flow enforcement (Intel CET shadow stack, ARM BTI) locked on and cannot be disabled [§8.1, line 2882]
- `mitigations_set_at_exec_immutable`: All mitigation fields determined by binary's metadata or signing properties at exec time; process cannot change them [§8.1, lines 2884-2886]
- `lsv_wxp_cfi_compose`: LSV + WXP + CFI compose: cannot inject new code (WXP), cannot reuse existing code out of order (CFI), cannot load malicious libraries (LSV/TLP) [§8.1, lines 2888-2893]

#### UI Access
##### Cargo
- `ui_access_set_at_exec_immutable`: ui_access is set at exec, immutable [§8.1, line 2895]
- `ui_access_bypasses_uipi`: ui_access permits interaction with higher-integrity UI elements (bypasses UIPI restrictions) [§8.1, line 2899]

#### Process Restrictions
##### Cargo
- `no_child_process_one_way`: no_child_process is one-way; once set, cannot be cleared [§8.1, lines 2903-2905]
- `no_child_process_blocks_fork_not_thread`: no_child_process blocks fork/clone without CLONE_THREAD; new threads unaffected [§8.1, line 2905]
- `no_child_process_set_between_fork_and_exec`: no_child_process can be set between fork and exec by the parent's code running in the freshly forked child [§8.1, lines 2910-2913]
- `no_child_process_set_at_runtime`: A process can set no_child_process on itself at any time [§8.1, lines 2914-2916]
- `no_child_process_via_kacs_syscall`: The mechanism is a KACS syscall operating on the calling process's own PSB [§8.1, lines 2918-2920]

##### Provium
- `no_child_process_blocks_fork`: Process with no_child_process set cannot fork (clone without CLONE_THREAD); fork fails [§8.1]
- `no_child_process_allows_thread_creation`: Process with no_child_process set can still create new threads (CLONE_THREAD) [§8.1]
- `no_child_process_cannot_be_cleared`: Once no_child_process is set, attempting to clear it fails [§8.1]
- `no_child_process_set_then_exec`: Process sets no_child_process between fork and exec; after exec, fork still blocked [§8.1]
- `no_child_process_impersonation_cannot_bypass`: Process with no_child_process impersonates a token without the restriction; fork still blocked because PSB is not affected by impersonation [§8.1]

#### Identity Virtualization
##### Cargo
- `virtualization_reserved_not_active_v1`: virtualization is reserved in PSB; not active in v1 [§8.1, line 2935]

---

### §8.2 Lifecycle (lines 2937-2957)
#### Cargo
- `fork_copies_psb`: At fork (clone without CLONE_THREAD), child receives a copy of parent's PSB [§8.2, lines 2939-2940]
- `pip_inherits_across_fork`: PIP fields, mitigations, and active restrictions inherited at fork [§8.2, lines 2940-2942]
- `protected_children_start_protected`: A Protected process's children start as Protected (PIP propagates across fork) [§8.2, line 2942]
- `exec_resets_pip_from_signature`: At exec, pip_type and pip_trust are reset based on new binary's cryptographic signature [§8.2, lines 2944-2945]
- `exec_resets_mitigations_from_metadata`: At exec, mitigation flags (lsv, wxp, tlp, cfi, ui_access) are reset based on new binary's metadata [§8.2, lines 2945-2946]
- `protected_parent_unsigned_child_loses_pip`: A Protected parent that execs an unsigned binary loses PIP protection [§8.2, lines 2947-2948]
- `no_child_process_persists_across_exec`: no_child_process flag persists across exec; a restricted process remains restricted regardless of what binary it loads [§8.2, lines 2950-2953]
- `clone_thread_shares_psb`: Threads share the process's PSB (CLONE_THREAD) [§8.2, line 2955]
- `thread_creation_not_affected_by_no_child`: Thread creation (CLONE_THREAD) is not affected by no_child_process [§8.2, lines 2956-2957]

#### Provium
- `fork_inherits_psb_pip_mitigations`: Fork inherits PIP fields and mitigations from parent to child [§8.2]
- `exec_unsigned_binary_loses_pip`: Protected process execs unsigned binary; child has pip_type = None [§8.2]
- `exec_signed_binary_gains_pip`: Non-protected process execs a signed binary; child has pip_type based on signature [§8.2]
- `no_child_process_survives_exec`: Process sets no_child_process, then execs a different binary; fork still blocked after exec [§8.2]
- `exec_resets_mitigations`: Process with lsv=true execs a binary without LSV requirement; lsv is reset to false [§8.2]

### §8.3 Relationship to AccessCheck (lines 2959-2985)
#### Cargo
- `psb_not_input_to_access_check_general`: PSB is not an input to AccessCheck in the general case [§8.3, lines 2961-2963]
- `pip_is_exception`: PIP is the exception; AccessCheck pipeline includes a PIP enforcement step that reads pip_type and pip_trust [§8.3, lines 2965-2966]
- `pip_from_psb_not_token`: PIP values come from the PSB (task_struct->security), not from any token [§8.3, lines 2967-2968]
- `pip_passed_as_explicit_params_to_access_check`: Enforcement layer extracts PIP values from PSB and passes them as explicit parameters to AccessCheck [§8.3, lines 2968-2970]
- `mic_uses_effective_token`: MIC (integrity level) uses the effective token; impersonation changes how MIC evaluates [§8.3, lines 2974-2977]
- `pip_uses_psb`: PIP (process protection) uses the PSB; impersonation does not change how PIP evaluates [§8.3, lines 2978-2980]
- `mitigations_no_access_check_interaction`: Process mitigations (lsv, wxp, tlp, cfi) and no_child_process do not interact with AccessCheck at all [§8.3, lines 2982-2985]

#### Provium
- `mic_changes_with_impersonation`: Thread impersonating a lower-integrity client; MIC uses impersonation token's integrity level for access evaluation [§8.3]
- `pip_unchanged_with_impersonation`: Thread impersonating a client; PIP check still uses process's PSB pip_type, not any token value [§8.3]
- `lsv_enforced_at_mmap_not_access_check`: LSV enforced at security_mmap_file hook, not through AccessCheck pipeline [§8.3]
- `wxp_enforced_at_mmap_and_mprotect`: WXP enforced at security_mmap_file and security_file_mprotect hooks [§8.3]
- `cfi_enforced_at_shstk_management`: CFI enforced at kernel CET management code, not AccessCheck [§8.3]

### §8.4 Process Security Descriptors (lines 2987-3117)
#### Cargo
- `every_process_has_sd`: Every process carries a security descriptor that controls who can perform operations on it [§8.4, lines 2989-2990]
- `process_sd_stored_on_psb`: Process SD is stored on the PSB [§8.4, line 2991]
- `process_terminate_right_value`: PROCESS_TERMINATE = 0x0001; send lethal signals [§8.4, line 3003]
- `process_signal_right_value`: PROCESS_SIGNAL = 0x0002; send non-lethal signals [§8.4, line 3004]
- `process_vm_read_right_value`: PROCESS_VM_READ = 0x0010 [§8.4, line 3005]
- `process_vm_write_right_value`: PROCESS_VM_WRITE = 0x0020; includes debugger attach [§8.4, line 3006]
- `process_dup_handle_right_value`: PROCESS_DUP_HANDLE = 0x0040 [§8.4, line 3007]
- `process_query_information_right_value`: PROCESS_QUERY_INFORMATION = 0x0400 [§8.4, line 3008]
- `process_query_limited_right_value`: PROCESS_QUERY_LIMITED = 0x1000 [§8.4, line 3009]
- `process_set_information_right_value`: PROCESS_SET_INFORMATION = 0x0200 [§8.4, line 3010]
- `generic_read_maps_to_process`: GENERIC_READ maps to PROCESS_QUERY_INFORMATION | PROCESS_VM_READ | READ_CONTROL [§8.4, lines 3018-3019]
- `generic_write_maps_to_process`: GENERIC_WRITE maps to PROCESS_SET_INFORMATION | PROCESS_VM_WRITE | WRITE_DAC [§8.4, line 3020]
- `generic_execute_maps_to_process`: GENERIC_EXECUTE maps to PROCESS_TERMINATE | PROCESS_QUERY_LIMITED [§8.4, line 3021]
- `generic_all_maps_to_all_process`: GENERIC_ALL maps to all process rights [§8.4, line 3022]

#### Default Process SD
##### Cargo
- `default_process_sd_owner_is_creator`: Default process SD owner is creator's user SID [§8.4, line 3029]
- `default_process_sd_self_generic_all`: Default SD: process's own user SID gets GENERIC_ALL [§8.4, line 3032]
- `default_process_sd_admins_generic_all`: Default SD: Administrators (S-1-5-32-544) get GENERIC_ALL [§8.4, line 3033]
- `default_process_sd_system_generic_all`: Default SD: SYSTEM (S-1-5-18) gets GENERIC_ALL [§8.4, line 3034]
- `default_process_sd_everyone_query_limited`: Default SD: Everyone (S-1-1-0) gets PROCESS_QUERY_LIMITED [§8.4, line 3035]
- `ps_top_works_for_all_users`: Everyone can see basic process info (PID, name, status) making ps and top work for all users [§8.4, lines 3042-3043]
- `detailed_inspection_restricted`: Detailed inspection (token, memory, environment) restricted to self, admin, and SYSTEM [§8.4, lines 3044-3045]

#### Enforcement via LSM Hooks
##### Cargo
- `task_kill_maps_to_terminate_or_signal`: security_task_kill maps to PROCESS_TERMINATE (lethal) or PROCESS_SIGNAL (non-lethal) based on signal number [§8.4, line 3058]
- `ptrace_read_maps_to_vm_read`: security_ptrace_access_check(MODE_READ) maps to PROCESS_VM_READ [§8.4, line 3059]
- `ptrace_attach_maps_to_vm_write`: security_ptrace_access_check(MODE_ATTACH) maps to PROCESS_VM_WRITE [§8.4, line 3060]
- `pidfd_getfd_maps_to_dup_handle`: security_ptrace_access_check(MODE_ATTACH|MODE_GETFD) maps to PROCESS_DUP_HANDLE [§8.4, line 3061]
- `pip_and_sd_complementary`: PIP and process SD are complementary, not redundant; SD controls who, PIP controls trust level [§8.4, lines 3070-3073]
- `both_pip_and_sd_must_pass`: Both AccessCheck against process SD and PIP trust level check must pass [§8.4, lines 3074-3079]
- `permissive_sd_but_pip_protected`: Process can have permissive SD but be PIP-protected; Administrators pass SD check but need sufficient PIP trust [§8.4, lines 3080-3082]
- `restrictive_sd_no_pip`: Non-PIP process can have restrictive SD that denies even Administrators specific operations [§8.4, lines 3083-3084]

#### Lifecycle
##### Cargo
- `fork_gets_new_default_sd`: At fork, child receives a new default SD; owner is forking thread's effective token's user SID [§8.4, lines 3088-3090]
- `exec_sd_not_reset`: At exec, the process SD is not reset; persists from fork time [§8.4, lines 3092-3095]
- `sd_reflects_creation_context_not_binary`: SD reflects process's creation context, not the binary it's running [§8.4, lines 3093-3094]
- `self_sd_modification_requires_write_dac`: Self-modification of process SD via kacs_set_sd requires WRITE_DAC (granted by default SD to process's own SID) [§8.4, lines 3097-3099]

#### Storage
##### Cargo
- `process_sd_inline_on_psb`: Process SD is stored inline on the PSB as a pointer to heap-allocated SD structure [§8.4, lines 3106-3108]
- `process_sd_freed_on_exit`: SD is freed when the process exits [§8.4, line 3109]
- `kacs_task_struct_has_proc_sd`: kacs_task struct contains proc_sd field (process security descriptor) [§8.4, lines 3112-3115]

##### Provium
- `kill_signal_requires_process_terminate`: Sending SIGKILL to a process requires PROCESS_TERMINATE access right on target's process SD [§8.4]
- `non_lethal_signal_requires_process_signal`: Sending SIGHUP requires PROCESS_SIGNAL [§8.4]

- `prlimit_requires_set_information`: prlimit on another process requires PROCESS_SET_INFORMATION [§8.4]
- `everyone_can_see_basic_info`: Unprivileged process can see PID, name, status of other processes (PROCESS_QUERY_LIMITED) [§8.4]
- `non_owner_cannot_read_maps`: Unprivileged non-owner/non-admin process cannot read /proc/<pid>/maps (requires PROCESS_QUERY_INFORMATION) [§8.4]
- `service_custom_sd`: Service launched with custom SD has different access control than default [§8.4]
- `self_tighten_sd`: Process tightens own SD after initialization (removes PROCESS_VM_WRITE from all principals); subsequent ptrace attach by Administrators fails [§8.4, lines 3099-3102]

- `exec_preserves_process_sd`: Process SD persists across exec; not reset to default [§8.4]

   AccessCheck does not walk up the directory tree to find inheritable ACEs
