# Section 12: Impersonation + Section 13: Process Integrity Protection
## Section 12: Impersonation
### 12.1 Impersonation Levels
P  anonymous_level_token_contains_only_anonymous_sid  12.1, 12.3
   When impersonation level is Anonymous, `kacs_impersonate_peer` and `kacs_open_peer_token` return a token containing only the Anonymous SID (`S-1-5-7`) -- no user SID, no groups, no privileges.
P  anonymous_level_hides_client_identity  12.1, 12.3
   At Anonymous level, both `kacs_impersonate_peer` and `kacs_open_peer_token` return a token that does not contain the client's actual user SID, group SIDs, or privileges.
P  identification_level_allows_sid_query  12.1
   A server impersonating an Identification-level token can read the client's SIDs and query their groups.
P  identification_level_blocks_access_check  12.1
   An Identification-level impersonation token cannot be used for AccessCheck against resources. A file open under Identification-level impersonation fails.
P  impersonation_level_allows_local_file_access  12.1
   A server impersonating at Impersonation level can open files and the access check evaluates against the client's identity.
P  impersonation_level_cascades_across_local_ipc  12.1
   If service A impersonates client B at Impersonation level and connects to local service C, service C sees client B's identity (identity cascades freely across local IPC).
P  delegation_level_identical_to_impersonation_locally  12.1
   For local operations, Delegation-level behaves identically to Impersonation-level: file access, registry reads, and local IPC connections all evaluate against the client's identity.
P  delegation_level_cascades_across_local_ipc  12.1
   Identity cascades across local IPC at Delegation level, same as Impersonation level.
C  delegation_level_flag_on_token  12.1, 12.6
   A Delegation-level impersonation token carries a flag indicating cross-machine Kerberos delegation is authorized. An Impersonation-level token does not carry this flag.
P  default_impersonation_level_is_impersonation  12.1
   If the client does not call `kacs_set_impersonation_level`, the default level on the socket is Impersonation.
P  client_can_set_level_to_anonymous  12.1
   The client can explicitly set the impersonation level to Anonymous via `kacs_set_impersonation_level` before `connect()`.
P  client_can_set_level_to_identification  12.1
   The client can explicitly set the impersonation level to Identification via `kacs_set_impersonation_level` before `connect()`.
P  client_can_set_level_to_delegation  12.1
   The client can explicitly set the impersonation level to Delegation via `kacs_set_impersonation_level` before `connect()`.
C  impersonation_level_ordering  12.1
   The four levels are ordered: Anonymous < Identification < Impersonation < Delegation.
### 12.2 The Two Gates
#### Identity Gate
C  identity_gate_same_user_same_restriction_passes  12.2
   If the server's primary token and client's token share the same user SID, and both are either restricted or both unrestricted, the identity gate passes.
C  identity_gate_same_user_restricted_vs_unrestricted_fails  12.2
   If the server and client share the same user SID but the server has a restricted token while the client has an unrestricted token (or vice versa), the identity gate fails.
P  identity_gate_restricted_cannot_impersonate_unrestricted_same_user  12.2
   A restricted (sandboxed) token cannot impersonate an unrestricted token of the same user -- prevents sandbox escape.
C  identity_gate_se_impersonate_privilege_passes  12.2
   If the server's primary token holds `SeImpersonatePrivilege` and it is enabled, the identity gate passes regardless of user SID match.
C  identity_gate_se_impersonate_disabled_fails  12.2
   If the server holds `SeImpersonatePrivilege` but it is not enabled, the identity gate fails (treated as if privilege is absent).
P  identity_gate_failure_caps_to_identification  12.2
   If neither same-user-same-restriction nor SeImpersonatePrivilege holds, impersonation level is silently capped to Identification. No error is returned; the call succeeds.
P  identity_gate_failure_no_error_returned  12.2
   When the identity gate fails, `kacs_impersonate_peer` succeeds (returns success), but the resulting token is Identification-level regardless of client's permitted level.
P  identity_gate_checks_primary_token_not_effective  12.2
   The identity gate is checked against the server's primary token (`real_cred`), not the effective/impersonation token. If the server is currently impersonating, its primary identity governs the gate.
#### Integrity Ceiling
C  integrity_ceiling_client_leq_server_passes  12.2
   If the client's token integrity level is less than or equal to the server's primary token integrity level, the integrity ceiling passes.
C  integrity_ceiling_client_gt_server_caps_to_identification  12.2
   If the client's token integrity level is greater than the server's primary token integrity level, the effective level is capped to Identification.
C  integrity_ceiling_medium_server_low_client_passes  12.2
   A Medium-integrity server can impersonate a Low-integrity client at full level.
C  integrity_ceiling_medium_server_medium_client_passes  12.2
   A Medium-integrity server can impersonate a Medium-integrity client at full level.
C  integrity_ceiling_medium_server_high_client_fails  12.2
   A Medium-integrity server cannot impersonate a High-integrity client at Impersonation level -- capped to Identification.
C  integrity_ceiling_not_bypassed_by_privilege  12.2
   `SeImpersonatePrivilege` does not bypass the integrity ceiling. A privileged Medium-integrity server impersonating a High-integrity token is still capped to Identification.
P  integrity_ceiling_checks_primary_token_not_effective  12.2
   The integrity ceiling is checked against the server's primary token, not the effective/impersonation token.
C  integrity_ceiling_unconditionally_enforced  12.2
   The integrity ceiling is always enforced, regardless of any privileges held. Even SYSTEM-integrity services cannot impersonate above their own integrity level.
#### Gate Composition
C  gate_composition_both_pass_preserves_client_level  12.2
   When both gates pass, the effective impersonation level equals the level the client set on the socket.
C  gate_composition_identity_fails_caps_to_identification  12.2
   When the identity gate fails but integrity ceiling passes, effective level is Identification.
C  gate_composition_integrity_fails_caps_to_identification  12.2
   When the identity gate passes but integrity ceiling fails, effective level is Identification.
C  gate_composition_both_fail_caps_to_identification  12.2
   When both gates fail, effective level is Identification.
C  gate_composition_starts_from_client_level  12.2
   The effective level computation starts with the level the client set, not a fixed maximum. If the client set Identification, both gates passing still yields Identification.
C  gate_composition_never_escalates  12.2
   The two gates can only reduce the impersonation level, never increase it above what the client set.
C  gate_composition_privilege_passes_identity_but_integrity_still_caps  12.2
   A server with SeImpersonatePrivilege (identity gate passes) at Medium integrity, impersonating a High-integrity client (integrity ceiling fails): effective level is Identification.
### 12.3 Anonymous Semantics
P  anonymous_socket_captures_no_real_identity  12.3
   When the client sets Anonymous level, the socket's LSM blob stores a token containing only the Anonymous SID; the client's actual user SID, groups, and privileges are not recorded.
P  anonymous_no_api_bypasses_client_choice  12.3
   There is no API that bypasses the client's Anonymous choice. If the client chooses Anonymous, the server cannot discover their identity through any mechanism.
P  anonymous_impersonation_skips_both_gates  12.3
   Any thread can impersonate the Anonymous identity without passing either the identity gate or the integrity ceiling.
P  anonymous_impersonation_no_privilege_needed  12.3
   Impersonating Anonymous requires no privilege (no SeImpersonatePrivilege needed).
C  anonymous_token_access_limited_to_anonymous_sid_and_everyone  12.3
   An Anonymous token has no access rights beyond what is explicitly granted to the Anonymous SID or Everyone.
### 12.4 The Impersonation Lifecycle
P  lifecycle_client_sets_level_before_connect  12.4
   The impersonation level must be set via `kacs_set_impersonation_level` before `connect()`.
P  lifecycle_identity_capture_at_connect_hook  12.4
   At `unix_stream_connect`, the LSM hook captures the client thread's effective credential and the socket's max impersonation level and stores the result on the socket's LSM blob.
P  lifecycle_anonymous_capture_stores_anonymous_token  12.4
   If the socket level is Anonymous, identity capture stores a token containing only `S-1-5-7` on the socket blob.
P  lifecycle_impersonation_capture_stores_effective_token  12.4
   For Impersonation or Delegation level, identity capture stores the connecting thread's effective token. If the thread is itself impersonating, the impersonated identity flows through.
P  lifecycle_identity_cascades_through_impersonating_connector  12.4
   If a connecting thread is itself impersonating client X, the downstream socket captures client X's identity (not the connector's primary identity), enabling identity cascade.
P  lifecycle_identification_capture_tagged  12.4
   For Identification level, the thread's effective token is stored but tagged at Identification level -- downstream server can inspect but not act as client.
P  lifecycle_impersonate_peer_evaluates_gates  12.4
   `kacs_impersonate_peer` retrieves the stored token from the socket blob and evaluates both gates against the server thread's primary token.
C  lifecycle_effective_level_is_minimum  12.4
   The effective impersonation level is the minimum of the stored level and whatever the gates permit.
P  lifecycle_override_creds_installs_impersonation  12.4
   After gate evaluation, `override_creds()` installs the impersonation token on the thread at the resulting level.
P  lifecycle_access_check_uses_impersonation_token  12.4
   All AccessCheck evaluations after impersonation use the impersonation token.
P  lifecycle_mic_uses_impersonation_integrity  12.4
   MIC uses the impersonation token's integrity level (not the primary token's).
P  lifecycle_pip_uses_psb_not_token  12.4
   PIP uses the PSB (unchanged by impersonation), not the impersonation token.
P  lifecycle_revert_restores_primary  12.4
   `kacs_revert()` restores the thread's `cred` to `real_cred`, returning to the service identity.
P  lifecycle_revert_noop_when_not_impersonating  12.4
   `kacs_revert()` is a no-op if the thread is not currently impersonating.
P  lifecycle_double_impersonation_replaces  12.4
   If a thread calls `kacs_impersonate_peer` while already impersonating, the kernel internally reverts and re-impersonates. The new impersonation replaces the old one.
P  lifecycle_double_impersonation_gates_use_primary  12.4
   During double impersonation, the gates are evaluated against the primary token (unaffected by previous impersonation), so the result is correct regardless of old impersonation.
### 12.5 Interaction with MIC and PIP
P  mic_uses_effective_token_under_impersonation  12.5
   MIC in AccessCheck compares the effective (impersonation) token's integrity level against the object's mandatory label, not the primary token's.
C  mic_impersonation_lowers_not_raises_integrity  12.5
   Because of the integrity ceiling, the effective token's integrity is always <= the primary token's integrity. A thread can never hold an impersonation token with higher integrity than its primary.
P  pip_reads_psb_not_effective_token  12.5
   PIP enforcement uses pip_type and pip_trust from the PSB, not from the impersonation token.
P  pip_immune_to_impersonation  12.5
   Impersonating a token carrying higher PIP values does not change the process's PIP enforcement. The PSB is fixed and immune to impersonation.
P  high_integrity_service_impersonating_low_client_gets_low_mic  12.5
   A High-integrity service impersonating a Low-integrity client: MIC evaluates at Low integrity (the client's), not High (the server's).
### 12.6 Delegation and the Network Boundary
C  delegation_token_carries_kerberos_authorization  12.6
   A Delegation-level impersonation token carries the authorization for the server to forward the client's identity to services on other machines.
C  impersonation_token_confined_to_local  12.6
   An Impersonation-level token is confined to the local machine -- it does not carry Kerberos credential forwarding authorization.
C  kacs_tracks_level_authd_acts_on_it  12.6
   KACS tracks the impersonation level on the token and socket. KACS has no Kerberos or network awareness -- the level is a flag that authd interprets.
### 12.7 SeImpersonatePrivilege
P  se_impersonate_privilege_allows_different_user  12.7
   With `SeImpersonatePrivilege` enabled, a service can impersonate tokens with different user SIDs at Impersonation level (assuming integrity ceiling passes).
P  without_se_impersonate_privilege_only_same_user  12.7
   Without `SeImpersonatePrivilege`, a process can only impersonate tokens that match its own user SID (and restriction status).
C  se_impersonate_checked_against_primary_token  12.7
   The privilege is checked against the server's primary token (`real_cred`), not the effective/impersonation token.
C  se_impersonate_does_not_bypass_integrity_ceiling  12.7
   `SeImpersonatePrivilege` bypasses only the identity gate. It does not bypass the integrity ceiling. A Medium-integrity service with the privilege cannot impersonate a High-integrity token at Impersonation level.
C  se_impersonate_must_be_enabled  12.7
   The privilege must be enabled at the time of the impersonation call. Holding but not enabling `SeImpersonatePrivilege` fails the identity gate.
C  se_impersonate_exercise_recorded_in_privileges_used  12.7
   When `SeImpersonatePrivilege` is exercised, it is recorded in the token's `privileges_used` field.
P  se_impersonate_exercise_emits_audit_event  12.7
   When `SeImpersonatePrivilege` is exercised, an audit event is emitted.
P  se_impersonate_during_double_impersonation_checks_primary  12.7
   A thread already impersonating client A tries to impersonate client B: the privilege check uses the server's primary token, not client A's token. Prevents leveraging impersonated privileges.
---

## Section 13: Process Integrity Protection
### 13.1 The Dominance Check
C  pip_dominance_requires_both_dimensions  13.1
   `pip_dominates(caller, target)` returns true iff `caller.pip_type >= target.pip_type AND caller.pip_trust >= target.pip_trust`. Both dimensions must pass.
C  pip_dominance_type_ge_trust_ge  13.1
   A caller with pip_type=Protected, pip_trust=5 dominates a target with pip_type=Protected, pip_trust=3.
C  pip_dominance_fails_if_type_lt  13.1
   A caller with pip_type=None dominates nothing with pip_type=Protected, regardless of pip_trust values.
C  pip_dominance_fails_if_trust_lt  13.1
   A caller with pip_type=Protected, pip_trust=3 does not dominate a target with pip_type=Protected, pip_trust=5 (trust dimension fails).
C  pip_none_target_trivially_dominated  13.1
   If the target has `pip_type = None`, dominance is trivially true for any caller -- unprotected processes are accessible to everyone.
C  pip_isolation_is_binary  13.1
   Process isolation is binary: dominate or don't. There is no partial access (no "can signal but not read memory" granularity at the process isolation level).
C  pip_dominance_equal_values_passes  13.1
   A caller with identical pip_type and pip_trust to the target dominates the target (>= on both dimensions).
### 13.2 Enforcement Points
#### ptrace
P  pip_ptrace_dominant_allowed  13.2
   A process that dominates the target can ptrace (attach, read, etc.) the target.
P  pip_ptrace_non_dominant_denied  13.2
   A process that does not dominate the target receives `-EACCES` on ptrace, regardless of ptrace mode.
P  pip_ptrace_se_debug_does_not_bypass  13.2
   `SeDebugPrivilege` does not bypass the PIP ptrace check. A process needs both the privilege (to bypass SD) AND PIP dominance (to bypass process isolation).
P  pip_ptrace_se_debug_without_dominance_denied  13.2
   A process with SeDebugPrivilege but without PIP dominance cannot ptrace a PIP-protected process.
#### Process Memory Access
P  pip_proc_mem_non_dominant_denied  13.2
   Reading `/proc/pid/mem` of a PIP-protected process from a non-dominant process is denied.
P  pip_process_vm_readv_non_dominant_denied  13.2
   `process_vm_readv()` against a PIP-protected process from a non-dominant process is denied.
P  pip_process_vm_writev_non_dominant_denied  13.2
   `process_vm_writev()` against a PIP-protected process from a non-dominant process is denied.
P  pip_proc_mem_dominant_allowed  13.2
   A dominant process can read `/proc/pid/mem` of a PIP-protected target.
#### Signal Delivery
P  pip_signal_non_dominant_denied  13.2
   A non-dominant process cannot send any signal to a PIP-protected process; `kill()` returns `-EACCES`.
P  pip_signal_all_signals_blocked_uniformly  13.2
   All signals are blocked uniformly for non-dominant callers -- no distinction between SIGTERM, SIGKILL, SIGSTOP, etc.
P  pip_signal_dominant_allowed  13.2
   A dominant process (e.g., peinit) can send signals to PIP-protected processes.
P  pip_signal_peinit_can_signal_all  13.2
   peinit (highest trust level) can signal any PIP-protected process because it dominates all of them.
P  pip_signal_sigterm_blocked_non_dominant  13.2
   SIGTERM to a PIP-protected process from a non-dominant process is denied.
P  pip_signal_sigkill_blocked_non_dominant  13.2
   SIGKILL to a PIP-protected process from a non-dominant process is denied.
P  pip_signal_sigstop_blocked_non_dominant  13.2
   SIGSTOP to a PIP-protected process from a non-dominant process is denied.
#### /proc Metadata
P  pip_proc_cmdline_non_dominant_denied  13.2
   A non-dominant process cannot read `/proc/pid/cmdline` of a PIP-protected process (returns `-EACCES`).
P  pip_proc_status_non_dominant_denied  13.2
   A non-dominant process cannot read `/proc/pid/status` of a PIP-protected process.
P  pip_proc_stat_non_dominant_denied  13.2
   A non-dominant process cannot read `/proc/pid/stat` of a PIP-protected process.
P  pip_proc_io_non_dominant_denied  13.2
   A non-dominant process cannot read `/proc/pid/io` of a PIP-protected process.
P  pip_proc_cgroup_non_dominant_denied  13.2
   A non-dominant process cannot read `/proc/pid/cgroup` of a PIP-protected process.
P  pip_proc_maps_non_dominant_denied  13.2
   A non-dominant process cannot read `/proc/pid/maps` of a PIP-protected process.
P  pip_proc_environ_non_dominant_denied  13.2
   A non-dominant process cannot read `/proc/pid/environ` of a PIP-protected process.
P  pip_proc_fd_non_dominant_denied  13.2
   A non-dominant process cannot read `/proc/pid/fd/` of a PIP-protected process.
P  pip_proc_metadata_dominant_allowed  13.2
   A dominant process can read all `/proc/pid/` metadata of a PIP-protected target.
P  pip_proc_pid_visible_in_directory_listing  13.2
   The PID directory is still visible in `ls /proc` (via `getdents`) even for PIP-protected processes -- only the contents are inaccessible, not the PID itself.
P  pip_proc_not_faceable  13.2
   `/proc` is not FACSable -- no SDs can be attached to procfs entries. PIP enforcement on /proc is a direct kernel check, not an AccessCheck evaluation.
#### /dev/mem and /dev/kmem
P  strict_devmem_enabled  13.2
   Peios builds with `CONFIG_STRICT_DEVMEM=y` -- physical RAM is inaccessible through `/dev/mem`.
P  dev_mem_restricted_sd  13.2
   FACS places a restrictive SD on `/dev/mem` and `/dev/kmem` that limits access to SYSTEM with appropriate privileges.
### 13.3 What PIP Does Not Protect Against
P  pip_kernel_module_bypasses_pip  13.3
   A loaded kernel module runs in ring 0 and can bypass PIP entirely (design fact, not a test per se -- but validates that SeLoadDriverPrivilege is the ceiling).
P  module_sig_force_enabled  13.3
   Kernel is built with `CONFIG_MODULE_SIG_FORCE=y` -- unsigned modules cannot load.
P  se_load_driver_stripped_from_non_peinit  13.3
   `SeLoadDriverPrivilege` is stripped from all tokens except peinit's. Only peinit can load kernel modules.
### 13.4 PIP and Impersonation
P  pip_process_isolation_uses_psb_under_impersonation  13.4
   When service A (Protected, trust 5) impersonates client B (whose token was created for a None-type process), process isolation checks still use service A's PSB. Service A can still signal/ptrace other PIP-protected processes it dominates.
P  pip_impersonation_does_not_grant_process_protection  13.4
   If a None-type process impersonates a token created for a Protected-type process, the process's PSB is still None -- it cannot touch PIP-protected processes regardless of the impersonated token.
P  pip_impersonation_ptrace_still_uses_psb  13.4
   A Protected service impersonating a None-type client can still ptrace PIP-protected targets it dominates (PSB governs, not impersonation token).
P  pip_impersonation_signal_still_uses_psb  13.4
   A Protected service impersonating a None-type client can still signal PIP-protected targets it dominates.
### 13.5 Coredumps
P  pip_protected_process_not_dumpable  13.5
   PIP-protected processes have the dumpable flag cleared at exec time (Option A). No core dump is generated on crash.
P  pip_coredump_not_readable_by_non_dominant  13.5
   Core dumps of PIP-protected processes (if generated via Option B crash handler) must not be readable by non-dominant processes.
---

## Summary
Key classification rationale:
- **Cargo tests** (37): Pure evaluation logic -- dominance check function, gate composition logic, impersonation level ordering, privilege state checks, token field assertions. All testable with data structures in userspace without a running kernel.
- **Provium tests** (81): Require LSM hooks firing, syscall behavior, procfs access, signal delivery, socket-based identity capture, `override_creds`/`revert_creds` lifecycle, kernel build configuration checks. All require a booted KACS kernel.

---

# Section 14: FACS (First Half)
## 1. KACS Open Syscall — Basic Semantics
P  kacs_open_read_data_grants_fmode_read  L9723, L11163
   kacs_open with FILE_READ_DATA in desired_access produces an fd with FMODE_READ
P  kacs_open_write_data_grants_fmode_write  L9724, L11164
   kacs_open with FILE_WRITE_DATA produces an fd with FMODE_WRITE
P  kacs_open_append_data_grants_fmode_write  L9724, L11164
   kacs_open with FILE_APPEND_DATA produces an fd with FMODE_WRITE
P  kacs_open_execute_alone_grants_fmode_exec  L9738, L11165
   kacs_open with only FILE_EXECUTE produces an fd with FMODE_EXEC (no data rights)
P  kacs_open_strict_mode_all_rights_required  L9714, L11159
   kacs_open fails if any bit in desired_access is denied by the SD
P  kacs_open_partial_deny_fails  L9714, L11159-11161
   kacs_open requesting FILE_READ_DATA + WRITE_DAC fails if SD grants read but denies WRITE_DAC
P  kacs_open_granted_mask_equals_requested  L9713-9714
   On success, the fd's granted mask equals exactly the requested desired_access
P  kacs_open_requires_at_least_one_data_or_execute_right  L9731-9734
   kacs_open with only WRITE_DAC (no data/execute rights) fails because f_mode would be invalid
P  kacs_open_read_data_satisfies_data_right_requirement  L9731-9734
   kacs_open with FILE_READ_DATA + WRITE_DAC succeeds (FILE_READ_DATA satisfies the data-right minimum)
P  kacs_open_execute_satisfies_data_right_requirement  L9731-9734
   kacs_open with FILE_EXECUTE + READ_CONTROL succeeds (FILE_EXECUTE satisfies the minimum)
P  kacs_open_metadata_only_rejected  L9765-9770
   kacs_open with only READ_CONTROL or WRITE_DAC (no data/execute) returns error
P  kacs_open_execute_only_no_read_data  L9742-9744
   An execute-only handle cannot read file contents (read returns EACCES)
P  kacs_open_execute_only_no_write_data  L9742-9744
   An execute-only handle cannot write file contents
P  kacs_open_execute_only_execveat_works  L9747-9749
   An execute-only handle works with execveat(fd, "", ..., AT_EMPTY_PATH)
P  kacs_open_directory_list_directory_maps_to_fmode_read  L9779-9787

---

**Summary counts:**

- Total tests extracted: **258**
- Cargo tests (pure Rust logic): **~35** (core rights mapping, inheritance algorithm, SD format/parsing, bitmask check function, disposition mapping)
- Provium tests (require running KACS kernel): **~223** (syscall behavior, LSM hook enforcement, handle model, capability management, SD operations, xattr protection, directory operations)

Many assertions listed as "Cargo + Provium" have a Cargo component (testing the mapping/algorithm logic in the kacs-core crate) and a Provium component (testing end-to-end behavior in a running kernel). The Cargo tests validate the computation; the Provium tests validate that the kernel applies it.

---

   `fremovexattr()` for a non-SD xattr on an fd without `FILE_WRITE_EA` returns `EACCES`
P  fremovexattr_sd_xattr_denied_unconditionally  §14.3 Patch 11 (10198)
   `fremovexattr()` for `security.peios.sd` / `system.ntfs_security` is denied unconditionally
P  fallocate_punch_hole_denied_on_append_only_fd  §14.3 Patch 8 (9960)
   `fallocate(FALLOC_FL_PUNCH_HOLE)` on an append-only fd returns `EPERM`
P  fallocate_zero_range_denied_on_append_only_fd  §14.3 Patch 8
   `fallocate(FALLOC_FL_ZERO_RANGE)` on an append-only fd returns `EPERM`
P  fallocate_collapse_range_denied_on_append_only_fd  §14.3 Patch 8
   `fallocate(FALLOC_FL_COLLAPSE_RANGE)` on an append-only fd returns `EPERM`
P  fallocate_insert_range_denied_on_append_only_fd  §14.3 Patch 8 (10696)
   `fallocate(FALLOC_FL_INSERT_RANGE)` on an append-only fd returns `EPERM`
### Group 2: File Open and Create
P  open_stamps_granted_mask_on_fd  §14.3 (9986–9989)
   A successful `open()` / `openat()` stamps the AccessCheck result (core + compat) as the fd's immutable granted mask
P  open_core_rights_must_be_fully_granted  §14.3 (9988)
   Legacy `open()` AccessCheck runs in subset mode: all core rights must be granted or open fails
P  kacs_native_open_strict_mode  §14.3 (9993)
   KACS-native open runs AccessCheck in strict mode: all requested rights must be granted or the open fails
P  open_read_data_sets_fmode_read  §14.3 (9996)
   `FILE_READ_DATA` in granted mask sets `FMODE_READ` on the file description
P  open_write_data_sets_fmode_write  §14.3 (9997)
   `FILE_WRITE_DATA` or `FILE_APPEND_DATA` in granted mask sets `FMODE_WRITE` on the file description
P  open_o_noatime_requires_write_attributes  §14.3 (10001)
   `O_NOATIME` flag on `open()` requires `FILE_WRITE_ATTRIBUTES` in the granted mask
P  o_path_fd_not_facs_managed  §14.3 (10008–10009)
   `O_PATH` fds carry no granted mask and are not FACS-managed
P  create_requires_file_add_file_on_parent  §14.3 (10064)
   Creating a new regular file checks `FILE_ADD_FILE` on the parent directory's SD
P  mkdir_requires_add_subdirectory_on_parent  §14.3 (10067)
   Creating a new directory checks `FILE_ADD_SUBDIRECTORY` on the parent directory's SD
P  mknod_requires_file_add_file_on_parent  §14.3 (10069)
   Creating a device node / pipe / socket checks `FILE_ADD_FILE` on the parent directory's SD
P  symlink_requires_file_add_file_on_parent  §14.3 (10073)
   Creating a symlink checks `FILE_ADD_FILE` on the parent directory's SD
P  new_file_sd_inherited_from_parent_atomically  §14.3 (10077–10081)
   New files inherit SDs from parent via `security_inode_init_security` — no window where newly created file has no SD (on xattr-capable deny-mode filesystems)
P  o_tmpfile_inherits_sd_from_directory  §14.3 (10093–10096)
   `open(dir, O_TMPFILE)` creates unnamed inode that inherits SD from the directory
P  o_tmpfile_linkat_checks_add_file_and_write_attributes  §14.3 (10100–10101)
   `linkat(fd, "", destdir, name, AT_EMPTY_PATH)` for O_TMPFILE checks `FILE_ADD_FILE` on dest dir and `FILE_WRITE_ATTRIBUTES` on source inode
P  o_tmpfile_linkat_preserves_original_sd  §14.3 (10098–10099)
   When O_TMPFILE inode is linked via `linkat`, the existing SD travels with the inode; no re-inheritance occurs
### Group 3: O_PATH fd Behavior
P  o_path_fstat_allowed_unconditionally  §14.3 (10014–10016)
   `fstat()` on an `O_PATH` fd is allowed unconditionally, regardless of SD
P  o_path_fstatfs_allowed_unconditionally  §14.3 (10014–10016)
   `fstatfs()` on an `O_PATH` fd is allowed unconditionally
P  o_path_at_syscalls_allowed  §14.3 (10017–10019)
   `*at()` syscalls using an `O_PATH` fd as dirfd are allowed; target is evaluated independently
P  o_path_fchdir_runs_live_accesscheck  §14.3 (10020–10023)
   `fchdir()` on an `O_PATH` directory fd runs a live AccessCheck for `FILE_TRAVERSE` against the directory's SD
P  o_path_fchmod_denied_ebadf  §14.3 (10024–10027)
   `fchmod()` on `O_PATH` fd returns `EBADF`
P  o_path_fchown_denied_ebadf  §14.3 (10024–10027)
   `fchown()` on `O_PATH` fd returns `EBADF`
P  o_path_mmap_denied_ebadf  §14.3 (10025)
   `mmap()` on `O_PATH` fd returns `EBADF`
P  o_path_exec_checks_file_execute_live  §14.3 (10540–10544)
   `execveat(O_PATH_fd, "", ..., AT_EMPTY_PATH)` falls back to live AccessCheck for `FILE_EXECUTE` on the binary's SD
P  o_path_bypasses_file_read_attributes  §14.3 (10041–10048)
   An SD that denies `FILE_READ_ATTRIBUTES` does not prevent attribute reads via `O_PATH` + `fstat()`
P  fstat_after_open_always_succeeds  §14.3 (10056–10061)
   `FILE_READ_ATTRIBUTES` is a core right for all legacy open modes, so `fstat()` after a successful `open()` always succeeds
P  sd_denying_read_attributes_causes_open_to_fail  §14.3 (10059–10060)
   An SD that denies `FILE_READ_ATTRIBUTES` causes legacy `open()` itself to fail (core right denied)
### Group 4: Data Operations (Read/Write/Truncate)
P  read_requires_file_read_data  §14.3 (10112)
   `read()` / `readv()` / `pread64()` / `preadv()` require `FILE_READ_DATA` in granted mask
P  write_requires_file_write_data  §14.3 (10113)
   Sequential `write()` on a non-append fd requires `FILE_WRITE_DATA` in granted mask
P  append_write_accepts_append_data_or_write_data  §14.3 (10114)
   Sequential write on an `O_APPEND` fd accepts either `FILE_APPEND_DATA` or `FILE_WRITE_DATA` (write_data is superset)
P  positioned_write_requires_write_data_not_append  §14.3 (10115)
   `pwrite()` family requires `FILE_WRITE_DATA`; `FILE_APPEND_DATA` alone is insufficient for positioned writes
P  readdir_requires_file_list_directory  §14.3 (10116)
   `readdir()` / `getdents()` / `getdents64()` on a directory fd requires `FILE_LIST_DIRECTORY` in granted mask
P  ftruncate_requires_file_write_data  §14.3 (10122–10124)
   `ftruncate()` requires `FILE_WRITE_DATA` in granted mask; `FILE_APPEND_DATA` alone is insufficient
P  truncate_path_based_requires_write_data  §14.4 (10693)
   Path-based `truncate()` runs live AccessCheck for `FILE_WRITE_DATA`
P  sendfile_checks_both_fds  §14.4 (10678)
   `sendfile()` checks `FILE_READ_DATA` on source fd and `FILE_WRITE_DATA` on dest fd
P  copy_file_range_checks_both_fds  §14.4 (10679)
   `copy_file_range()` checks `FILE_READ_DATA` on source and `FILE_WRITE_DATA` on dest
P  splice_checks_direction  §14.4 (10680)
   `splice()` checks `FILE_READ_DATA` or `FILE_WRITE_DATA` depending on direction
P  fallocate_extend_accepts_write_or_append  §14.4 (10694)
   `fallocate()` for extend/preallocate accepts `FILE_WRITE_DATA` or `FILE_APPEND_DATA`
### Group 5: Memory Mapping (mmap/mprotect)
P  mmap_prot_read_requires_read_data  §14.3 (10131)
   `mmap(PROT_READ)` requires `FILE_READ_DATA` in granted mask
P  mmap_prot_write_map_shared_requires_write_data  §14.3 (10132)
   `mmap(PROT_WRITE, MAP_SHARED)` requires `FILE_WRITE_DATA`; `FILE_APPEND_DATA` is insufficient for shared writable mappings
P  mmap_prot_exec_requires_file_execute  §14.3 (10133)
   `mmap(PROT_EXEC)` requires `FILE_EXECUTE` in granted mask
P  mmap_prot_exec_does_not_require_mode_execute_bit  §14.3 (10512–10524)
   `mmap(PROT_EXEC)` does not require the mode execute bit (only `execve` does)
P  mmap_prot_write_map_private_requires_read_data  §14.4 (10705)
   `mmap(PROT_WRITE, MAP_PRIVATE)` requires only `FILE_READ_DATA` (copy-on-write, no write to file)
P  mmap_audit_bit_25_denies_mmap  §14.3 (10135–10140)
   If SACL alarm ACE sets bit 25 in audit mask for the opener's SID, `mmap()` is denied regardless of granted rights
P  mprotect_prevents_escalation  §14.3 (10143–10145)
   `mprotect()` upgrading `PROT_READ` mapping to `PROT_WRITE` requires `FILE_WRITE_DATA` in granted mask
P  mprotect_same_checks_as_mmap  §14.3 (10143)
   `mprotect()` applies same right checks as `mmap()` for new protection flags
P  mremap_no_lsm_hook  §14.4 (10707)
   `mremap()` has no LSM hook; inherits mapping permissions from the original mapping
### Group 6: File Locking
P  flock_shared_requires_read_data  §14.3 (10151)
   `flock(LOCK_SH)` requires `FILE_READ_DATA` in granted mask
P  flock_exclusive_requires_write_data_or_append  §14.3 (10152)
   `flock(LOCK_EX)` requires `FILE_WRITE_DATA` or `FILE_APPEND_DATA` in granted mask
P  fcntl_rdlck_requires_read_data  §14.3 (10151)
   `fcntl(F_RDLCK)` requires `FILE_READ_DATA` in granted mask
P  fcntl_wrlck_requires_write_or_append  §14.3 (10152)
   `fcntl(F_WRLCK)` requires `FILE_WRITE_DATA` or `FILE_APPEND_DATA` in granted mask
### Group 7: fcntl Operations
P  fcntl_setfl_o_noatime_requires_write_attributes  §14.3 (10325)
   `fcntl(F_SETFL)` adding `O_NOATIME` requires `FILE_WRITE_ATTRIBUTES` in granted mask
P  fcntl_clear_o_append_denied_without_write_data  §14.3 (10326–10327)
   `fcntl(F_SETFL)` clearing `O_APPEND` is denied if fd has `FILE_APPEND_DATA` but not `FILE_WRITE_DATA`
P  fcntl_set_o_append_always_allowed  §14.3 (10328–10331)
   `fcntl(F_SETFL)` setting `O_APPEND` is always allowed (privilege reduction)
P  fcntl_setown_setsig_allowed  §14.3 (10332)
   `fcntl(F_SETOWN)` and `fcntl(F_SETSIG)` are allowed unconditionally
### Group 8: ioctl Classification
P  ioctl_fs_ioc_setflags_requires_write_attributes  §14.3 (10340)
   `FS_IOC_SETFLAGS` on a regular file requires `FILE_WRITE_ATTRIBUTES`
P  ioctl_fs_ioc_getflags_requires_read_attributes  §14.3 (10342)
   `FS_IOC_GETFLAGS` on a regular file requires `FILE_READ_ATTRIBUTES`
P  ioctl_ficlone_requires_write_data_on_dest  §14.3 (10341)
   `FICLONE` / `FICLONERANGE` requires `FILE_WRITE_DATA` on destination fd
P  ioctl_fiemap_requires_read_data  §14.3 (10343)
   `FIEMAP` / `FS_IOC_FIEMAP` requires `FILE_READ_DATA`
P  ioctl_fitrim_requires_write_data  §14.3 (10344)
   `FITRIM` requires `FILE_WRITE_DATA`
P  ioctl_unclassified_denied_on_regular_files  §14.3 (10346–10348)
   Unclassified (unknown) ioctls on regular files and directories are denied
P  ioctl_device_requires_any_data_right  §14.3 (10360–10362)
   Device node ioctls are allowed if fd has at least one data right or `KACS_FILE_IOCTL_ONLY`
C  ioctl_direction_bits_not_security_classifier  §14.3 (10373–10374)
   `_IOC_DIR` is not used as a security classifier; ioctl direction bits describe buffer flow only
### Group 9: Directory Traversal and SeChangeNotifyPrivilege
P  traverse_skipped_with_change_notify_privilege  §14.3 (10391–10393)
   Path resolution skips per-directory `FILE_TRAVERSE` checks when `SeChangeNotifyPrivilege` is held
P  traverse_checked_without_change_notify_privilege  §14.3 (10393)
   Without `SeChangeNotifyPrivilege`, FACS checks `FILE_TRAVERSE` on each intermediate directory's SD during path resolution
P  traverse_default_inert  §14.3 (10395–10399)
   In default configuration (all principals have `SeChangeNotifyPrivilege`), directory `FILE_TRAVERSE` ACEs are effectively inert for path resolution
P  access_x_ok_on_dir_checks_file_traverse  §14.4 (10751)
   `access(dir, X_OK)` checks `FILE_TRAVERSE` on the directory
P  access_x_ok_succeeds_with_change_notify_privilege  §14.3 (10407–10411)
   `access(dir, X_OK)` returns success when `SeChangeNotifyPrivilege` is held (privilege applies to all MAY_EXEC directory checks)
P  fchdir_normal_fd_checks_granted_mask_traverse  §14.3 (10413–10417)
   `fchdir()` on a normal fd checks `FILE_TRAVERSE` in the fd's granted mask (handle model, patch 16)
P  fchdir_not_affected_by_change_notify_privilege  §14.3 (10413–10417)
   `fchdir()` requires `FILE_TRAVERSE` in the fd's granted mask regardless of `SeChangeNotifyPrivilege`
P  fchdir_denied_without_traverse_in_granted_mask  §14.3 (10400, 10834)
   `fchdir()` on a normal fd without `FILE_TRAVERSE` in granted mask is denied
P  inode_permission_defers_non_dir_to_file_open  §14.3 (10385–10388)
   `security_inode_permission` on non-directory final component returns 0 (allow) and defers to `security_file_open`
### Group 10: Link Operations
P  link_requires_add_file_on_dest_dir  §14.3 (10421–10422)
   `link()` / `linkat()` checks `FILE_ADD_FILE` on destination directory SD
P  link_requires_write_attributes_on_source  §14.3 (10422)
   `link()` / `linkat()` checks `FILE_WRITE_ATTRIBUTES` on source inode SD
P  unlink_requires_delete_or_parent_delete_child  §14.3 (10425–10427)
   `unlink()` / `unlinkat()` requires either `DELETE` on the file OR `FILE_DELETE_CHILD` on the parent directory (either is sufficient)
P  unlink_succeeds_with_only_delete_on_file  §14.3 (10426)
   `unlink()` succeeds if caller has `DELETE` on the file but not `FILE_DELETE_CHILD` on parent
P  unlink_succeeds_with_only_delete_child_on_parent  §14.3 (10426)
   `unlink()` succeeds if caller has `FILE_DELETE_CHILD` on parent but not `DELETE` on file
P  rmdir_requires_delete_or_parent_delete_child  §14.3 (10429–10430)
   `rmdir()` same as unlink: `DELETE` on directory OR `FILE_DELETE_CHILD` on parent (either sufficient)
### Group 11: Rename Operations
P  rename_plain_requires_delete_on_source  §14.3 (10437)
   Plain `rename()` requires `DELETE` on source OR `FILE_DELETE_CHILD` on source parent
P  rename_plain_requires_add_file_on_dest_dir  §14.3 (10437)
   Plain `rename()` requires `FILE_ADD_FILE` on destination directory (or `FILE_ADD_SUBDIRECTORY` for dirs)
P  rename_overwrite_requires_delete_on_existing_dest  §14.3 (10438)
   Rename overwriting existing dest requires `DELETE` on existing dest OR `FILE_DELETE_CHILD` on dest parent
P  rename_exchange_requires_delete_on_both  §14.3 (10439)
   `renameat2(RENAME_EXCHANGE)` requires `DELETE` or `FILE_DELETE_CHILD` on both source and dest sides
P  rename_whiteout_requires_add_file_on_source_parent  §14.3 (10440)
   `renameat2(RENAME_WHITEOUT)` requires same as plain rename plus `FILE_ADD_FILE` on source parent for whiteout creation
P  rename_same_volume_preserves_sd  §14.3 (10442)
   Same-volume rename preserves the SD (same inode, same xattr)
### Group 12: Symlink Operations
P  readlink_requires_read_data_on_symlink  §14.3 (10452–10453)
   `readlink()` / `readlinkat()` checks `FILE_READ_DATA` on the symlink's own SD, not the target's
P  follow_link_allowed_unconditionally  §14.3 (10455–10457)
   `security_inode_follow_link` allows unconditionally; the target's SD is evaluated at target open
### Group 13: Execution
P  execve_path_based_requires_file_execute  §14.3 (10468–10470)
   `execve()` path-based runs live AccessCheck for `FILE_EXECUTE` on the binary's SD
P  execveat_fd_based_checks_granted_mask  §14.3 (10472–10474)
   `execveat(fd, "", ..., AT_EMPTY_PATH)` checks `FILE_EXECUTE` in the fd's granted mask (patch 15)
P  exec_fd_without_file_execute_denied  §14.3 (10488–10490)
   An fd without `FILE_EXECUTE` in its granted mask cannot be used for exec, even if the current SD would allow it
P  exec_sd_change_after_open_does_not_affect_granted_mask  §14.3 (10490)
   SD changes after open do not affect the granted mask; fd-based exec uses the snapshot
P  exec_requires_mode_execute_bit_live  §14.3 (10492–10497)
   Execute mode-bit (`+x`) is checked live against the inode at exec time; removing `+x` after fd open causes exec to fail
P  execve_requires_both_mode_bit_and_file_execute  §14.3 (10520–10521)
   For `execve`: both `+x` mode bit AND `FILE_EXECUTE` must be true
P  exec_binfmt_chain_checks_interpreter_sd  §14.3 (10476–10482)
   In binfmt chain (shebang → interpreter), subsequent `bprm_check` invocations check the interpreter's SD via live AccessCheck, not the original fd's granted mask
P  bprm_creds_from_file_suppresses_setuid_setgid  §14.3 (10546–10548)
   `security_bprm_creds_from_file` suppresses setuid/setgid file capabilities
P  bprm_creds_for_exec_reasserts_dac_bypass_caps  §14.3 (10461–10462)
   `security_bprm_creds_for_exec` reasserts four DAC bypass capabilities on new credential set
### Group 14: FD Transfer and Lifecycle
P  scm_rights_transfer_allowed_unconditionally  §14.3 (10553–10556)
   `SCM_RIGHTS` fd transfer is allowed unconditionally in `security_file_receive`; fd is a capability token
P  fd_transfer_does_not_reevaluate_mic  §14.3 (10566–10572)
   MIC and PIP are not re-evaluated on fd recipients; authority is on the handle, not the holder
P  dup_preserves_granted_mask  §14.4 (10816–10818)
   `dup()` / `dup2()` / `dup3()` / `F_DUPFD` produce same file description with same granted mask
P  fork_inherits_fds_same_granted_masks  §14.4 (10826)
   `fork()` / `clone()` child inherits fds with same granted masks
P  exec_non_cloexec_fd_survives_same_granted_mask  §14.4 (10827)
   Fds without `FD_CLOEXEC` survive exec with same granted mask
P  file_free_frees_granted_mask  §14.3 (10574–10575)
   `security_file_free` frees the granted mask on file description cleanup; no security decision
### Group 15: Credential Management
P  prepare_creds_asserts_implementation_caps  §14.3 (10579–10580)
   `security_prepare_creds` asserts six implementation capabilities on new credential sets
P  capset_denies_clearing_implementation_caps  §14.3 (10582)
   `security_capset` denies clearing the six implementation capabilities
P  prctl_denies_ambient_raise_implementation_caps  §14.3 (10584–10586)
   `security_task_prctl` denies ambient capability raises affecting the six implementation capabilities
P  prctl_denies_bounding_set_reduction_implementation_caps  §14.3 (10585)
   `security_task_prctl` denies bounding set reductions affecting the six implementation capabilities
### Group 16: Dentry-Based Hook Coordination (File + Dentry Dedup)
P  file_hook_sets_decision_marker  §14.3 (10218–10220)
   File-based hook populates `kacs_file_decision` with inode and op_class before returning
P  dentry_hook_noop_when_file_hook_decided  §14.3 (10218–10225)
   Dentry-based hook is a no-op when `kacs_file_decision` matches inode and op_class
P  dentry_hook_evaluates_on_mismatch  §14.3 (10222–10224)
   Dentry-based hook evaluates normally when `kacs_file_decision` does not match (different inode or op_class)
P  decision_marker_cleared_after_dentry_hook  §14.3 (10224–10225)
   `kacs_file_decision` struct is cleared unconditionally at the end of each dentry-based hook
P  decision_marker_scoped_single_syscall  §14.3 (10229–10230)
   Decision marker scope is exactly one syscall invocation, one inode, one operation class
P  overlayfs_marker_not_consumed_by_wrong_hook  §14.3 (10236–10242)
   In stacked filesystems (overlayfs), marker is not consumed by wrong hook because different inode
### Group 17: Path-Based Metadata Operations
P  path_chmod_requires_write_dac  §14.3 (10265)
   Path-based `chmod()` / `fchmodat()` checks `WRITE_DAC` via `security_inode_setattr`
P  path_chown_requires_write_owner  §14.3 (10266)
   Path-based `chown()` / `lchown()` / `fchownat()` checks `WRITE_OWNER` via `security_inode_setattr`
P  path_truncate_requires_write_data  §14.3 (10267)
   Path-based `truncate()` (`ATTR_SIZE`) checks `FILE_WRITE_DATA` via `security_inode_setattr`
P  path_utimensat_requires_write_attributes  §14.3 (10268)
   Path-based `utimensat()` / `utimes()` checks `FILE_WRITE_ATTRIBUTES` via `security_inode_setattr`
P  path_stat_requires_read_attributes  §14.3 (10272–10274)
   Path-based `stat()` / `lstat()` checks `FILE_READ_ATTRIBUTES` via `security_inode_getattr`
P  path_setxattr_sd_denied_unconditionally  §14.3 (10281)
   Path-based `setxattr()` for `security.peios.sd` / `system.ntfs_security` is denied unconditionally
P  path_setxattr_posix_acl_denied_unconditionally  §14.3 (10282)
   Path-based `setxattr()` for `system.posix_acl_access` / `system.posix_acl_default` is denied unconditionally
P  path_setxattr_normal_requires_write_ea  §14.3 (10283)
   Path-based `setxattr()` for other xattrs checks `FILE_WRITE_EA` via AccessCheck
P  path_getxattr_sd_denied_unconditionally  §14.3 (10292–10293)
   Path-based `getxattr()` for `security.peios.sd` / `system.ntfs_security` returns `-EACCES` unconditionally
P  path_getxattr_normal_requires_read_ea  §14.3 (10294)
   Path-based `getxattr()` for non-SD xattrs checks `FILE_READ_EA` via AccessCheck
P  path_removexattr_sd_denied_unconditionally  §14.3 (10309–10311)
   Path-based `removexattr()` for SD xattrs is denied unconditionally
P  path_removexattr_normal_requires_write_ea  §14.3 (10311)
   Path-based `removexattr()` for other xattrs checks `FILE_WRITE_EA` via AccessCheck
P  listxattr_allowed_unconditionally  §14.3 (10314–10317)
   `listxattr()` / `flistxattr()` / `llistxattr()` is allowed unconditionally; xattr names are not sensitive
P  posix_acl_set_denied_unconditionally  §14.3 (10319–10320)
   `security_inode_set_acl` denies POSIX ACL setting unconditionally
### Group 18: access() / faccessat() Behavior
P  access_f_ok_no_accesscheck  §14.4 (10748)
   `access(path, F_OK)` is an existence check only; no AccessCheck runs
P  access_r_ok_file_checks_read_data  §14.4 (10749)
   `access(path, R_OK)` on a file checks `FILE_READ_DATA`
P  access_r_ok_dir_checks_list_directory  §14.4 (10749)
   `access(dir, R_OK)` checks `FILE_LIST_DIRECTORY`
P  access_w_ok_file_checks_write_data  §14.4 (10750)
   `access(path, W_OK)` on a file checks `FILE_WRITE_DATA`
P  access_w_ok_dir_checks_add_file  §14.4 (10750)
   `access(dir, W_OK)` checks `FILE_ADD_FILE` (approximation)
P  access_x_ok_file_checks_file_execute  §14.4 (10751)
   `access(path, X_OK)` on a file checks `FILE_EXECUTE`
P  access_is_advisory_only  §14.4 (10753–10754)
   `access()` answers "does the SD broadly permit this?" not "will the next syscall succeed"
P  access_at_eaccess_is_noop  §14.4 (10742)
   `AT_EACCESS` flag is a no-op because FACS always uses effective token (patch 5)
### Group 19: Corrupt SD Handling
P  corrupt_sd_denies_all_access  §14.2 (10882–10883)
   A corrupt `security.peios.sd` xattr (truncated, invalid ACE, malformed SID) denies all access; AccessCheck is not called
C  corrupt_sd_truncated_dacl_not_treated_as_empty  §14.2 (10885)
   A truncated DACL must not be treated as empty (which would grant `GENERIC_ALL` to everyone)
C  corrupt_sd_garbled_ace_not_skipped  §14.2 (10886)
   A garbled ACE must not be skipped (could remove a critical deny entry)
P  corrupt_sd_emits_audit_event  §14.2 (10888–10894)
   Every corrupt SD encounter emits an audit event with file path/inode, xattr size, parse failure reason, mount path
P  corrupt_sd_audit_once_per_inode_per_cache  §14.2 (10897)
   Audit event fires once per inode per cache population, not on every access attempt
P  corrupt_sd_state_cached_sentinel  §14.2 (10897–10898)
   Corrupt state is cached as a sentinel value in `i_security` to avoid repeated xattr reads
P  corrupt_sd_recovery_requires_restore_privilege  §14.2 (10902–10906)
   Online recovery from corrupt SD requires a process with `SeRestorePrivilege` to call set-security syscall
P  corrupt_sd_no_unprivileged_recovery  §14.2 (10906–10907)
   No unprivileged recovery path exists for corrupt SDs (corrupt SD denies `WRITE_DAC` and `WRITE_OWNER`)
### Group 20: SD Validation (Cargo — pure parse/format logic)
C  sd_parse_detects_truncated_blob  §14.2 (10879–10880)
   SD parser detects and rejects a truncated binary blob
C  sd_parse_detects_invalid_ace_type  §14.2 (10879)
   SD parser detects and rejects an invalid ACE type value
C  sd_parse_detects_malformed_sid  §14.2 (10879, 10892–10893)
   SD parser detects and rejects a malformed SID (e.g., sub-authority count exceeds remaining buffer)
C  sd_parse_detects_size_mismatch  §14.2 (10879)
   SD parser detects and rejects size mismatch in SD/ACL headers
C  sd_parse_detects_acl_size_exceeding_buffer  §14.2 (10880)
   SD parser detects ACL size field exceeding the actual buffer size
C  sd_parse_any_error_is_corrupt  §14.2 (10880)
   Any parse error in the xattr blob produces a corrupt-SD result, not a partial parse
### Group 21: Handle Model Core Logic
C  granted_mask_subset_check  §14.3 (9928–9929)
   Fd-based operation check is `(fd->granted & required) == required`; pass if all required bits present
P  granted_mask_immutable_after_open  §14.3 (9989, 10490)
   Granted mask set at open time is immutable for the lifetime of the fd
C  granted_mask_no_accesscheck_no_sd_read  §14.3 (9929)
   Fd-based checks do not call AccessCheck and do not read the SD
### Group 22: Special Filesystem Handling
P  fat_always_synthesize_mode  §14.2 (9835–9838)
   FAT (vfat) uses synthesize mode with mount-level template; every access synthesizes ephemerally
P  ntfs_uses_system_ntfs_security_xattr  §14.2 (9840–9841)
   NTFS (ntfs3) reads/writes SD from `system.ntfs_security` xattr; SDs round-trip to Windows
P  tmpfs_supports_xattrs_facs_normal  §14.2 (9846–9848)
   tmpfs supports xattrs; FACS works normally with mount root SD set by init
P  devtmpfs_sd_applied_by_udev_helper  §14.2 (9850–9852)
   devtmpfs device node SDs are applied by udev `RUN+=` helper after device creation
P  procfs_not_facs_managed_pip_protected  §14.2 (9854)
   `/proc` is not FACS-managed; protected by PIP (not SD-based access control)
P  sysfs_writes_require_admin_or_system  §14.2 (9855–9856)
   `/sys` uses hardcoded rule: writes require Administrators or SYSTEM
P  nfs_synthesize_mode_with_template  §14.2 (9858–9859)
   NFS client mounts use synthesize mode with mount-level template
C  nfs_not_sole_authority  §14.2 (9862–9864)
   NFS client mounts: FACS is not sole authority; server enforces independently
C  nfs_no_post_open_success_guarantee  §14.2 (9865–9868)
   NFS client mounts: locally authorized `open()` may produce fd whose `read()` fails server-side
### Group 23: SD Synthesis and Persistence
P  persist_synthesized_true_writes_xattr  §14.2 (9817–9820)
   With `persist_synthesized = true`, synthesized SD is immediately written to `security.peios.sd`; subsequent accesses use persisted SD
P  persist_synthesized_false_caches_only  §14.2 (9822–9826)
   With `persist_synthesized = false`, synthesized SD is cached in inode blob only; never written to disk
P  persist_false_staleness_on_parent_change  §14.2 (9828–9831)
   With `persist_synthesized = false`, cached synthesized SDs are not recomputed when parent SD or mount template changes
P  hardlink_ambiguity_first_access_wins  §14.2 (9802–9812)
   File with multiple hard links under different parents: whichever path is accessed first determines the synthesized SD for all paths (per-inode cache)
### Group 24: Unix Socket SD Enforcement
P  unix_stream_connect_requires_write_data_on_socket  §14.3 (10599)
   `connect()` on Unix stream socket checks `FILE_WRITE_DATA` on the listening socket's SD
P  unix_dgram_send_requires_write_data_on_socket  §14.3 (10599)
   `sendto()` / `sendmsg()` on Unix dgram checks `FILE_WRITE_DATA` on the socket file's SD
P  abstract_socket_sd_set_at_bind_from_token  §14.3 (10605–10609)
   Abstract socket's SD is set at `bind()` time from the binding thread's effective token using default SD template
P  socketpair_no_sd_handle_possession  §14.3 (10610–10612)
   `socketpair()` creates sockets with no SD; security is by handle possession
### Group 25: Not-FACS-Managed Objects
P  pipe_not_facs_managed  §14.4 (10849)
   `pipe()` / `pipe2()` creates anonymous pipes; no FACS enforcement
P  eventfd_not_facs_managed  §14.4 (10850)
   `eventfd()` / `timerfd_create()` / `signalfd()` are anonymous fds; not FACS-managed
P  epoll_inotify_fanotify_not_facs_managed  §14.4 (10851)
   `epoll_create()` / `inotify_init()` / `fanotify_init()` are anonymous fds; not FACS-managed
P  socket_not_facs_managed_at_create  §14.4 (10852)
   `socket()` creates network sockets; not a filesystem object; Unix sockets gated at connect/send
P  memfd_create_not_facs_managed  §14.4 (10853)
   `memfd_create()` creates anonymous memory fd; not FACS-managed
### Group 26: Inode Cache Management
P  inode_getsecurity_returns_sd_from_cache_or_xattr  §14.3 (10590–10591)
   `security_inode_getsecurity` returns SD data from cache or xattr for kernel-internal reads
P  inode_free_security_rcu_frees_cached_sd  §14.3 (10593–10594)
   `inode_free_security_rcu` frees cached SD after RCU grace period
---

## Summary
**Total tests: 205**

- **Cargo tests (pure Rust logic, no kernel): 11** — tests 94, 166, 167, 173, 174, 175, 176, 177, 178, 179, 181, 189, 190
- **Provium tests (requires booted KACS kernel): 194** — all remaining tests

The Cargo tests cluster around SD parsing/validation (detecting corrupt SDs in pure data structures) and the granted-mask subset-check logic (pure bitwise operation). Nearly everything else requires a running KACS kernel because the behaviors are enforced by LSM hooks, kernel patches, and syscall-level interactions that cannot be tested outside the kernel.

---

# Section 15: Kernel Interface + Section 16: Derooting + Section 17: Audit Pipeline
## Test Corpus: KACS §15 Kernel Interface, §16 Derooting, §17 Audit Pipeline
---

### §15.1 Syscalls — Token Lifecycle
#### kacs_open_self_token
P  open_self_token_returns_fd  §15.1
   `kacs_open_self_token(0, TOKEN_QUERY)` returns a valid token fd
P  open_self_token_no_privilege_required  §15.1
   An unprivileged thread can open its own token; no privilege gate applies
P  open_self_token_effective_token_default  §15.1
   With `flags=0`, returns the impersonated token if the thread is impersonating, or the primary token otherwise
P  open_self_token_real_token_flag  §15.1
   With `KACS_REAL_TOKEN` flag, returns the primary token even when thread is impersonating
P  open_self_token_access_mask_gates_ioctls  §15.1
   The returned fd's access mask controls which ioctls succeed; requesting TOKEN_QUERY allows QUERY but not ADJUST_PRIVS
P  open_self_token_sd_access_check  §15.1
   The access mask is checked against the token's own SD (tokens are self-securing objects)
P  open_self_token_returns_neg_errno_on_failure  §15.1
   Returns `-errno` on failure (e.g., invalid access mask bits that fail the token's SD check)
#### kacs_open_process_token
P  open_process_token_returns_fd  §15.1
   `kacs_open_process_token(pidfd, TOKEN_QUERY)` returns a valid token fd for another process
P  open_process_token_process_gate  §15.1, §7.9
   AccessCheck for `PROCESS_QUERY_INFORMATION` runs against the target process's SD using the caller's effective token
P  open_process_token_token_gate  §15.1, §7.9
   AccessCheck for the requested access_mask runs against the token's own SD
P  open_process_token_denied_without_process_query  §15.1
   Fails with `-EACCES` if the caller cannot satisfy `PROCESS_QUERY_INFORMATION` on the target process SD
P  open_process_token_denied_without_token_access  §15.1
   Fails with `-EACCES` if the caller can reach the process but the token SD denies the requested access_mask
P  open_process_token_live_reference  §15.1
   The returned handle is a live reference (refcounted Arc); privilege adjustments via another handle are visible through this one
P  open_process_token_identity_immutable  §15.1
   User SID and groups queried through the returned handle are immutable and never change
P  open_process_token_pip_protection  §15.1
   PIP provides additional protection for high-trust processes; a low-trust caller cannot open a PIP-protected process's token
#### kacs_create_token
P  create_token_returns_fd  §15.1
   `kacs_create_token` with valid spec returns a token fd
P  create_token_requires_se_create_token_privilege  §15.1
   Fails with `-EPERM` if the caller's real (primary) token lacks `SeCreateTokenPrivilege`
P  create_token_checks_real_token  §15.1
   The privilege check is on the real (primary) token, not the impersonated token
C  create_token_wire_format_primary  §15.1
   A wire-format spec with `token_type=Primary` produces a Primary token
C  create_token_wire_format_impersonation  §15.1
   A wire-format spec with `token_type=Impersonation` and an impersonation level produces an Impersonation token
C  create_token_wire_format_all_fields  §15.1
   Wire format correctly encodes user SID, group SIDs with attributes, privilege bitmask, owner SID, primary group SID, default DACL, token source, logon session ID, elevation type, mandatory policy
C  create_token_wire_format_optional_fields  §15.1
   Wire format accepts optional fields: device groups, AppContainer SID, capabilities
P  create_token_rejects_malformed_spec  §15.1
   Returns `-EINVAL` for a malformed/truncated wire-format specification
#### kacs_open_peer_token
P  open_peer_token_returns_fd  §15.1
   `kacs_open_peer_token(sock_fd)` returns a valid token fd from a connected Unix socket
P  open_peer_token_snapshot_at_connect  §15.1
   The returned token is a snapshot of the peer's identity at `connect()` time; subsequent changes to the peer's token are not reflected
P  open_peer_token_no_privilege_required  §15.1
   No privilege required; any thread can call it on a connected socket it owns
P  open_peer_token_impersonation_level_from_socket  §15.1
   The impersonation level on the returned token matches the level stored on the socket (set by client via `kacs_set_impersonation_level`)
P  open_peer_token_identification_level_inspect_only  §15.1
   An Identification-level peer token can be inspected (QUERY) but not impersonated
P  open_peer_token_fails_not_connected  §15.1
   Returns `-errno` on an unconnected or non-Unix socket

### §15.1 Syscalls — Impersonation
#### kacs_impersonate_peer
P  impersonate_peer_success  §15.1
   `kacs_impersonate_peer(sock_fd)` returns 0 and the calling thread is now impersonating the peer
P  impersonate_peer_with_privilege  §15.1, §12.2
   If the caller has `SeImpersonatePrivilege`, impersonation proceeds at the level stored on the socket
P  impersonate_peer_same_user_fallback  §15.1, §12.2
   If the caller lacks `SeImpersonatePrivilege` but the peer token is the same user, impersonation proceeds
P  impersonate_peer_same_restriction_fallback  §15.1, §12.2
   If the caller lacks `SeImpersonatePrivilege` but the peer token is more restricted, impersonation proceeds
P  impersonate_peer_capped_to_identification  §15.1, §12.2
   If neither gate passes, the token is capped to Identification level (not rejected)
P  impersonate_peer_identification_denies_resource_access  §15.1, §12.2
   At Identification level, AccessCheck step 0 denies all resource access
P  impersonate_peer_all_four_levels_installable  §15.1
   All four impersonation levels (Anonymous, Identification, Impersonation, Delegation) are valid installable states
P  impersonate_peer_overwrites_existing  §15.1
   Calling `kacs_impersonate_peer` while already impersonating does an implicit revert-then-impersonate
P  impersonate_peer_combines_open_impersonate_close  §15.1
   Functionally equivalent to `kacs_open_peer_token` + `KACS_IOC_IMPERSONATE` + close in one syscall
#### kacs_revert
P  revert_success  §15.1
   `kacs_revert()` returns 0 and the thread returns to its primary token
P  revert_noop_when_not_impersonating  §15.1
   Returns 0 (success) when the thread is not impersonating (no-op)
P  revert_no_privilege_required  §15.1
   No privilege required; any thread can revert to its own primary token
#### kacs_set_impersonation_level
P  set_impersonation_level_success  §15.1
   `kacs_set_impersonation_level(sock_fd, IMPERSONATION)` returns 0 on an unconnected socket
P  set_impersonation_level_default_impersonation  §15.1
   Default level is IMPERSONATION (matching Windows) when not explicitly set
P  set_impersonation_level_anonymous  §15.1
   Level ANONYMOUS (0) is accepted and stored
P  set_impersonation_level_identification  §15.1
   Level IDENTIFICATION (1) is accepted and stored
P  set_impersonation_level_delegation  §15.1
   Level DELEGATION (3) is accepted and stored
P  set_impersonation_level_captured_at_connect  §15.1
   The level is captured into the connection at `connect()` time; changes after connect have no effect
P  set_impersonation_level_fails_after_connect  §15.1
   Returns `-errno` when called on an already-connected socket
P  set_impersonation_level_delegation_forwards_identity  §15.1
   Delegation level allows the server to forward the client's identity to other services (impersonated token stored in socket blob)
P  set_impersonation_level_invalid_value  §15.1
   Returns `-EINVAL` for values outside 0-3

### §15.1 Syscalls — Session Management
#### kacs_create_session
P  create_session_returns_id  §15.1
   `kacs_create_session` returns a session ID >= 0
P  create_session_requires_se_tcb_privilege  §15.1
   Fails with `-EPERM` if caller lacks `SeTcbPrivilege`
P  create_session_auto_logon_sid  §15.1
   The session receives an auto-generated logon SID `S-1-5-5-{high32}-{low32}`
P  create_session_logon_sid_injected_into_tokens  §15.1
   The logon SID is injected into the groups of any token associated with the session

### §15.1 Syscalls — File Operations
#### kacs_open
P  kacs_open_returns_fd  §15.1
   `kacs_open` with valid params returns a file fd
P  kacs_open_access_check_strict  §15.1
   Every bit in `desired_access` must be granted by the file's SD or the open fails
P  kacs_open_granted_mask_stamped_on_fd  §15.1
   The granted mask is stamped on the fd's LSM blob
P  kacs_open_fmode_read_mapping  §15.1
   `FILE_READ_DATA` maps to `FMODE_READ`
P  kacs_open_fmode_write_mapping  §15.1
   `FILE_WRITE_DATA` / `FILE_APPEND_DATA` maps to `FMODE_WRITE`
P  kacs_open_fmode_exec_mapping  §15.1
   `FILE_EXECUTE` (alone) maps to `FMODE_EXEC`
P  kacs_open_disposition_open  §15.1
   `FILE_OPEN` (1): opens existing file, fails if file doesn't exist
P  kacs_open_disposition_create  §15.1
   `FILE_CREATE` (2): creates new file, fails if file exists
P  kacs_open_disposition_open_if  §15.1
   `FILE_OPEN_IF` (3): opens existing file or creates new file
P  kacs_open_disposition_overwrite  §15.1
   `FILE_OVERWRITE` (4): truncates existing file to zero, fails if file doesn't exist; requires `FILE_WRITE_DATA`
P  kacs_open_disposition_overwrite_if  §15.1
   `FILE_OVERWRITE_IF` (5): truncates existing or creates new
P  kacs_open_disposition_supersede_new_inode  §15.1
   `FILE_SUPERSEDE` (0): deletes existing file and creates new one with new inode
P  kacs_open_supersede_requires_delete  §15.1
   Supersede requires `DELETE` on the existing file (or `FILE_DELETE_CHILD` on the parent) AND `FILE_ADD_FILE` on the parent
P  kacs_open_supersede_breaks_hardlinks  §15.1
   Supersede creates a new inode; old hardlinks to the old inode are broken
P  kacs_open_supersede_old_fds_see_old_inode  §15.1
   Already-open fds reference the old (now unlinked) inode with their old granted masks
P  kacs_open_supersede_atomic  §15.1
   Supersede holds parent directory inode_lock across unlink + create, making it atomic from userspace
P  kacs_open_supersede_failure_rollback  §15.1
   If any step fails after creation in supersede, the new inode is cleaned up and the old file is untouched
P  kacs_open_sd_from_caller  §15.1
   If `sd` is non-NULL, the provided SD is used (merged with inheritable ACEs from parent per §9.5)
P  kacs_open_sd_inherited_from_parent  §15.1
   If `sd` is NULL, the SD is inherited from the parent directory entirely
P  kacs_open_status_out_created  §15.1
   `status_out` reports `KACS_STATUS_CREATED` when a new file was created
P  kacs_open_status_out_opened  §15.1
   `status_out` reports `KACS_STATUS_OPENED` when an existing file was opened
P  kacs_open_status_out_overwritten  §15.1
   `status_out` reports `KACS_STATUS_OVERWRITTEN` when an existing file was truncated
P  kacs_open_status_out_superseded  §15.1
   `status_out` reports `KACS_STATUS_SUPERSEDED` when an existing file was superseded
P  kacs_open_status_out_null_ok  §15.1
   If `status_out` is NULL, no status is reported and no error occurs
P  kacs_open_overwrite_preserves_inode  §15.1
   `FILE_OVERWRITE` / `FILE_OVERWRITE_IF` preserves the same inode, same SD, and hardlinks
P  kacs_open_overwrite_visible_to_existing_fds  §15.1
   Already-open fds see the truncated file after overwrite
P  kacs_open_at_fdcwd  §15.1
   `dirfd=AT_FDCWD` resolves path relative to the current working directory
P  kacs_open_directory_file  §15.1
   `FILE_DIRECTORY_FILE` in create_options constrains the open to directories
P  kacs_open_delete_on_close  §15.1
   `FILE_DELETE_ON_CLOSE` causes the file to be deleted when the last handle closes
#### kacs_get_sd
P  get_sd_returns_self_relative  §15.1
   `kacs_get_sd` returns a self-relative SD in the output buffer
P  get_sd_owner_requires_read_control  §15.1
   `OWNER_SECURITY_INFORMATION` (0x01) requires `READ_CONTROL`
P  get_sd_group_requires_read_control  §15.1
   `GROUP_SECURITY_INFORMATION` (0x02) requires `READ_CONTROL`
P  get_sd_dacl_requires_read_control  §15.1
   `DACL_SECURITY_INFORMATION` (0x04) requires `READ_CONTROL`
P  get_sd_sacl_requires_access_system_security  §15.1
   `SACL_SECURITY_INFORMATION` (0x08) requires `ACCESS_SYSTEM_SECURITY` (which requires `SeSecurityPrivilege`)
P  get_sd_label_requires_read_control_only  §15.1
   `LABEL_SECURITY_INFORMATION` (0x10) requires only `READ_CONTROL`, not `ACCESS_SYSTEM_SECURITY`, despite labels being stored in the SACL
P  get_sd_two_call_pattern  §15.1
   First call with `buf_len=0` returns `-ERANGE` and populates `len_needed`; second call with sufficient buffer succeeds
P  get_sd_erange_on_small_buffer  §15.1
   Returns `-ERANGE` if buffer is too small, with `len_needed` set to the actual size
P  get_sd_at_empty_path_file_fd  §15.1
   With `AT_EMPTY_PATH` on a normal file fd, operates on the file's SD using the fd's granted mask
P  get_sd_at_empty_path_opath_fd  §15.1
   With `AT_EMPTY_PATH` on an `O_PATH` fd, operates on the file's SD via a live AccessCheck (not snapshot)
P  get_sd_at_empty_path_socket_fd  §15.1
   With `AT_EMPTY_PATH` on a socket fd, operates on the socket's SD
P  get_sd_at_empty_path_pidfd  §15.1
   With `AT_EMPTY_PATH` on a pidfd, operates on the process's SD (§8.4); authorized via `PROCESS_QUERY_INFORMATION`
P  get_sd_at_empty_path_token_fd  §15.1
   With `AT_EMPTY_PATH` on a token fd, operates on the token's SD; authorized via the token handle's access mask
P  get_sd_file_fd_uses_granted_mask  §15.1
   For normal file fd with `AT_EMPTY_PATH`, `READ_CONTROL` must be in the fd's granted mask
P  get_sd_opath_no_snapshot_authorization  §15.1
   O_PATH provides race-free object identity but live authorization (not snapshot)
#### kacs_set_sd
P  set_sd_owner_requires_write_owner  §15.1
   `OWNER_SECURITY_INFORMATION` requires `WRITE_OWNER`
P  set_sd_group_requires_write_owner  §15.1
   `GROUP_SECURITY_INFORMATION` requires `WRITE_OWNER`
P  set_sd_dacl_requires_write_dac  §15.1
   `DACL_SECURITY_INFORMATION` requires `WRITE_DAC`
P  set_sd_sacl_requires_access_system_security  §15.1
   `SACL_SECURITY_INFORMATION` requires `ACCESS_SYSTEM_SECURITY` (requires `SeSecurityPrivilege`)
P  set_sd_label_requires_write_owner_plus_integrity  §15.1
   `LABEL_SECURITY_INFORMATION` requires `WRITE_OWNER` plus integrity constraints (§10.3)
P  set_sd_owner_other_sid_requires_se_restore  §15.1
   Setting owner to a SID other than the caller's own SID or a group with `SE_GROUP_OWNER` requires `SeRestorePrivilege`
P  set_sd_missing_sd_repair  §15.1
   In deny mode, `kacs_set_sd` with `SeRestorePrivilege` bypasses the missing-SD hard-deny, allowing stamping an SD onto a file with none
P  set_sd_validates_format  §15.1
   Malformed SDs, invalid SID structures, or ACLs exceeding 64 KB are rejected with `-EINVAL`
C  set_sd_malformed_sid_rejected  §15.1
   An SD with a structurally invalid SID is rejected with `-EINVAL`
C  set_sd_acl_exceeding_64kb_rejected  §15.1
   An ACL exceeding 64 KB is rejected with `-EINVAL`
P  set_sd_at_empty_path_dispatch  §15.1
   With `AT_EMPTY_PATH`, the same object-type dispatch as `kacs_get_sd` applies: file fd, O_PATH fd, pidfd, token fd
