### §15.1 Syscalls — AccessCheck
#### kacs_access_check
P  access_check_returns_zero_on_grant  §15.1
   Returns 0 when all requested rights are granted
P  access_check_returns_eacces_on_deny  §15.1
   Returns `-EACCES` when any requested right is denied
P  access_check_granted_out_always_populated  §15.1
   `granted_out` is populated even on failure, showing which rights were granted
P  access_check_requires_token_query  §15.1
   The token fd must have `TOKEN_QUERY` access or the call fails
C  access_check_generic_mapping_required  §15.1
   GenericMapping must be provided; generic bits in ACEs are expanded using the mapping
C  access_check_generic_read_expansion  §15.1
   `GENERIC_READ` in an ACE is expanded to the `generic_read` mapping
C  access_check_generic_write_expansion  §15.1
   `GENERIC_WRITE` in an ACE is expanded to the `generic_write` mapping
C  access_check_generic_execute_expansion  §15.1
   `GENERIC_EXECUTE` in an ACE is expanded to the `generic_execute` mapping
C  access_check_generic_all_expansion  §15.1
   `GENERIC_ALL` in an ACE is expanded to the `generic_all` mapping
C  access_check_self_sid_substitution  §15.1
   When `self_sid_ptr` is non-null, `PRINCIPAL_SELF` in ACEs is substituted with the provided SID
C  access_check_privilege_intent_backup  §15.1
   `KACS_BACKUP_INTENT` in `privilege_intent` enables backup-privilege-granted access
C  access_check_privilege_intent_restore  §15.1
   `KACS_RESTORE_INTENT` in `privilege_intent` enables restore-privilege-granted access
C  access_check_no_privilege_intent_default  §15.1
   `privilege_intent=0` disables backup/restore privilege grants
C  access_check_optional_fields_zero  §15.1
   `self_sid_ptr=0`, `object_tree_ptr=0`, `local_claims_ptr=0` all work (optional fields)
P  access_check_extensibility_smaller_size  §15.1
   Older callers with smaller `size` field have missing trailing fields default to zero
P  access_check_extensibility_larger_size  §15.1
   The kernel accepts a struct with a `size` larger than it knows (future fields), ignoring unknown trailing fields
C  access_check_same_pipeline_as_facs  §15.1
   Uses the same DACL walk, privilege evaluation, and MIC check as FACS
C  access_check_object_tree_support  §15.1
   `object_tree_ptr` with a valid `OBJECT_TYPE_LIST` array enables per-property access decisions
C  access_check_local_claims_support  §15.1
   `local_claims_ptr` with claim attributes enables conditional ACE evaluation using `@Local.` references
---

### §15.2 Ioctls on Token Fds
#### Token Access Rights
C  token_query_right_value  §15.2
   `TOKEN_QUERY` has value 0x0008
C  token_adjust_privileges_right_value  §15.2
   `TOKEN_ADJUST_PRIVILEGES` has value 0x0020
C  token_adjust_groups_right_value  §15.2
   `TOKEN_ADJUST_GROUPS` has value 0x0040
C  token_duplicate_right_value  §15.2
   `TOKEN_DUPLICATE` has value 0x0002
C  token_impersonate_right_value  §15.2
   `TOKEN_IMPERSONATE` has value 0x0004
C  token_assign_primary_right_value  §15.2
   `TOKEN_ASSIGN_PRIMARY` has value 0x0001
C  token_query_source_folded_into_query  §15.2
   `TOKEN_QUERY_SOURCE` (0x0010) is reserved; TokenSource is queryable with `TOKEN_QUERY`; bit must not be reused
#### KACS_IOC_IMPERSONATE
P  ioc_impersonate_requires_token_impersonate  §15.2
   Requires `TOKEN_IMPERSONATE` on the handle; fails without it
P  ioc_impersonate_must_be_impersonation_token  §15.2
   The token must be an Impersonation token (any level)
P  ioc_impersonate_anonymous_level  §15.2
   Anonymous-level impersonation token can be installed
P  ioc_impersonate_delegation_level  §15.2
   Delegation-level impersonation token can be installed
P  ioc_impersonate_two_gate_model  §15.2, §12.2
   If caller lacks `SeImpersonatePrivilege` and same-user/same-restriction fallback does not apply, effective level is capped to Identification (not rejected)
P  ioc_impersonate_overwrites_existing  §15.2
   Overwrites any existing impersonation on the calling thread
#### KACS_IOC_INSTALL
P  ioc_install_requires_token_assign_primary  §15.2
   Requires `TOKEN_ASSIGN_PRIMARY` on the handle
P  ioc_install_requires_se_assign_primary_token  §15.2
   Requires `SeAssignPrimaryTokenPrivilege` on the caller's real token
P  ioc_install_must_be_primary_token  §15.2
   The token must be a Primary token
P  ioc_install_commits_creds  §15.2
   Commits the token as the calling process's primary token via `commit_creds()`
P  ioc_install_process_sd_regen_on_user_change  §15.2, §8.4
   When the new token's user SID differs from current, KACS auto-regenerates the process SD using the new token's identity
P  ioc_install_process_sd_template  §15.2
   The default template: new user SID gets `GENERIC_ALL`, Administrators and SYSTEM get `GENERIC_ALL`, Everyone gets `PROCESS_QUERY_LIMITED`
P  ioc_install_process_sd_same_user_no_regen  §15.2
   When new token's user SID is the same as current, the process SD is NOT regenerated
#### KACS_IOC_QUERY
P  ioc_query_requires_token_query  §15.2
   Requires `TOKEN_QUERY` on the handle
P  ioc_query_two_call_pattern  §15.2
   Call with `buf_len=0` gets needed size, second call with buffer gets data
P  ioc_query_token_user  §15.2
   `TokenUser` class returns the user SID
P  ioc_query_token_groups  §15.2
   `TokenGroups` class returns array of (SID, attributes) pairs
P  ioc_query_token_privileges  §15.2
   `TokenPrivileges` class returns privilege bitmask (present, enabled, default, used)
P  ioc_query_token_owner  §15.2
   `TokenOwner` class returns default owner SID for new objects
P  ioc_query_token_primary_group  §15.2
   `TokenPrimaryGroup` class returns default primary group SID
P  ioc_query_token_default_dacl  §15.2
   `TokenDefaultDacl` class returns default DACL for new objects
P  ioc_query_token_source  §15.2
   `TokenSource` class returns 8-byte name + 64-bit source ID (queryable with `TOKEN_QUERY`, not `TOKEN_QUERY_SOURCE`)
P  ioc_query_token_type  §15.2
   `TokenType` class returns Primary (1) or Impersonation (2)
P  ioc_query_token_impersonation_level  §15.2
   `TokenImpersonationLevel` class returns Anonymous/Identification/Impersonation/Delegation
P  ioc_query_token_statistics  §15.2
   `TokenStatistics` class returns token ID, logon session ID, modified ID, token type, expiration
P  ioc_query_token_restricted_sids  §15.2
   `TokenRestrictedSids` class returns restricting SID array
P  ioc_query_token_session_id  §15.2
   `TokenSessionId` class returns logon session ID
P  ioc_query_token_origin  §15.2
   `TokenOrigin` class returns originating logon session ID
P  ioc_query_token_elevation_type  §15.2
   `TokenElevationType` class returns Default (1) / Full (2) / Limited (3)
P  ioc_query_token_integrity_level  §15.2
   `TokenIntegrityLevel` class returns mandatory integrity SID
P  ioc_query_token_mandatory_policy  §15.2
   `TokenMandatoryPolicy` class returns `NO_WRITE_UP`, `NEW_PROCESS_MIN` flags
P  ioc_query_token_logon_type  §15.2
   `TokenLogonType` class returns Interactive/Service/Network/etc.
P  ioc_query_token_logon_sid  §15.2
   `TokenLogonSid` class returns the session's logon SID (`S-1-5-5-x-y`)
P  ioc_query_token_device_groups  §15.2
   `TokenDeviceGroups` class returns device group SIDs (for claims-based access)
#### KACS_IOC_DUPLICATE
P  ioc_duplicate_requires_token_duplicate  §15.2
   Requires `TOKEN_DUPLICATE` on the source handle
P  ioc_duplicate_deep_clone  §15.2
   Deep-clones the token into a new token fd
P  ioc_duplicate_target_type_primary  §15.2
   Can target Primary token type
P  ioc_duplicate_target_type_impersonation  §15.2
   Can target Impersonation token type with specified level
P  ioc_duplicate_target_access_mask  §15.2
   The new handle's access mask is set from the `desired_access` parameter
P  ioc_duplicate_impersonation_to_primary_requires_tcb  §15.2
   Converting Impersonation to Primary requires `SeTcbPrivilege`
P  ioc_duplicate_impersonation_to_primary_without_tcb_fails  §15.2
   Converting Impersonation to Primary without `SeTcbPrivilege` fails
#### KACS_IOC_ADJUST_PRIVS
P  ioc_adjust_privs_requires_token_adjust_privileges  §15.2
   Requires `TOKEN_ADJUST_PRIVILEGES` on the handle
P  ioc_adjust_privs_enable  §15.2
   Can enable a present-but-disabled privilege
P  ioc_adjust_privs_disable  §15.2
   Can disable an enabled privilege
P  ioc_adjust_privs_remove_irreversible  §15.2
   Removal is irreversible; a removed privilege cannot be re-enabled
P  ioc_adjust_privs_cannot_enable_removed  §15.2
   Cannot enable a privilege that has been removed
P  ioc_adjust_privs_bumps_modified_id  §15.2
   Bumps the token's `modified_id`
P  ioc_adjust_privs_atomic  §15.2
   Multiple (privilege_index, action) pairs are applied atomically
#### KACS_IOC_ADJUST_GROUPS
P  ioc_adjust_groups_requires_token_adjust_groups  §15.2
   Requires `TOKEN_ADJUST_GROUPS` on the handle
P  ioc_adjust_groups_enable  §15.2
   Can enable a disabled group
P  ioc_adjust_groups_disable  §15.2
   Can disable a non-mandatory group
P  ioc_adjust_groups_mandatory_cannot_disable  §15.2
   Mandatory groups (`SE_GROUP_MANDATORY`) cannot be disabled
P  ioc_adjust_groups_bumps_modified_id  §15.2
   Bumps `modified_id`
#### KACS_IOC_RESTRICT
P  ioc_restrict_requires_token_duplicate  §15.2
   Requires `TOKEN_DUPLICATE` on the handle
P  ioc_restrict_returns_new_fd  §15.2
   Returns a new token fd (not the same fd)
P  ioc_restrict_deep_clone  §15.2
   The restricted token is a deep clone with reduced authority
P  ioc_restrict_deny_only_sids  §15.2
   SIDs to mark deny-only are correctly applied
P  ioc_restrict_remove_privileges  §15.2
   Privileges to remove are removed from the restricted token
P  ioc_restrict_restricting_sids  §15.2
   Restricting SIDs are added, enabling the two-pass AccessCheck (§11)
C  ioc_restrict_two_pass_access_check  §15.2, §11
   A restricted token triggers the two-pass DACL walk: normal pass intersected with restricting-SID pass
#### KACS_IOC_LINK_TOKENS
P  ioc_link_tokens_requires_se_tcb_privilege  §15.2
   Requires `SeTcbPrivilege`
P  ioc_link_tokens_same_session  §15.2
   Both tokens must belong to the same logon session
P  ioc_link_tokens_different_session_fails  §15.2
   Fails if the two tokens belong to different logon sessions
P  ioc_link_tokens_stores_arc_clones  §15.2
   Stores Arc clones on the LogonSession object
#### KACS_IOC_GET_LINKED_TOKEN
P  ioc_get_linked_token_returns_deep_clone  §15.2
   Returns a deep clone of the partner token
P  ioc_get_linked_token_identification_level  §15.2
   The returned token is at Identification level
P  ioc_get_linked_token_query_access_only  §15.2
   The returned handle has `TOKEN_QUERY` access only
P  ioc_get_linked_token_no_impersonate  §15.2
   The caller can inspect the partner but not impersonate it (Identification level + TOKEN_QUERY only)
P  ioc_get_linked_token_requires_token_query  §15.2
   No privilege required beyond `TOKEN_QUERY` on the source handle
---

### §15.3 LSM Blob Layout
P  cred_blob_token_refcounted  §15.3
   The cred blob contains an Arc-managed token pointer; multiple creds can share the same token after fork()
P  cred_blob_prepare_copies_token  §15.3
   `security_prepare_creds` copies the token pointer and increments refcount
P  cred_blob_free_decrements_refcount  §15.3
   `security_cred_free` decrements the token's refcount
P  file_blob_granted_immutable  §15.3
   The file blob's `granted` field is set once at open time and never modified
P  file_blob_continuous_audit  §15.3
   The file blob's `continuous_audit` field holds alarm ACE bits including bit 25 (no-mmap)
P  inode_blob_sd_rcu_protected  §15.3
   The inode blob's parsed SD is RCU-protected; updates via `kacs_set_sd` use RCU replacement
P  inode_blob_sd_from_xattr  §15.3
   The parsed SD is populated on first access from `security.peios.sd` xattr
P  task_blob_proc_sd  §15.3
   The task blob contains a pointer to the process SD (§8.4)
P  socket_blob_peer_token_captured_at_connect  §15.3
   Socket blob's `peer_token` is captured in `security_unix_stream_connect` from the connecting thread's effective cred
P  socket_blob_default_impersonation_level  §15.3
   Socket blob's `max_impersonation_level` defaults to IMPERSONATION
P  socket_blob_socket_sd_at_bind  §15.3
   Socket blob's `socket_sd` is stamped at `bind()` time for abstract sockets (NULL for pathname/socketpair)
P  file_blob_continuous_audit_no_mmap  §15.3, §14
   Bit 25 in `continuous_audit` (from alarm ACE) causes mmap to be denied regardless of granted rights
---

### §15.4 Inspection Interfaces
#### procfs
P  procfs_pid_token_shows_primary  §15.4
   `/proc/<pid>/token` displays the primary token (user SID, groups, privileges, integrity level, token type, logon session ID)
P  procfs_tid_token_shows_effective  §15.4
   `/proc/<pid>/task/<tid>/token` displays the effective (impersonated) token if the thread is impersonating
P  procfs_token_access_gated  §15.4
   Access to `/proc/<pid>/token` is gated by AccessCheck for `PROCESS_QUERY_INFORMATION` against the target process SD, plus PIP trust level comparison
P  procfs_self_token_always_readable  §15.4
   `/proc/self/token` is always readable (own token)
P  procfs_token_not_weaker_than_syscall  §15.4
   procfs token inspection does not provide a weaker authorization path than the `kacs_open_process_token` syscall
#### securityfs
P  securityfs_self_readable  §15.4
   `/sys/kernel/security/kacs/self` shows the calling thread's effective token
P  securityfs_self_always_readable  §15.4
   Reading own token via securityfs is always allowed
P  securityfs_sessions_lists_sessions  §15.4
   `/sys/kernel/security/kacs/sessions` lists active logon sessions with session ID, user SID, logon type, logon time
P  securityfs_sessions_requires_admin_or_system  §15.4
   Reading sessions requires Administrators or SYSTEM
---

### §15.5 Build Configuration
P  config_kacs_enabled  §15.5
   `CONFIG_SECURITY_KACS=y` enables the KACS LSM
P  config_rust_required  §15.5
   `CONFIG_RUST=y` is required for the AccessCheck engine
P  config_no_selinux  §15.5
   `CONFIG_SECURITY_SELINUX=n` is required
P  config_no_apparmor  §15.5
   `CONFIG_SECURITY_APPARMOR=n` is required
P  config_no_bpf_lsm  §15.5
   `CONFIG_BPF_LSM=n` is required
P  config_lsm_stack  §15.5
   `CONFIG_LSM="commoncap,kacs"` is the exact LSM stack
P  config_rejects_unexpected_lsm  §15.5
   KACS verifies the LSM stack at initialization and refuses to activate if any unexpected LSM is present
---

### §15.6 Kernel Patches
P  patch12_do_dentry_open_desired_access  §15.6
   `do_dentry_open` accepts KACS `desired_access` and sets `f_mode` from granted mask instead of open flags
P  patch13_pidfd_getfd_mode  §15.6
   `pidfd_getfd()` uses `PTRACE_MODE_GETFD` flag to distinguish fd extraction from ptrace attach
P  patch14_current_fsuid_projected  §15.6, §16.2
   `current_fsuid()` returns projected UID from KACS token instead of `cred->fsuid`
P  patch15_execveat_file_execute  §15.6
   `execveat` / `do_open_execat` with `AT_EMPTY_PATH` checks `FILE_EXECUTE` on the original fd's granted mask
P  patch16_fchdir_file_traverse  §15.6
   `fchdir()` / `vfs_fchdir()` has a new `security_file_fchdir` hook that checks `FILE_TRAVERSE` in granted mask
---

### §15.7 Boot Sequence
P  boot_lsm_registration_second_after_commoncap  §15.7
   KACS registers as the second LSM after commoncap
P  boot_lsm_stack_verification  §15.7
   KACS verifies the LSM stack; if an unexpected LSM is present, KACS logs error and does not activate
P  boot_system_session_zero  §15.7
   Session 0 is created with `logon_type=SERVICE`, `user_sid=S-1-5-18`, `auth_package="Negotiate"`
P  boot_system_session_logon_sid  §15.7
   Session 0's logon SID is `S-1-5-5-0-0`
P  boot_system_token_user  §15.7
   The SYSTEM token has `user=S-1-5-18` (Local System)
P  boot_system_token_all_privileges  §15.7
   The SYSTEM token has all 35 privileges enabled
P  boot_system_token_integrity  §15.7
   The SYSTEM token has `integrity=S-1-16-16384` (System)
P  boot_system_token_primary  §15.7
   The SYSTEM token has `token_type=Primary`
P  boot_system_token_session_id  §15.7
   The SYSTEM token has `logon_session_id=0`
P  boot_system_token_groups  §15.7
   The SYSTEM token includes groups: `S-1-5-32-544` (Administrators), `S-1-1-0` (Everyone), `S-1-5-11` (Authenticated Users)
P  boot_init_attachment  §15.7
   The SYSTEM token is attached to the init process's cred via `commit_creds()`
P  boot_init_children_inherit  §15.7
   All processes forked from init inherit the SYSTEM token
P  boot_implementation_caps_asserted  §15.7
   Six implementation capabilities are asserted on the SYSTEM cred: `CAP_DAC_OVERRIDE`, `CAP_DAC_READ_SEARCH`, `CAP_FOWNER`, `CAP_CHOWN`, `CAP_SETUID`, `CAP_SETGID`
P  boot_everything_system_phase  §15.7
   Between init attachment and authd startup, all file access succeeds (SYSTEM has all rights)
---

### §16.1 The Projected UID
P  projected_uid_on_token  §16.1
   Every KACS token carries a projected UID derived from the token's user SID via authd's projection system
P  projected_uid_not_authorization  §16.1
   The projected UID is not an authorization primitive; KACS tokens are the sole authorization mechanism
P  projected_uid_stored_on_token_object  §16.1
   The projected UID is stored on the token object and available through the KACS credential blob
---

### §16.2 The current_fsuid() Patch
P  current_fsuid_returns_projected_uid  §16.2
   When KACS is active, `current_fsuid()` returns the projected UID from the KACS token, not `cred->fsuid`
P  current_fsuid_static_branch  §16.2
   The check uses `static_branch_unlikely` for near-zero-cost; when KACS is not configured, compiled out entirely
P  current_fsuid_inode_init_owner  §16.2
   Files created by a process are owned by the projected UID, not `cred->fsuid`
P  current_fsuid_disk_quotas  §16.2
   Disk quotas (ext4, XFS) track usage against the projected UID
P  current_fsuid_kernel_keyring  §16.2
   Per-user keyrings (`_uid.<uid>`) are keyed by the projected UID
P  current_fsuid_nfs_client  §16.2
   NFS RPC credentials use the projected UID, not UID 0
P  current_fsuid_capable_wrt_inode  §16.2
   `capable_wrt_inode_uidgid` ("Are you the owner?") matches against the projected UID
P  current_fsuid_uid0_interaction  §16.2
   After `uid0` sets `cred->fsuid` to 0, `current_fsuid()` still returns the projected UID; files are owned by the real user
P  current_fsuid_ignores_setfsuid  §16.2, §16.6
   `setfsuid()` changes `cred->fsuid` but `current_fsuid()` ignores it and returns the projected UID
---

### §16.3 The uid0 Utility
P  uid0_getuid_returns_zero  §16.3
   A program run under `uid0` sees `getuid() == 0`
P  uid0_token_unaffected  §16.3
   The KACS token is unaffected by `uid0`; the program runs with its real identity for access control
P  uid0_no_kacs_privilege_required  §16.3
   `uid0` requires no special KACS privilege because UIDs carry no authorization meaning
P  uid0_uses_cap_setuid  §16.3
   `uid0` uses `setuid(0)` under the hood, which requires `CAP_SETUID` (granted universally by KACS)
P  uid0_file_ownership_projected  §16.3
   Files created by a uid0 process are owned by the projected UID, not UID 0
---

### §16.4 Subsystem-by-Subsystem Analysis
#### Disk Quotas
P  quotas_track_projected_uid  §16.4
   ext4/XFS quotas track disk usage against the projected UID (via `inode->i_uid` set by the `current_fsuid()` patch)
P  quotas_no_subsystem_changes  §16.4
   No changes to the quota subsystem itself are needed
#### Kernel Keyring
P  keyring_per_user_projected_uid  §16.4
   Per-user keyrings (`@u`, `@us`) are keyed by the projected UID
P  keyring_session_process_unaffected  §16.4
   Session and process keyrings (`@s`, `@p`, `@t`) are not UID-based and are unaffected by derooting
#### File Ownership
P  file_ownership_ls_shows_projected_uid  §16.4
   `ls -l` shows the projected UID (resolved to username via `/etc/passwd` or NSS)
P  file_ownership_chown_via_write_owner  §16.4
   `chown` semantics are handled by FACS (`WRITE_OWNER` on the SD), not by UID comparison
#### SysV IPC
P  sysv_ipc_sd_at_creation  §16.4
   Each SysV IPC object receives a default SD at creation (creator full control, Administrators/SYSTEM full control)
P  sysv_ipc_access_check  §16.4
   Every SysV IPC operation is checked via AccessCheck against the object's SD (via `security_ipc_permission` LSM hook)
#### nftables UID Matching
P  nftables_uid_sees_cosmetic_uid  §16.4
   nftables `meta skuid` matches against `cred->uid` (cosmetic UID), not the projected UID
P  nftables_uid0_matches_zero  §16.4
   uid0 processes match as UID 0 in nftables UID matching
#### Programs Calling setuid()
P  setuid_cosmetic_only  §16.4
   A daemon calling `setuid(service_uid)` changes `cred->uid`/`cred->euid`/`cred->fsuid` but the KACS token is unchanged
P  setuid_getuid_returns_new_uid  §16.4
   After `setuid()`, `getuid()` returns the new UID; the program is satisfied
P  setuid_fsuid_returns_projected  §16.4
   After `setuid()`, `current_fsuid()` still returns the projected UID from the token (not affected by setuid)
P  setuid_files_owned_by_projected_uid  §16.4
   Files created after `setuid()` are owned by the projected UID, not the new UID
P  setuid_dac_bypass_irremovable  §16.4
   DAC bypass capabilities are irremovable even after `setuid()`
---

### §16.5 Kernel Patch Summary
P  patch14_ci_test  §16.5
   File created by a uid0 process is owned by the projected UID, not UID 0 (CI test assertion)
---

### §16.6 What Does Not Work
P  quota_split_on_token_change  §16.6
   If a process changes its KACS token via `KACS_IOC_INSTALL`, the projected UID changes; files before and after are owned by different UIDs
P  setfsuid_noop_for_filesystem  §16.6
   `setfsuid()` becomes a no-op for filesystem purposes; `current_fsuid()` returns the projected UID regardless
P  nftables_uid0_matches_zero_known_limitation  §16.6
   Legacy nftables UID rules match the cosmetic UID; uid0 processes match as UID 0 (known limitation)
---

### §17.1 Architecture
P  audit_three_layers  §17.1
   Audit pipeline has three layers: emitters, ring buffer, eventd
P  audit_ring_buffer_kernel_stamps_identity  §17.1
   The kernel stamps every event with trusted metadata (identity, timestamp, sequence)
P  audit_emitter_identity_unforgeable  §17.1
   The emitter's identity is unforgeable in the ring buffer
P  audit_timestamp_authoritative  §17.1
   The timestamp in the event header is authoritative (kernel-stamped)
P  audit_sequence_monotonic  §17.1
   The sequence number is monotonic
P  audit_event_subsystem_independent  §17.1
   The event infrastructure is a separate PKM subsystem, not part of KACS itself
---

### §17.2 Event Format
#### Kernel Header
P  event_header_sequence_monotonic_never_reused  §17.2
   `sequence` is monotonic and never reused; a gap indicates lost events
P  event_header_timestamp_clock_monotonic  §17.2
   `timestamp_ns` uses `CLOCK_MONOTONIC` nanoseconds
P  event_header_emitter_pid_kernel_verified  §17.2
   `emitter_pid` is kernel-verified from `current`
P  event_header_emitter_tid_kernel_verified  §17.2
   `emitter_tid` is kernel-verified from `current`
P  event_header_emitter_uid_projected  §17.2
   `emitter_uid` is the projected UID from the token (kernel-verified)
C  event_header_size_32_bytes  §17.2
   Header struct is 28 bytes padded to 32
C  event_header_source_kernel_or_userspace  §17.2
   `source` field is `PEIOS_EVENT_SOURCE_KERNEL` or `_USERSPACE`
P  event_header_forged_identity_impossible  §17.2
   A compromised service calling `event_emit` gets its real token identity stamped, not whatever identity it claims in the payload
#### Event Body
P  event_body_opaque_to_kernel  §17.2
   The kernel treats the body as opaque except for the event ID prefix check
P  event_body_event_id_prefix_check  §17.2
   The kernel reads the event ID from a fixed position at the start of the body (msgpack string, first element) to enforce reserved namespace restrictions
P  event_body_reserved_namespace_kacs  §17.2
   `kacs.*` event IDs are reserved for kernel-originated events
P  event_body_reserved_namespace_kernel  §17.2
   `kernel.*` event IDs are reserved for kernel-originated events
P  event_body_userspace_namespace  §17.2
   Userspace services use their own namespace (`authd.*`, `registryd.*`, `lpsd.*`, etc.)
C  event_body_msgpack_serialized  §17.2
   The body is serialized using msgpack
C  event_body_contains_event_id  §17.2
   The body contains an event ID string (e.g., `"kacs.access_check.denied"`)
C  event_body_contains_categories  §17.2
   The body contains an arbitrary list of category strings
C  event_body_contains_fields  §17.2
   The body contains arbitrary key-value pairs for event data
---

### §17.3 The event_emit Syscall
P  event_emit_returns_zero_on_success  §17.3
   `event_emit` returns 0 on success
P  event_emit_max_body_8kb  §17.3
   Returns `-EINVAL` if `body_len` exceeds 8 KB
P  event_emit_enospc_on_overflow  §17.3
   Returns `-ENOSPC` if ring buffer is full and overflow policy dropped the event
P  event_emit_eperm_reserved_namespace  §17.3
   Returns `-EPERM` if the event ID uses a reserved namespace (`kacs.*` or `kernel.*`) from userspace
P  event_emit_validates_body_len  §17.3
   Step 1: validates `body_len <= 8 KB`
P  event_emit_checks_namespace  §17.3
   Step 2: reads event ID prefix to check namespace reservation
P  event_emit_allocates_header_plus_body  §17.3
   Step 3: allocates `sizeof(header) + body_len` in the ring buffer
P  event_emit_stamps_header  §17.3
   Step 4: stamps header with sequence number, `ktime_get_ns()` timestamp, PID/TID, projected UID
P  event_emit_copies_body  §17.3
   Step 5: copies body via `copy_from_user()`
P  event_emit_advances_write_ptr  §17.3
   Step 6: advances the write pointer
P  event_emit_notifies_eventd  §17.3
   Step 7: notifies eventd via eventfd if blocked on poll
P  event_emit_kernel_internal_skips_namespace  §17.3
   Kernel-originated events via `peios_event_emit_kernel()` skip the syscall overhead and namespace check
P  event_emit_kernel_internal_same_buffer  §17.3
   Kernel internal events go to the same ring buffer with same header format
---

### §17.4 Ring Buffer Mechanism
#### Structure
P  ring_buffer_default_4mb  §17.4
   Default ring buffer size is 4 MB (configurable via boot parameter or securityfs)
P  ring_buffer_status_page_read_only  §17.4
   Status page (`write_ptr`, `overflow_count`, `buffer_size`) is mapped read-only for eventd
P  ring_buffer_consumer_page_read_write  §17.4
   Consumer page (`read_ptr`) is mapped read-write for eventd
P  ring_buffer_event_data_read_only  §17.4
   Event data region is mapped read-only for eventd
P  ring_buffer_separate_page_mappings  §17.4
   Status page and consumer page are separate mappings with different permissions
P  ring_buffer_read_ptr_only_forward  §17.4
   The kernel validates that `read_ptr` only moves forward and does not exceed `write_ptr`
P  ring_buffer_compromised_eventd_cannot_falsify_write_ptr  §17.4
   A compromised eventd can advance `read_ptr` (skip events) but cannot falsify `write_ptr`, `overflow_count`, or `buffer_size`
P  ring_buffer_atomic_pointers  §17.4
   Both pointers are atomic u64s; no locks needed for single-producer/single-consumer
P  ring_buffer_mapped_via_securityfs  §17.4
   The buffer is mapped into eventd via `/sys/kernel/security/peios/events`
#### Notification
P  ring_buffer_eventfd_notification  §17.4
   When the kernel writes an event, it increments an eventfd counter
P  ring_buffer_eventd_epoll  §17.4
   eventd blocks on `epoll_wait()` on the eventfd
P  ring_buffer_batch_wakeup  §17.4
   One wakeup per batch, not per event; eventd drains all available events from `read_ptr` to `write_ptr`
#### Overflow Policy — best_effort
P  overflow_best_effort_default  §17.4
   `best_effort` is the default overflow policy
P  overflow_best_effort_advances_read_ptr  §17.4
   When buffer is full, kernel advances `read_ptr` past oldest events to make room
P  overflow_best_effort_increments_count  §17.4
   `overflow_count` is incremented when events are discarded
P  overflow_best_effort_sequence_gap  §17.4
   eventd detects the gap via sequence numbers and logs a warning
P  overflow_best_effort_system_continues  §17.4
   The system continues operating after overflow in best_effort mode
#### Overflow Policy — audit_required
P  overflow_audit_required_uses_overflow_space  §17.4
   When buffer is full, kernel uses pre-allocated overflow space (default 512 KB)
P  overflow_audit_required_overflow_allocated_at_boot  §17.4
   The overflow region is allocated at boot alongside the main buffer
P  overflow_audit_required_no_remap  §17.4
   The overflow region is part of the original mmap'd allocation; eventd's mapping remains valid
P  overflow_audit_required_buffer_size_updated  §17.4
   The `buffer_size` field in the shared header is updated atomically to reflect expanded logical size
P  overflow_audit_required_policy_switches_to_best_effort  §17.4
   After using overflow space, the policy switches to `best_effort` for the remainder of the boot
P  overflow_audit_required_signals_peinit_shutdown  §17.4
   The kernel signals peinit to initiate a normal shutdown sequence
P  overflow_audit_required_shutdown_events_captured  §17.4
   Shutdown events are captured in the expanded buffer during peinit shutdown
P  overflow_audit_required_crash_file  §17.4
   After peinit completes shutdown, the kernel flushes ring buffer to `/var/log/peios/audit-crash` with a SYSTEM-only SD
P  overflow_audit_required_safe_mode_on_reboot  §17.4
   On next boot, peinit detects the `audit-crash` file and boots into safe mode (minimal services, admin-only access)
P  overflow_audit_required_crash_file_ingested  §17.4
   eventd ingests the crash file into its normal SQLite storage on the next boot
P  overflow_audit_required_crash_file_deleted_after_drain  §17.4
   Once the crash file is fully drained, peinit deletes it and transitions to normal mode
P  overflow_policy_configurable  §17.4
   Overflow policy is configurable via `/sys/kernel/security/peios/events/overflow_policy`
---

### §17.5 eventd Drain Contract
#### Liveness
P  eventd_heartbeat_interval  §17.5
   eventd writes a monotonic heartbeat timestamp at a fixed interval (default 1 second) regardless of whether events exist
P  eventd_peinit_monitors_heartbeat_and_backlog  §17.5
   peinit monitors both the heartbeat and the backlog (`write_ptr - read_ptr`)
P  eventd_restart_both_conditions  §17.5
   peinit kills and restarts eventd (SIGKILL) only if BOTH conditions are true: heartbeat stale (default 10s) AND unread events exist
P  eventd_long_fsync_no_restart  §17.5
   A long fsync or SQLite checkpoint does not trigger restart as long as heartbeat continues
P  eventd_idle_no_restart  §17.5
   On an idle system with no events, no liveness action is taken; a healthy idle eventd is not restarted
#### Crash Recovery
P  eventd_ring_buffer_survives_crash  §17.5
   The ring buffer is kernel memory; it survives eventd restarts
P  eventd_new_instance_continues_draining  §17.5
   A new eventd instance maps the same buffer and continues draining
#### Durability Protocol
P  eventd_read_ptr_after_commit  §17.5
   eventd advances `read_ptr` only AFTER the corresponding SQLite transaction has committed
P  eventd_durability_ordering  §17.5
   Ordering: read batch, INSERT into SQLite in transaction, COMMIT (fsync via WAL), then advance `read_ptr`
P  eventd_crash_recovery_dedup  §17.5
   If eventd crashes between commit and read_ptr advance, new eventd re-reads events; `INSERT OR IGNORE` on sequence number deduplicates
P  eventd_crash_recovery_last_committed_sequence  §17.5
   New eventd reads `last_committed_sequence` from SQLite and advances `read_ptr` to the event after that sequence
P  eventd_batching  §17.5
   eventd writes in batches (configurable, default 100-1000 events per transaction)
#### Storage
P  eventd_sqlite_path  §17.5
   Events stored in SQLite at `/var/log/peios/events.db`
P  eventd_header_fields_indexed  §17.5
   Kernel header fields (sequence, timestamp, emitter PID/TID/UID) are mapped to indexed columns
P  eventd_body_deserialized  §17.5
   Event body is deserialized from msgpack and stored as structured columns (event_id, categories, fields)
---

### §17.6 Kernel-Originated Events
#### KACS Events (kacs.*)
P  kacs_event_access_check_allowed  §17.6
   `kacs.access_check.allowed` emitted when SACL audit ACE matches and access is granted; contains object, desired, granted, token user
P  kacs_event_access_check_denied  §17.6
   `kacs.access_check.denied` emitted when access is denied; contains object, desired, token user, deny reason
P  kacs_event_privilege_used  §17.6
   `kacs.privilege.used` emitted when a privilege contributes to the access decision; contains privilege name, object, granted bits
P  kacs_event_privilege_adjusted  §17.6
   `kacs.privilege.adjusted` emitted when a privilege is enabled/disabled/removed; contains token, privilege, action
P  kacs_event_token_created  §17.6
   `kacs.token.created` emitted when a new token is minted; contains token ID, user SID, source
P  kacs_event_token_installed  §17.6
   `kacs.token.installed` emitted when a primary token is replaced; contains process, old token, new token
P  kacs_event_token_impersonated  §17.6
   `kacs.token.impersonated` emitted when a thread begins impersonation; contains thread, impersonated SID, level
P  kacs_event_token_reverted  §17.6
   `kacs.token.reverted` emitted when a thread ends impersonation; contains thread
P  kacs_event_session_created  §17.6
   `kacs.session.created` emitted when a new logon session is created; contains session ID, user SID, logon type
P  kacs_event_sd_modified  §17.6
   `kacs.sd.modified` emitted when an SD is changed; contains object, security_info, modifier SID
P  kacs_event_process_access  §17.6
   `kacs.process.access` emitted on a process SD access check; contains source PID, target PID, right, result
#### Kernel Events (kernel.*)
P  kernel_event_module_load  §17.6
   `kernel.module.load` emitted when a kernel module is loaded; contains module name, loader PID
P  kernel_event_audit_overflow  §17.6
   `kernel.audit.overflow` emitted on ring buffer overflow; contains events_dropped, policy
P  kernel_event_audit_shutdown  §17.6
   `kernel.audit.shutdown` emitted when audit_required shutdown is initiated; contains events_in_buffer
---

### §17.7 Userspace Event Emission
P  userspace_event_emit_via_syscall  §17.7
   Userspace services emit events via the `event_emit` syscall
P  userspace_event_kernel_stamps_not_in_body  §17.7
   Kernel-stamped fields (sequence, timestamp, emitter identity) are not included in the emitter's body; they are added by the kernel
P  userspace_event_cannot_override_stamps  §17.7
   An emitter cannot override or forge kernel-stamped fields
---

### §17.8 Tamper Resistance
P  tamper_emitter_identity_unforgeable  §17.8
   The kernel stamps every event with the calling thread's real token identity; a compromised service cannot claim to be different
P  tamper_event_data_immutable  §17.8
   Event data region and status page are mapped read-only from userspace
P  tamper_eventd_write_only_read_ptr  §17.8
   eventd has write access only to `read_ptr` on the consumer page; cannot modify events or kernel metadata
P  tamper_skipped_events_visible  §17.8
   Skipped events produce sequence number gaps visible in the database
P  tamper_sqlite_append_only  §17.8
   eventd inserts events but does not delete or modify them during normal operation
P  tamper_ring_buffer_survives_crash  §17.8
   Buffer is kernel memory; eventd crashing does not lose events
P  tamper_sequence_numbers_detect_gaps  §17.8
   If events are lost (overflow in best_effort mode), the gap is visible in sequence numbers; eventd logs a warning
P  tamper_audit_required_guarantees_completeness  §17.8
   In audit_required mode, the system shuts down rather than operate without audit; ring buffer is flushed to crash file before reboot
---

### §11.10 / §17 Cross-Reference — SACL Evaluation (Audit ACE Matching)
These tests cover the SACL evaluation rules referenced from §17 but specified in §11.10 and §9.3. Included here because the task explicitly asks for audit ACE matching, SACL evaluation rules, mandatory label ACEs, resource attribute ACEs, and alarm ACEs.

#### Access Auditing (SACL Audit ACEs)
C  sacl_audit_sid_matching_deny_polarity  §11.10
   Audit ACE SID is matched using deny polarity (broadest identity view: deny-only and disabled-but-deny-only groups are visible)
C  sacl_audit_mask_overlap_success  §11.10
   For success auditing: the audit ACE's mask overlaps with the granted bits (access result)
C  sacl_audit_mask_overlap_failure  §11.10
   For failure auditing: the audit ACE's mask overlaps with the denied bits
C  sacl_audit_success_flag  §11.10
   `SUCCESSFUL_ACCESS_ACE_FLAG` (0x40) audits granted access
C  sacl_audit_failure_flag  §11.10
   `FAILED_ACCESS_ACE_FLAG` (0x80) audits denied access
C  sacl_audit_both_flags  §11.10
   An ACE with both 0x40 and 0x80 audits every matching access attempt
C  sacl_audit_failure_only_detects_unauthorized  §11.10
   An ACE with only the failure flag audits denied attempts (unauthorized access detection)
C  sacl_audit_purely_observational  §11.10
   Auditing does not affect the access decision; audit ACEs do not grant or deny rights
C  sacl_audit_after_access_decision  §11.10
   Audit ACEs are evaluated after the access decision is final
C  sacl_audit_ace_basic_type  §11.10, §9.3
   SYSTEM_AUDIT (0x02) basic audit ACE is recognized
C  sacl_audit_ace_object_type  §11.10, §9.3
   SYSTEM_AUDIT_OBJECT (0x07) object-scoped audit ACE targets specific properties via GUIDs
C  sacl_audit_ace_conditional_type  §11.10, §9.3
   SYSTEM_AUDIT_CALLBACK (0x0D) conditional audit ACE carries an expression
C  sacl_audit_ace_conditional_object_type  §11.10, §9.3
   SYSTEM_AUDIT_CALLBACK_OBJECT (0x0F) conditional object-scoped audit ACE
C  sacl_conditional_audit_unknown_emits  §11.10, §11.12
   For conditional audit ACEs, expression evaluating to UNKNOWN results in the event being emitted (when in doubt, audit)
C  sacl_conditional_audit_false_skips  §11.10, §11.12
   For conditional audit ACEs, expression evaluating to FALSE skips the event
#### Continuous Auditing (Alarm ACEs)
P  alarm_ace_continuous_audit_mask  §11.10
   When an alarm ACE's SID matches the caller, the ACE's access mask is recorded as a continuous audit mask on the open handle
P  alarm_ace_per_operation_check  §11.10
   On each subsequent operation (read, write, execute), the enforcement point checks the handle's continuous audit mask
P  alarm_ace_emit_on_match  §11.10
   If the operation matches the continuous audit mask, an audit event is emitted
P  alarm_ace_no_mask_zero_cost  §11.10
   Objects without alarm ACEs have a zero continuous audit mask; no per-operation cost
C  alarm_ace_basic_type  §9.3
   SYSTEM_ALARM (0x03) basic continuous audit ACE
C  alarm_ace_object_type  §9.3
   SYSTEM_ALARM_OBJECT (0x08) object-scoped continuous audit ACE
C  alarm_ace_conditional_type  §9.3
   SYSTEM_ALARM_CALLBACK (0x0E) conditional continuous audit ACE
C  alarm_ace_conditional_object_type  §9.3
   SYSTEM_ALARM_CALLBACK_OBJECT (0x10) conditional continuous audit ACE, scoped to GUID
P  alarm_ace_bit25_no_mmap  §14, §15.3
   Bit 25 in alarm ACE mask (`MAXIMUM_ALLOWED` repurposed as no-mmap flag) causes mmap to be denied on matching handles
C  alarm_ace_intentional_divergence  §9.3
   Alarm ACEs are intentionally diverged from Windows (which reserves them); SDs from external sources will not contain them
#### Privilege-Use Auditing
P  privilege_use_audit_fires  §11.10
   When a privilege is exercised to grant access that the DACL would not have granted, a privilege-use audit event is emitted
P  privilege_use_audit_identifies_privilege  §11.10
   The audit records "access was granted because [specific privilege] was used"
C  privilege_use_audit_after_pipeline  §11.10
   Privilege-use auditing fires after the complete evaluation pipeline (integrity, confinement, CAP)
C  privilege_use_audit_only_when_necessary  §11.10
   Only fires when the privilege was actually necessary for the final result; if a later stage revoked privilege-granted bits, no audit
#### Mandatory Label ACEs in SACL
C  mandatory_label_ace_type  §9.3
   SYSTEM_MANDATORY_LABEL_ACE (0x11) sets the object's integrity level
C  mandatory_label_ace_at_most_one  §9.3
   At most one mandatory label ACE per SACL
C  mandatory_label_ace_sid_encodes_level  §9.3
   The SID encodes the integrity level (e.g., S-1-16-8192 = Medium, S-1-16-12288 = High)
C  mandatory_label_ace_mask_encodes_policy  §9.3
   The access mask encodes MIC policy: which operations are blocked when caller's integrity is below the object's
P  mandatory_label_readable_with_read_control  §15.1
   Labels readable via `LABEL_SECURITY_INFORMATION` with only `READ_CONTROL`, not `ACCESS_SYSTEM_SECURITY`
P  mandatory_label_write_requires_write_owner_plus_integrity  §15.1
   Writing labels via `kacs_set_sd` with `LABEL_SECURITY_INFORMATION` requires `WRITE_OWNER` plus integrity constraints
#### Resource Attribute ACEs in SACL
C  resource_attribute_ace_type  §9.3
   SYSTEM_RESOURCE_ATTRIBUTE_ACE (0x12) defines a resource attribute on the object
C  resource_attribute_ace_sid_everyone  §9.3
   The ACE's SID is always the well-known Everyone SID (S-1-1-0)
C  resource_attribute_ace_format  §9.3
   Attribute data follows the `CLAIM_SECURITY_ATTRIBUTE_RELATIVE_V1` format from MS-DTYP §2.4.10.1
C  resource_attribute_ace_name_value  §11.11
   Each resource attribute ACE encodes a single named, typed, multi-valued attribute
C  resource_attribute_ace_value_types  §11.11
   Values can be integers, strings, booleans, SIDs, or byte arrays
C  resource_attribute_ace_multiple  §11.11
   Multiple resource attribute ACEs can appear in the same SACL, each carrying a different attribute
C  resource_attribute_ace_first_wins  §11.11
   If two ACEs carry the same attribute name, the first one wins (duplicates silently ignored)
C  resource_attribute_extracted_before_dacl  §11.11
   Resource attributes are extracted from the SACL before the DACL walk begins
C  resource_attribute_available_in_conditional  §11.11
   Extracted attributes are available for conditional expression evaluation via `@Resource.` prefix
#### Audit Event Contents
C  audit_event_subject  §11.10
   Each audit event contains the calling token's identity (user SID, group SIDs, integrity level, PIP identity)
C  audit_event_object  §11.10
   Each audit event contains caller-provided context identifying the object
C  audit_event_access  §11.10
   Each audit event contains what was requested, what was granted, whether succeeded or failed
C  audit_event_trigger  §11.10
   Each audit event contains which audit ACE matched or which privilege was exercised
P  audit_event_process  §11.10
   Each audit event contains the calling process's PID, name, and executable path (from kernel task context)
---

## Summary
**Total tests extracted: 443**

The heavy Provium skew is expected: §15-17 are predominantly about kernel interfaces (syscalls, ioctls, procfs, boot, ring buffers) that cannot be tested without a running KACS kernel. The Cargo tests cluster around format parsing/validation, AccessCheck evaluation logic, ACE type recognition, and audit event structure -- pure data-structure and algorithm tests that the kacs-core crate can exercise in userspace.

---

#### Module: `test_dacl_walk`

?  dacl_walk_mask_accumulation  
   Multiple allow ACEs accumulate their masks via bitwise OR
?  dacl_walk_deny_clears_accumulated  
   A deny ACE removes bits from the remaining-desired set, preventing later allows from granting them
?  dacl_walk_empty_dacl  
   An empty DACL (present but no ACEs) denies all access
?  dacl_walk_null_dacl  
   A NULL DACL (not present) grants all access

# Appendix A: Audit-Finding Gap Tests
Tests proposed to cover the specific bugs found during the KACS implementation audit.
**None of the 24 P0-P2 audit findings had existing tests that would catch them.**

?  kernel_copy_matches_canonical_crate (Cargo/CI): Run a checksum or diff between pkm/crates/kacs-core/src/ and pkm/kacs/kacs_core/. Assert they are identical (or that a single-source mechanism exists). Type: CI build step, not a cargo test.  
   
?  inherit_ci_io_clears_io_on_child_container (Cargo): Parent ACE with CI\  OI\
   IO (no OI). Inherit to child container. Assert the child's inherited ACE does NOT have INHERIT_ONLY_ACE set. Also: `inherit_ci_oi_io_clears_io_on_child_container`: same for CI\
?  se_group_logon_id_value_is_0xC0000000 (Cargo): Assert SE_GROUP_LOGON_ID == 0xC000_0000. Also: se_group_integrity_value_is_0x20 and se_group_integrity_enabled_value_is_0x40 to assert the missing constants.  
   
?  se_relabel_privilege_bit_is_32 (Cargo): Assert the bit index for SeRelabelPrivilege equals 32 (LUID 33, index 32). se_undock_privilege_bit_is_25 (Cargo): Assert the bit index for SeUndockPrivilege equals 25. Also: privilege_bit_positions_match_windows_luids (Cargo): Exhaustive assertion of all 36 privilege bit assignments against MS-DTYP LUID values.  
   
?  restricted_pass_with_object_tree_evaluates_per_node (Cargo): Build an SD with object ACEs targeting specific GUIDs, create a restricted token, provide an object_tree. Assert restricted pass evaluates tree nodes with restricted SIDs (not None). confinement_pass_with_object_tree_evaluates_per_node (Cargo): Same pattern for confinement. Both must verify that individual tree nodes reflect the restricted/confinement SID evaluation, not just the scalar result.  
   
?  audit_ace_owner_rights_sid_fires (Cargo): SACL audit ACE targeting S-1-3-4, SD owner matches token user. Assert audit event is generated. audit_ace_principal_self_fires (Cargo): SACL audit ACE targeting S-1-5-10 with self_sid matching token. Assert audit event fires. Both require EnrichedToken in audit evaluation.  
   
?  token_user_sid_mutation_rejected (Cargo): Attempt to assign token.user_sid directly after creation. Assert this either doesn't compile (if fields are made private) or panics/errors at runtime. Same for integrity_level, token_type, impersonation_level. This is fundamentally a type-system enforcement, best done via private fields + getters rather than runtime tests.  
   
?  concurrent_token_adjust_privileges_no_ub (Provium): Two threads hold fds to the same token. Both call KACS_IOC_ADJUST_PRIVS concurrently in a tight loop. Assert no data corruption (modified_id is consistent, privilege state is valid). Run under Miri for UB detection in the Cargo version if possible.  
   
?  inode_init_security_concurrent_sd_replace (Provium): Thread A continuously replaces the parent directory's SD. Thread B continuously creates files in that directory. Run under KASAN. Assert no use-after-free. This is a kernel stress test, not a Cargo test.  
   
?  session_release_at_zero_refcount_does_not_underflow (Cargo): Create a session, drop all references, call release() again. Assert the refcount does not wrap to u32::MAX (either panics, errors, or is a no-op).  
   
?  concurrent_session_link_and_release_no_deadlock (Provium): Thread A calls kacs_session_link_tokens. Thread B concurrently releases a session. Run in a tight loop with timeout detection. Assert no deadlock within timeout. Also a code review item: document and enforce canonical lock order.  
   
?  inherit_dacl_protected_carried_to_output_sd (Cargo): Creator SD has SE_DACL_PROTECTED set. Create inherited SD. Assert the output SD's control word includes SE_DACL_PROTECTED.  
   
?  sd_parse_rejects_absolute_format (Cargo): Create an SD binary buffer with SE_SELF_RELATIVE clear in control word. Pass to SecurityDescriptor::from_bytes(). Assert parse error (not silent acceptance with garbage offsets).  
   
?  cap_unknown_policy_does_not_grant_arbitrary_access (Cargo): Scoped policy ACE with unknown SID. Non-admin, non-owner, non-SYSTEM token. Assert access is DENIED (recovery policy restricts to owner/admin/SYSTEM). The continue bug would grant access to this non-privileged token.  
   
?  object_tree_duplicate_guid_panics_or_errors (Cargo): Construct a tree with duplicate GUIDs. Pass to AccessCheck. Assert ERROR_INVALID_PARAMETER (not a panic). object_tree_level_gap_returns_error (Cargo): Construct tree with level 0 then level 2. Assert error. object_tree_root_not_level_zero_returns_error (Cargo): Root node at level 1. Assert error.  
   
?  ace_serialization_rejects_body_exceeding_u16 (Cargo): Construct an ACE with body > 65531 bytes. Assert serialization returns an error (not silently truncated). acl_serialization_rejects_size_exceeding_u16 (Cargo): Construct an ACL that would exceed u16::MAX total size. Assert error.  
   
?  resolve_claim_composite_elements_retain_correct_origin (Cargo): Create a @Device. claim with multiple values. Resolve it. Assert each element in the COMPOSITE Value has Origin::DeviceAttr (not Origin::UserAttr). Same for @Local. and @Resource. namespaces.  
   
?  audit_object_ace_0x07_not_silently_skipped (Cargo): SACL with SYSTEM_AUDIT_OBJECT_ACE (0x07) targeting a GUID. Matching tree node with access. Assert audit event is generated for that node. audit_callback_object_ace_0x0f_fires (Cargo): Same for type 0x0F with a conditional expression.  
   
?  se_group_integrity_value_is_0x20 (Cargo): Assert the constant exists and equals 0x20. se_group_integrity_enabled_value_is_0x40 (Cargo): Assert equals 0x40. integrity_sid_group_entry_has_integrity_flags (Cargo): Create a token with an integrity level SID in groups. Assert the group entry has SE_GROUP_INTEGRITY \  
   SE_GROUP_INTEGRITY_ENABLED set.
?  privilege_set_backup_starts_disabled (Cargo): Create a privilege set containing SeBackupPrivilege. Assert it is present but NOT enabled by default. privilege_set_restore_starts_disabled (Cargo): Same for SeRestorePrivilege. new_with_disabled constructor test: Create privilege set via a constructor that takes (present, enabled) separately. Assert present contains backup/restore, enabled does not.  
   
?  session_table_lock_does_not_schedule_while_atomic (Provium): Enable CONFIG_DEBUG_ATOMIC_SLEEP. Perform session operations that trigger token drop under lock. Assert no "BUG: scheduling while atomic" in dmesg.  
   
?  session_remove_under_oom_does_not_corrupt_sids (Cargo): Create a session with multiple user SIDs. Simulate allocation failure during remove(). Assert no SID is replaced with a null-authority SID (S-0-0). If fallible allocation is used, assert the error is propagated rather than silently corrupting.  
   
---

**Summary of coverage:**

- **0 of 24 findings** have existing tests that would definitively catch the specific bug.
- **2 findings** (P2-3 CAP recovery, P2-4 object type validation) have partial coverage -- the test corpus specifies the correct behavior, but either the tests are not yet in the running suite or test the behavior at a level that might not catch the specific implementation shortcut.
- **22 findings** have clear test gaps. No existing test would catch the bug.
- The most impactful missing test categories: inheritance flag combination tests (would have prevented P0-2), constant value assertion tests (would have prevented P0-3 and P0-4), code tree sync checks (would have prevented P0-1 and P0-6), and concurrent access/stress tests (would have caught P1-3 through P1-6).

Key files referenced:
- `/home/jack/projects/peios/kacs-audit-report.md` (audit findings)
- `/home/jack/projects/peios/kacs-test-corpus.md` (test corpus, ~3,127 specified tests)

---

# Appendix B: Compound Interaction Tests
Cross-subsystem tests that exercise multiple KACS features simultaneously.
These scenarios test the composition of MIC, PIP, restricted tokens, confinement,
CAP, privileges, impersonation, and inheritance in adversarial combinations.

### Category 1: MIC + PIP Combined
**Test 1**
- **Name:** `mic_and_pip_both_present_dominant_on_both`
- **Assertion:** When the caller dominates both the MIC label and the PIP trust label, neither mechanism restricts access; the DACL alone determines the result.
- **Subsystems:** MIC (11.13), PIP (11.15), DACL walk (11.3)
- **Target:** Cargo
- **Spec refs:** 11.13 (dominant callers bypass MIC), 11.15 (dominant callers bypass PIP), 11.17 steps 4-5

**Test 2**
- **Name:** `mic_blocks_write_pip_allows_all_nondominated`
- **Assertion:** Object has Medium MIC label (NO_WRITE_UP) and a PIP trust label with mask allowing all rights. A Low-integrity caller who dominates PIP but not MIC is blocked from GENERIC_WRITE by MIC, even though PIP imposes no restriction.
- **Subsystems:** MIC (11.13), PIP (11.15)
- **Target:** Cargo
- **Spec refs:** 11.13 (no-write-up), 11.15 (allowed mask), 11.17 PreSACLWalk ordering

**Test 3**
- **Name:** `pip_revokes_bits_mic_would_allow`
- **Assertion:** Object has Low MIC label and a PIP trust label with mask 0 (total lockout). A Medium-integrity caller dominates MIC (no restriction) but does not dominate PIP. PIP denies everything. Result: zero granted.
- **Subsystems:** MIC (11.13), PIP (11.15)
- **Target:** Cargo
- **Spec refs:** 11.15 (mask of 0 = total lockout), 11.17 EnforcePIP

**Test 4**
- **Name:** `mic_and_pip_both_restrict_intersection`
- **Assertion:** Object has High MIC label (NO_WRITE_UP + NO_READ_UP) and a PIP trust label with mask allowing only READ_CONTROL. A Medium-integrity None-type caller gets nothing: MIC blocks read and write, PIP allows only READ_CONTROL but MIC already decided those bits as denied.
- **Subsystems:** MIC (11.13), PIP (11.15)
- **Target:** Cargo
- **Spec refs:** 11.13 (NO_READ_UP), 11.15 (PIP allowed set), 11.17 mandatory_decided

**Test 5**
- **Name:** `pip_trust_label_ordering_before_mic_label_in_sacl`
- **Assertion:** When the SACL has the PIP trust label ACE listed before the MIC mandatory label ACE, both are still correctly extracted and enforced. PreSACLWalk scans the entire SACL.
- **Subsystems:** MIC (11.13), PIP (11.15), SACL parsing
- **Target:** Cargo
- **Spec refs:** 11.17 PreSACLWalk (scan all ACEs)

**Test 6**
- **Name:** `mic_default_medium_plus_explicit_pip_label`
- **Assertion:** Object has no MIC label ACE (defaults to Medium/NO_WRITE_UP) but has an explicit PIP trust label. A Low-integrity caller who dominates PIP is still blocked by the default MIC label.
- **Subsystems:** MIC (11.13), PIP (11.15)
- **Target:** Cargo
- **Spec refs:** 11.13 (default label), 11.15 (no default)

### Category 2: Restricted Token + Confinement Combined
**Test 7**
- **Name:** `restricted_and_confined_both_intersect`
- **Assertion:** A token that is both restricted (restricting SIDs) and confined (confinement_sid). The DACL grants READ+WRITE to the user SID, READ to a restricting SID, and READ to the confinement SID. Result: READ only (three-way intersection: normal=READ+WRITE, restricted=READ, confinement=READ).
- **Subsystems:** Restricted tokens (11.7), Confinement (11.14)
- **Target:** Cargo
- **Spec refs:** 11.17 steps 8, 8a

**Test 8**
- **Name:** `restricted_pass_grants_write_confinement_blocks_it`
- **Assertion:** Restricted pass grants WRITE (restricting SID matches allow ACE). But confinement SID has no matching ACE for WRITE. Final result: WRITE is denied by confinement intersection.
- **Subsystems:** Restricted tokens (11.7), Confinement (11.14)
- **Target:** Cargo
- **Spec refs:** 11.14 (absolute intersection), 11.17 step 8a

**Test 9**
- **Name:** `privilege_orback_after_restricted_then_stripped_by_confinement`
- **Assertion:** Token has SeBackupPrivilege, restricting SIDs, and confinement. After restricted intersection, privilege-granted bits are OR'd back (step 8). But confinement in step 8a strips them again -- privileges do NOT bypass confinement.
- **Subsystems:** Restricted tokens (11.7), Confinement (11.14), Privileges (11.6)
- **Target:** Cargo
- **Spec refs:** 11.7 (privileges bypass restricted), 11.14 (no privilege bypass), 11.17 step 8 vs 8a ordering

**Test 10**
- **Name:** `write_restricted_plus_confinement_write_bits`
- **Assertion:** Write-restricted token with confinement. Normal pass grants READ+WRITE. Restricted intersection applies only to write bits. Confinement applies to ALL bits. Confinement that grants only READ strips WRITE regardless of write-restricted semantics.
- **Subsystems:** Restricted tokens (11.7 write-restricted), Confinement (11.14)
- **Target:** Cargo
- **Spec refs:** 11.7 (write-restricted definition), 11.14, 11.17

**Test 11**
- **Name:** `restricted_and_confined_null_dacl`
- **Assertion:** Object has NULL DACL. Normal pass grants all. Restricted pass on NULL DACL also grants all (NULL DACL grants to any SID matcher). Confinement pass on NULL DACL also grants all. Final: all granted.
- **Subsystems:** Restricted tokens (11.7), Confinement (11.14), NULL DACL (11.3)
- **Target:** Cargo
- **Spec refs:** 11.3 (NULL DACL), 11.14 (NULL DACL grants access to confined)

**Test 12**
- **Name:** `restricted_and_confined_empty_dacl`
- **Assertion:** Object has empty DACL (present, zero ACEs). Owner implicit rights in normal pass (if owner matches). Restricted pass: owner implicit rights evaluated if owner in restricting SIDs. Confinement: skip_owner_implicit=true, so no implicit rights. Result: confinement blocks owner implicit.
- **Subsystems:** Restricted tokens (11.7), Confinement (11.14), Owner implicit (11.4)
- **Target:** Cargo
- **Spec refs:** 11.4, 11.14 (owner implicit skipped), 11.17 EvaluateDACL skip_owner_implicit

### Category 3: Restricted + MIC + Privilege
**Test 13**
- **Name:** `backup_privilege_survives_mic_and_restricted_intersection`
- **Assertion:** Token has SeBackupPrivilege (with BACKUP_INTENT) and restricting SIDs. Object has Medium MIC label. Caller is Medium integrity, so MIC does not restrict. Backup grants all read bits. After restricted intersection, backup bits are OR'd back. Result: read access granted.

**Test 14**
- **Name:** `backup_privilege_blocked_by_high_integrity_mic`

MIC blocks WRITE bits but not read bits. Backup privilege grants read bits before MIC runs. MIC only decides undecided bits. Backup read bits survive MIC.
- **Subsystems:** Privileges (11.6), MIC (11.13), Restricted tokens (11.7)
- **Target:** Cargo
- **Spec refs:** 11.13 ("MIC does not constrain privileges"), 11.17 step order (privileges at step 3, MIC at step 4)

**Test 15**
- **Name:** `restricted_token_with_backup_privilege_and_mic_write_up`
- **Assertion:** Low-integrity token with SeBackupPrivilege and restricting SIDs. Object is Medium integrity with NO_WRITE_UP. Backup grants read bits (step 3). MIC blocks write bits (step 4). Restricted intersection happens (step 8), but privilege bits are OR'd back. Write bits remain blocked by MIC. Final: read granted via privilege, write denied by MIC.
- **Subsystems:** Privileges (11.6), MIC (11.13), Restricted tokens (11.7)
- **Target:** Cargo
- **Spec refs:** 11.6, 11.7, 11.13, 11.17

**Test 16**
- **Name:** `take_ownership_privilege_blocked_by_mic_mandatory_decided`

- **Target:** Cargo

**Test 17**
- **Name:** `relabel_privilege_punches_through_mic_for_write_owner`

**Test 28**

**Test 29**

Restricted pass: GroupA must be in restricting SIDs for the SID match. If not, the deny does not fire in the restricted pass -- but the normal pass already denied it.

**Test 30**

- **Target:** Cargo

**Test 49**

### Category 14: Fork + Impersonation + Exec

- **Subsystems:** Exec (7.4), Impersonation (12)
- **Target:** Provium
- **Spec refs:** 7.4 ("impersonation is reverted before the new program runs")

**Test 58**
- **Name:** `fork_then_exec_token_survives_both`
- **Assertion:** Parent has primary token T. Fork: child gets deep copy of T. Child execs: token survives (no setuid, no NEW_PROCESS_MIN trigger). Token after exec is equivalent to T.
- **Subsystems:** Fork (7.4), Exec (7.4)
- **Target:** Provium
- **Spec refs:** 7.4 ("primary token survives execve unchanged")

**Test 59**
- **Name:** `fork_impersonating_exec_service_binary_primary_survives`
- **Assertion:** peinit-like flow: parent impersonating, forks, installs service token on child, child execs. At each stage: (1) after fork: child has parent's primary token, no impersonation; (2) after token install: child has service token; (3) after exec: service token survives.
- **Subsystems:** Fork (7.4), Exec (7.4), Impersonation (12), Token install
- **Target:** Provium
- **Spec refs:** 7.4, 12, 7.5 (SeAssignPrimaryTokenPrivilege)

### Additional Adversarial Compound Tests
**Test 60**
- **Name:** `all_layers_active_simultaneously`
- **Assertion:** Token is confined + restricted + has SeBackupPrivilege + Low integrity. Object has High MIC label (NO_WRITE_UP + NO_READ_UP) + PIP trust label + DACL + CAP scoped policy. Verify each layer's contribution is correct and the final result is the composition of all constraints.
- **Subsystems:** All
- **Target:** Cargo
- **Spec refs:** 11.17 (full pipeline)

**Test 61**
- **Name:** `confinement_blocks_access_system_security_via_privilege`
- **Assertion:** Confined token with SeSecurityPrivilege. ACCESS_SYSTEM_SECURITY is granted by privilege (step 3). Confinement (step 8a) intersects -- ACCESS_SYSTEM_SECURITY is not in any confinement ACE. Result: ACCESS_SYSTEM_SECURITY denied.
- **Subsystems:** Confinement (11.14), Privileges (11.6)
- **Target:** Cargo
- **Spec refs:** 11.14 ("SACL access is unreachable")

**Test 62**
- **Name:** `confinement_blocks_take_ownership_privilege`
- **Assertion:** Confined token with SeTakeOwnershipPrivilege. Step 7a grants WRITE_OWNER. Step 8a confinement strips it (no confinement ACE for WRITE_OWNER).
- **Subsystems:** Confinement (11.14), Privileges (11.6)
- **Target:** Cargo
- **Spec refs:** 11.14 ("Privileges do not bypass confinement")

**Test 63**
- **Name:** `restricted_owner_implicit_rights_owner_not_in_restricting_sids`
- **Assertion:** Token is owner of object. Restricted token where owner SID is NOT in restricting SIDs. Normal pass: owner gets READ_CONTROL + WRITE_DAC. Restricted pass: owner implicit not triggered (SidInRestrictingSids fails). Intersection: READ_CONTROL + WRITE_DAC removed. BUT: privilege OR-back does not help (these are not privilege-granted).
- **Subsystems:** Restricted tokens (11.7), Owner implicit (11.4)
- **Target:** Cargo
- **Spec refs:** 11.7 ("Owner implicit rights in the restricted pass"), 11.17

**Test 64**
- **Name:** `restricted_owner_implicit_rights_owner_in_restricting_sids`
- **Assertion:** Token is owner. Owner SID IS in restricting SIDs. Both normal and restricted passes grant owner implicit. Intersection preserves READ_CONTROL + WRITE_DAC.
- **Subsystems:** Restricted tokens (11.7), Owner implicit (11.4)
- **Target:** Cargo
- **Spec refs:** 11.7, 11.17

**Test 65**
- **Name:** `owner_rights_ace_suppresses_in_both_normal_and_restricted_passes`
- **Assertion:** DACL has OWNER RIGHTS ACE. Normal pass: owner implicit suppressed. Restricted pass: also evaluates owner implicit independently. If OWNER RIGHTS is present, implicit suppressed in both passes.
- **Subsystems:** Restricted tokens (11.7), Owner implicit (11.4), OWNER RIGHTS

- **Spec refs:** 11.4, 11.7, 11.17

**Test 66**
- **Name:** `virtual_group_owner_rights_in_restricted_pass`
- **Assertion:** Owner SID is in restricting SIDs. The restricted pass builds restricted_sids with SID_OWNER_RIGHTS injected. ACEs targeting S-1-3-4 can match in the restricted pass SID matcher.
- **Subsystems:** Restricted tokens (11.7), OWNER RIGHTS, Virtual groups
- **Target:** Cargo

**Test 67**
- **Name:** `principal_self_in_restricted_pass`

**Test 68**

- **Assertion:** Confined token, self_sid matches user's SID (not a confinement SID). Confinement pass: PRINCIPAL_SELF is NOT injected (self_sid not in confinement_sids). ACEs targeting S-1-5-10 do not match in confinement pass.

**Test 69**
- **Name:** `confinement_conditional_sees_real_groups`
- **Assertion:** Conditional ACE targeting confinement SID with condition `Member_of({GroupA})`. GroupA is in the token's real groups. Confinement pass: SID match succeeds (confinement SID in confinement_sids). Condition evaluates against full token -- sees GroupA. ACE fires.

**Test 70**

**Test 71**
- **Name:** `cap_no_backup_intent_inside_rule_evaluation`

**Test 72**
- **Name:** `cap_security_privilege_survives_intersection`

**Test 73**
- **Name:** `cap_error_preserves_privilege_granted_only`

**Test 74**
- **Name:** `mic_plus_restricted_plus_confinement_plus_cap_all_narrow`

**Test 80**

**Test 81**

**Test 82**
- **Name:** `conditional_ace_resource_attribute_plus_cap_applies_to`

CAP rule has applies_to: `@Resource.department == "finance"`. Both evaluate the same resource attribute independently. The DACL conditional grants access. The CAP applies_to triggers the rule. The CAP rule's DACL further restricts.

**Test 83**

Restricted SIDs have ACE for READ_CONTROL + DELETE. Confinement SID has ACE for READ_CONTROL only. Final: READ_CONTROL (the tightest constraint wins at each bit).

**Test 96**

**Test 97**
- **Name:** `claim_deny_only_flag_plus_conditional_allow_ace`

Condition: absent >= 3 is UNKNOWN. Allow ACE skipped. Combined with the same condition on a deny ACE: deny-only claim is visible, condition evaluates to TRUE, deny fires.

**Test 98**
- **Name:** `confinement_plus_restricted_plus_cap_triple_intersection_with_privileges`
- **Assertion:** Token is confined + restricted + has SeSecurityPrivilege. CAP rule active. Privilege grants ACCESS_SYSTEM_SECURITY in normal eval and in CAP rule eval. Restricted OR-back restores it. But confinement strips it (runs after restricted). CAP rule's confinement pass also strips it. Final: ACCESS_SYSTEM_SECURITY denied.

**Test 99**
- **Name:** `enriched_token_virtual_groups_visible_in_cap_applies_to`
- **Assertion:** CAP rule's applies_to condition uses `Member_of({S-1-3-4})`. Caller is the owner. EnrichToken injects S-1-3-4 before CAP evaluation. applies_to evaluates against enriched_token. Condition TRUE. Rule applies.

**Test 100**
- **Name:** `mandatory_policy_no_write_up_cleared_skips_mic`
- **Assertion:** Token has mandatory_policy without TOKEN_MANDATORY_POLICY_NO_WRITE_UP (cleared at creation by authd). MIC is effectively disabled for this token. Combined with PIP: PIP still enforces independently (PIP does not check mandatory_policy). A Low-integrity token with MIC disabled can write to High-integrity objects, but PIP can still block it.
- **Subsystems:** MIC (11.13), PIP (11.15), Token policy
- **Target:** Cargo
- **Spec refs:** 11.13 (token mandatory policy flag), 11.17 EnforceMIC (early return)

---

## Summary
100 compound interaction tests generated across 14 categories:

All tests target Cargo (the `no_std` evaluation core) except for lifecycle/process tests (fork/exec/impersonation state transitions) which require Provium for kernel integration testing. Some tests (marked both) should have Cargo unit tests for the AccessCheck logic and Provium integration tests for the kernel-level enforcement.
